Claim of Assumption Drops Hadd in Shubha Hukmiyya
Expands the principle of shubha hukmiyya with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a claim of assumption (gunnan) drops hadd in cases of shubha hukmiyya.

Core Idea
A claim of assumption suffices to avert the hadd penalty, even without actual doubt.

The hadd penalties are severe, and the Shari'ah commands their avoidance in cases of doubt. The Hanafi school extends this to accept a mere claim of assumption (gunnan) by the accused, even if the act was objectively haram. This lesson examines the examples given in the text and the reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching principle
Recognize that the passage builds on the known rule: doubt drops hadd. The text distinguishes two types of doubt: actual (shubha fi'liyya) and legal (shubha hukmiyya).
2
Distinguish shubha fi'liyya and shubha hukmiyya
Shubha fi'liyya is objective doubt about the occurrence of the act; shubha hukmiyya is doubt about its legal permissibility due to some semblance of lawfulness. The passage focuses on shubha hukmiyya.
3
List the examples of shubha hukmiyya
Work through each example: intercourse with a mukatib's slave-girl, with a slave-girl bought for trade, with war booty before distribution, with a purchased slave-girl before purification, with an apostate wife, and with in-laws under mistaken permission. In each, the act is haram but a potential justification exists.
4
Understand the role of gunnan (assumption)
The text states that in all these cases, if the person claims he had an assumption that the act was halal, the claim is accepted and hadd is dropped, even if he actually had no such assumption. This is a unique Hanafi leniency.
5
Examine the evidentiary rule
The passage concludes with a procedural point: if witnesses testify that the accused confessed to having no assumption, their testimony is rejected. The claim of gunnan takes precedence to avoid hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جیسا کہ اسی کتاب میں پہلے معلوم ہو چکا ہے کہ شبہ سے حد ساقط ہو جاتی ہے خواہ وہ بد فعلی ہو یا حکمی ہو۔ شبہ حکمی میں سے یہ بھی ہے کہ مکاتب کی باندی سے کسی نے ولی کی یا اپنے غلام کو تجارت کی اجازت دی اور اس نے تجارت کی غرض سے کوئی باندی خریدی۔ اور اس باندی سے اس کے مولی نے وطی کرلی حالانکہ اس غلام پر لوگوں کا اتنا قرض ہو گیا ہو جو اس کے پاس کے مال اور خود اس کی جان کی مجموعی قیمت سے بھی زیادہ ہے۔ یا مال غنیمت کی تقسیم سے پہلے ہی اس میں سے کسی باندی سے ولی کر لی خواہ وہ غنیمت دار الاسلام میں لا کر محفوظ کرنے کے پہلے ہو یا بعد میں ۔ یا خریدی ہوئی باندی کا حیض سے پاک ہونے سے پہلے ہی اس سے وطی کر لی۔ یا اپنی ایسی بیوی سے وطی کی ہو جو مرتد ہو جانے کی وجہ سے اس پر حرام ہو چکی ہو۔ یا اپنے شوہر کے بالغ لڑکے کو اس نے خود پر قدرت دیدی یا شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کی ماں (ساس)۔ سے یا پہلے شوہر - کی بیٹی ( سوتیلی بیٹی سے جماع کر لیا تو ان تمام صورتوں میں اگر چہ ولی حرام ہوگی پھر بھی شہ فعلی میں حلال ہونے کا گمان کافی ہے اور گمان کا اگر دعوی کر لیا تو اس کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا اگر چہ اسے گمان نہ ہوا ہو ۔ اب اگر ایک شخص نے گمان کا دعوی کیا اور دو گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ اس نے اقرار کیا تھا کہ مجھے کچھ گمان نہیں ہوا تو گواہی مقبول نہ ہوگی۔
As has been known earlier in this book, hadd is dropped due to doubt, whether it is actual (fi'li) or legal (hukmi). Among legal doubt is that someone had intercourse with the slave-girl of a mukatib, or he gave permission to his slave to trade and the slave bought a slave-girl for trade, and then the master had intercourse with her, even though the slave had debts exceeding his property and his own value. Or he had intercourse with a slave-girl from the war booty before its distribution, whether before or after bringing it to Dar al-Islam for safekeeping. Or he had intercourse with a purchased slave-girl before she was purified from menstruation. Or he had intercourse with his wife who had become forbidden due to apostasy. Or a man allowed his wife to have intercourse with his adult son, or a husband had intercourse with his wife's mother (mother-in-law) or the daughter from a previous husband (step-daughter). In all these cases, even though the intercourse was haram, nevertheless the assumption of being halal in the actual act is sufficient, and if he claims the assumption, it will be accepted, even if he did not actually have that assumption. Now if a person claimed assumption (gunnan) and two witnesses testified that he had confessed that he had no assumption, the testimony will not be accepted.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with examples explaining the principle that doubt (shubha) drops the hadd penalty. It distinguishes between actual doubt (shubha fi'liyya) and legal doubt (shubha hukmiyya). Several cases of legal doubt are given where the act is haram but due to some factor, the person might have thought it halal: intercourse with a mukatib's slave-girl (ownership issues), with a slave-girl bought by a slave for trade (but the master's right is unclear due to debt), with war booty before distribution, with a purchased slave-girl before her waiting period, with an apostate wife, with in-laws by permission or mistake. In all these, if the person claims that he had an assumption (gunnan) that it was permissible, the claim is accepted and hadd is dropped, even if he actually had no such assumption. The burden of proof is on the claimant; if witnesses testify that he confessed to having no assumption, their testimony is not accepted because it contradicts his claim, and the claim is given precedence to avoid hudud. This underscores the Hanafi principle that hudud are to be averted by doubts (dar' al-hudud bi al-shubuhat).

Key Terms
شبه حکمی (shubha hukmiyya): A legal doubt arising from a semblance of legal permissibility.
گمان (gunnan): A subjective assumption or belief that the act might be permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person claims he had an assumption (gunnan) that the intercourse was halal, but witnesses testify that he confessed to having no such assumption, what is the ruling?
A) The witnesses' testimony is accepted and hadd is imposed.
B) The person's claim is accepted and the witnesses' testimony is rejected.
C) He must prove his assumption with evidence.
D) Hadd is not dropped because the act was clearly haram.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts a mere claim of assumption (gunnan) to drop hadd, prioritizing the avoidance of punishment over rigid proof.

Miscellaneous Rulings: Masturbation and Renting for Zina
Rulings on masturbation and renting for zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on masturbation and on hiring for zina, and identify the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf on the latter.

Core Idea
Masturbation is haram, using spouse's hand is makruh; hiring for zina triggers hadd per the stronger view.

This passage from al-Jawhara and al-Fath presents three distinct rulings touching on sexual offenses and their penalties. The first ruling clarifies the prohibition of masturbation and the distinction when a spouse's hand is used. The second ruling addresses the controversial case of renting a woman for zina, where a weak transmission suggests no hadd, but the relied-upon view imposes the full penalty. The third ruling ensures that even high-ranking officials are subject to hadd. By studying these rulings, you will learn how Hanafi fiqh categorizes sexual acts and applies the hudud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
List the three acts: masturbation, using wife's/slave-girl's hand, and hiring for zina. State the initial hukm for each: haram, makruh, and 'hadd not obligatory' vs 'hadd obligatory'.
The text uses clear terms: 'haram', 'makruh', and the ikhtilaf on hiring.
2
Distinguish the spousal hand case
Note why using one's own hand is haram but using the spouse's hand is only makruh and carries no punishment. This reflects the principle that marital intimacy is permitted but self-stimulation is prohibited.
The absence of ta'zir for makruh acts is key.
3
Analyze the ikhtilaf on hiring for zina
The text presents a weak transmission that says no hadd, and then the correct view that hadd is obligatory, analogized to a hired servant. Understand the doubt argument versus the analogy.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf resolved by tarjih.
4
Apply the third ruling on high-ranking officials
The passage extends the obligation of hadd to governors, emphasizing that authority does not prevent punishment. Execution requires the king's order, respecting legal procedure.
This ensures justice and deters abuse of power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۲۔ حلق (مشت زنی) کرنا حرام ہے۔ اور اگر ظاہر ہو جائے تو حاکم اسے سزا دے گا۔ اور اگر اپنی باندی یا بیوی کو اپنے آلہ تناسل سے ہاتھ ملنے دیا یہاں تک کہ انزال ہو گیا تو یہ مکروہ ہوگا اور اس پر کچھ سزا بھی واجب نہ ہوگی۔ (الجوہرہ) ۱۳۔ اگر کسی عورت کو کرایہ کے طور پر زنا کرنے کے لئے مقرر کیا تو حد واجب نہ ہوگی۔ (ت) مگر حق بات یہ ہے کہ حد واجب ہوگی جیسے اگر کوئی عورت خدمت کے لئے نو کر رکھی گئی۔ اور اس سے دلی کی تو حد واجب ہوگی۔ (الفتح) اگر کسی شہر کے حاکم یا صوبہ دار نے زنا کیا اور بعد ثبوت اس پر حد واجب ہوئی تو بادشاہ کے حکم سے اسے حد لگائی جائے گی۔
12. Masturbation is haram. And if it becomes apparent, the ruler will punish him. And if he lets his slave-girl or wife rub his penis until ejaculation, it is makruh and no punishment is obligatory upon him. (al-Jawhara) 13. If a woman is hired for zina, hadd is not obligatory. (T) But the correct view is that hadd will be obligatory, just as if a woman is hired for service and then he had intercourse with her, hadd is obligatory. (al-Fath) If the governor or ruler of a city committed zina, and after proof hadd becomes obligatory, then hadd will be executed by the order of the king.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage gives three miscellaneous rulings. First, masturbation (istimna) is forbidden (haram). If it becomes known, the ruler may impose a discretionary punishment (ta'zir). However, if a man uses his wife's or slave-girl's hand for stimulation to the point of ejaculation, it is only disliked (makruh) and no punishment is required. Second, regarding hiring a woman for zina: one transmission says no hadd because of doubt (the contract might give a semblance of legality), but the correct view (al-Fath) is that hadd is obligatory, analogized to a woman hired for service and then intercourse occurred—that is zina and hadd applies. Third, when a high-ranking official like a governor commits zina, once it is proven, the hadd is executed by the king's order, emphasizing that no one is above the law.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Masturbation (istimna') using the hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a man letting his wife rub his penis until ejaculation?
A) Haram and subject to punishment.
B) Makruh, no punishment.
C) Halal and recommended.
D) Mubah, but punishment if done publicly.

Key Takeaway
Masturbation is haram; using spouse's hand is makruh; hiring for zina incurs hadd according to the stronger Hanafi view, and no one is above the hudud.

Testimony on Old Hadd and Retraction from Testimony
Ruling on accepting testimony about an old hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on accepting testimony about an old hadd and identify the exception for qadhf.

Core Idea
Old testimony for hudud is rejected unless delay is excused; qadhf is excepted.

This lesson examines a key rule in Hanafi law of evidence: testimony about a hadd that occurred long ago is generally not accepted. The rationale is that delay may indicate falsehood or collusion. However, an important exception exists for the hadd of qadhf (false accusation of zina) because the right of the accused to vindicate his honor is not time-bound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
Recognize that the act is 'giving testimony about a hadd that occurred long ago.' The default ruling is that such testimony is not accepted.
The ruling applies to all hudud except qadhf.
2
Locate the dalil
The source is the matn of Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir. The proof is based on consensus (ijma) that delayed testimony is suspect.
Ijma provides the epistemic basis.
3
Note the exception
Only the hadd of qadhf is excepted. This is because the right of the accused (maqdhuf) to clear his name is not lost over time.
The exception is explicitly stated: إِلَّا فِي حَدِ الْقَدَفِ خَاصَّةٌ
4
Understand the condition
The default rejection applies only when there was no valid excuse for delay (e.g., distance from Imam, illness, fear). If a valid excuse exists, the testimony is accepted.
The condition is mentioned in the phrase: لَمْ يَمْنَعَهُمْ عَنْ إِقَامَتِهِ بُعْدُهُمْ عَنِ الْإِمَامِ
5
Apply the ruling
Apply the rule to concrete cases: theft, drinking, zina (rejected if no excuse); qadhf (accepted even without excuse, but if excuse exists, also accepted).
Al-Jami' al-Saghir adds that for theft, the witness must guarantee the stolen property if his delay caused loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الشهادة على الزناء والرجوع عنها ترجمہ باب، زنا کے بارے میں گواہی دینے اور اس سے پھر جانے کے بیان۔ پرانی حد کی گواہی کب اور کس حق میں قبول ہے اور کب مردود ہے قَالَ وَإِذَا شَهِدَ الشُّهُودُ بِحَدٍ مُتَقَادِمٍ لَمْ يَمْنَعُهُمْ عَنْ إِقَامَتِهِ بُعْدُهُمْ عَنِ الْإِمَامِ لَمْ تَقْبَلُ شَهَادَتْهُمْ إِلَّا فِي حَدِ الْقَدَفِ خَاصَّةٌ وَفِي الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ وَإِذَاشَهِدَ عَلَيْهِ الشُّهُودُ بِسَرْقَةٍ أَوْبِشُرْبِ خَمْرٍ أَوْ بِزِنَاءِ بَعْدَ حِينٍ لَمْ يُؤْخَذْبِهِ وَضَمِنَ السَّرْقَةَ ترجمه قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ اگر گواہوں نے کسی پر گزشتہ زمانہ میں حد جاری کئے جانے کی گواہی دی حالانکہ ان کو امام کے سامنے ہر وقت اس بارے میں گواہی دینے میں ایسی کوئی چیز بھی مانع نہ تھی یا مجبوری نہ تھی۔ مثلاً امام سے بہت دور رہنایا اس کے علاوہ کسی خاص بیماری میں مبتلا رہنا یا راستہ کا خوف وغیرہ۔ تو ان کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی۔ البتہ صرف حد قذف کے سلسلہ میں مقبول ہو جائے گی ۔ (یعنی اگر کسی نے دوسرے کو زنا کی تہمت لگائی جس کے کئے گواہ ہیں پھر جسے تہمت لگائی گئی تھی اس (مقذوف) نے ایک مدت کے بعد دعوی کیا اس وقت تک ان گواہوں نے گواہی دی تو ان کی گواہی مقبول ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ فوری گواہی واجب ہونے کی وجہ سے اس سے پہلے تک ان کی گواہی واجب نہیں تھی ۔ ) اور
Chapter on Testimony Regarding Zina and Retraction from It. Translation of Chapter: Statement about giving testimony regarding zina and retracting from it. When and for which right is testimony about an old hadd accepted, and when is it rejected? He said: 'When witnesses testify about an old (outdated) hadd, and there was no prevention from their establishing it such as distance from the Imam, their testimony is not accepted except specifically in the hadd of qadhf.' And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'When witnesses testify against him about theft, or drinking alcohol, or zina after some time, it is not acted upon, and he guarantees the theft.' Translation: Quduri (may Allah have mercy on him) said that if witnesses gave testimony about someone that a hadd should have been executed in the past, while they had no prevention from giving testimony before the Imam at all times regarding it, like extreme distance from the Imam, or suffering from a particular illness, or fear of the road, etc., then their testimony will not be accepted. However, only in the case of hadd of qadhf it will be accepted. (Meaning, if someone accused another of zina (qadhf) which has witnesses, and then the accused (maqdhuf) claimed after a period, and those witnesses testified, their testimony will be accepted because it was not obligatory for them to testify earlier until the claim was made.) And
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on testimony regarding zina and retraction. It presents a ruling from the matn (Quduri) that testimony about a hadd that occurred long ago is not accepted if there was no excuse for delay, except in the case of qadhf (false accusation of zina). The reasoning is that in hudud, delay may suggest falsehood or collusion, so only qadhf is exempt because the right of the accused (maqdhuf) to clear his name is not time-bound. The text also cites al-Jami' al-Saghir adding that for theft, drinking, or zina, old testimony is not acted upon; for theft, the witness must guarantee the stolen property because they caused loss by delay. This establishes a strict rule for hudud testimony to protect defendants from stale claims.

Key Terms
حد قدیم (hadd qadim): A hadd penalty for an offense that occurred long ago, with no recent claim.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina, which incurs the hadd of 80 lashes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which hadd is testimony about an old offense accepted despite delay?
A) Hadd for theft.
B) Hadd for drinking alcohol.
C) Hadd for zina.
D) Hadd for qadhf.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, testimony on an old hadd is generally not accepted unless there is a valid excuse, with the sole exception of qadhf.

The Effect of Delay (Taqaddum) on Testimony for Hudud
Ruling on acceptance of testimony after delay, with exceptions and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on the effect of delay on testimony for hudud, identify the exceptions, and explain the rational proof and the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Delay invalidates testimony for hudud pure to Allah, except qadhf and property guarantee, due to the witness's choice and motive.

In this passage, we examine the Hanafi position on a critical procedural rule: if witnesses delay their testimony about a hadd crime without a valid excuse, their testimony is rejected. This rule is rooted in the principle that hudud are established for deterrence, and delay raises suspicion of personal motive. However, there are important exceptions: testimony for qadhf (false accusation) and for the guarantee of stolen property are accepted despite delay. We will explore the underlying rational proof and the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is being ruled upon? Testimony given after a delay (taqaddum) for a hadd punishment. The ruling: such testimony is not accepted (ghayr maqbul) for hudud that are pure rights of Allah, specifically zina, theft, and drinking wine.
The ruling is from the matn of Quduri and expanded in Al-Jami' al-Saghir.
2
Locate the exceptions
The exception: testimony for the hadd of qadhf (false accusation) is accepted despite delay. Also, for theft, the testimony is accepted for the guarantee of the stolen property (personal right) but not for the hadd.
Qadhf involves a personal right (clearing reputation).
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is rational: the witness has a choice between concealing and revealing. Delay indicates either a bad motive (if for concealment) or sin (if not), so the testimony is tainted.
This distinguishes testimony from confession, where delay is not an issue.
4
Understand the dispute with Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that delay does not invalidate testimony for hudud, comparing them to rights of people and to confession. The Hanafi response: confession is different because one does not harm oneself; testimony may involve enmity.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Shafi'i, old testimony is accepted; under Hanafi, it is rejected except for qadhf.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on the measure of delay
The text discusses the length of delay: Abu Hanifa left it to the judge, Muhammad estimated one month (also from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and Al-Jami' al-Saghir indicated six months. The relied-upon view is one month.
For drinking wine, delay is measured by the disappearance of the smell.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الشهادة على الزناء والرجوع عنها
ترجمہ باب، زنا کے بارے میں گواہی دینے اور اس سے پھر جانے کے بیان۔
پرانی حد کی گواہی کب اور کس حق میں قبول ہے اور کب مردود ہے
قَالَ وَإِذَا شَهِدَ الشُّهُودُ بِحَدٍ مُتَقَادَمٍ لَمْ يَمْنَعُهُمْ عَنْ إِقَامَتِهِ بُعْدُهُمْ عَنِ الْإِمَامِ لَمْ تَقْبَلُ شَهَادَتْهُمْ إِلَّا فِي حَدِ الْقَدَفِ خَاصَّةٌ وَفِي الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ وَإِذَاشَهِدَ عَلَيْهِ الشُّهُودُ بِسَرْقَةٍ أَوْبِشُرْبِ خَمْرٍ أَوْ بِزِنَاءِ بَعْدَ حِينٍ لَمْ يُؤْخَذْبِهِ وَضَمِنَ السَّرْقَةَ
ترجمه قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ اگر گواہوں نے کسی پر گزشتہ زمانہ میں حد جاری کئے جانے کی گواہی دی حالانکہ ان کو امام کے سامنے ہر وقت اس بارے میں گواہی دینے میں ایسی کوئی چیز بھی مانع نہ تھی یا مجبوری نہ تھی۔ مثلاً امام سے بہت دور رہنایا اس کے علاوہ کسی خاص بیماری میں مبتلا رہنا یا راستہ کا خوف وغیرہ۔ تو ان کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی۔ البتہ صرف حد قذف کے سلسلہ میں مقبول ہو جائے گی ۔ (یعنی اگر کسی نے دوسرے کو زنا کی تہمت لگائی جس کے کئے گواہ ہیں پھر جسے تہمت لگائی گئی تھی اس (مقذوف) نے ایک مدت کے بعد دعوی کیا اس وقت تک ان گواہوں نے گواہی دی تو ان کی گواہی مقبول ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ فوری گواہی واجب ہونے کی وجہ سے اس سے پہلے تک ان کی گواہی واجب نہیں تھی ۔ ) اور
باب الشهادة على الزناء والرجوع عنها.
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ اگر گواہوں نے کسی شخص پر چوری کرنے کی یا شراب خوری کی یاز نا کرنے کی گواہی کافی دنوں کے بعد دی تو ایسی گواہی پر اسے پکڑا نہیں جائے گا مگر چوری کئے ہوئے مال کا ضامن ضرور ہو گا (ف۔ یعنی وہ گواہی جو کسی عذر کے بغیر موخر کی گئی ہو وہ حد کے واسطے مقبول نہ ہوگی۔ لیکن چوری کیا ہوا مال جو کسی بندہ کا حق ہوتا ہے اس میں یہ گواہی بھی مقبول ہوگی۔ البتہ جب چور پر چوری کی حد قائم نہ ہو تو چوری کئے ہوئے مال کی ضمانت اس پر لازم ہوگی۔ پھر یہ معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ تقادم ( تاخیر اور پرانا ہونے کی مقدار میں تفصیل ہے۔ اس طرح سے کہ شراب پینے کے بارے میں تا خیر اس وقت ہو جائے گی جب کہ شراب پینے والے کے منہ سے شراب کی بدبو ختم ہو چکی ہو اس کے بعد گواہوں نے گواہی دی ہو اور زنا، چوری وغیرہ میں تا خیر یہ ہے کہ بغیر عذر کے ایک مہینہ گزر جانے کے بعد گواہی دی ہو اور یہی قول اصح ہے۔ اور اگر اتنی تاخیر ہو جانے کے بعد زنا کی گواہی دی تو بعض فقہاء کے نزدیک ان گواہوں کو حد قذف ( تہمت کی حد ) لگائی جائے گی اور دوسروں نے کہا ہے کہ نہیں لگائی جائے گی۔ (القاضی خان ) الحاصل جب تاخیر ہو جائے اور اس کے بعد گواہ اپنی گواہی دیں اور وہ تاخیر بغیر کسی عذر معقول کے ہو تو اس کی گواہی مقبول نہ ہوگی سوائے حد قذف کے اور چوری کئے مال کی ضمان کے۔ تشریح... قَالَ وَإِذَا شَهِدَ الشُّهُودُ بِحَدٍ مُتَقَادَمٍ لَمْ يَمْنَعُهُمْ عَنْ إِقَامَتِهِ بُعْدُ هُمْ عَنِ الْإِمَامِ لَم الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
وہ حدود جو محض اللہ تعالیٰ کا حق ہیں پرانے ہونے سے ساقط ہو جاتی ہیں، اقوال فقہاء
وَالْأَصْلُ اَنَّ الْحُدُودَ الْخَالِصَةَ حَقًّا لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى تَبْطُلُ بِالتَّقَادُمِ خِلَافَاً لِلشَّافِعِيِّ وَهُوَ يَعْتَبِرُ هَا بِحُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ وَبِالْإِقْرَارِ الَّذِي هُوَ إِحْدَى الْحُجَّتَيْنِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الشَّاهِدَ مُخَيَّرْبَيْنَ الْحَسْبَتَيْنِ مِنْ آدَاءِ الشَّهَادَةِ وَالسَّتْرِ فَالتَّاخِيْرُ إِنْ كَانَ لِاخْتِيَارِ السَّتْرِ فَالْإِقْدَامُ عَلَى الْآدَاءِ بَعْدَ ذَالِكَ لَصَغِيْنَةٍ هَيَّجَتْهُ وَلِعَدَاوَةٍ حَرَّكَتْهُ فَيْتَهُمُ فِيهَا وَإِنْ كَانَ التَّاخِيرَلَا لِلسَّتْرِيَصِيرُ فَاسِقًا أَثِمَا فَتَيَقَّنَّا بِالْمَانِعِ بِخِلافِ الْأَقْرَارِ لَانَّ الْإِنْسَانَ لَا يُعَادِي نَفْسَهُ فَحَدُّ الزِّنَاءِ وَشُرْبِ الْحُمْرِ وَ السَّرِقَةِ خَالِصُ حَقِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى حَتَّى يَصحَ الرَّجُوعُ عَنْهَا بَعْدَ الْإِقْرَارِ فَيَكُونُ التَّقَادُمُ فِيهِ مَانِعَا وَحَدُ الْقَذَفِ فِيهِ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنْ دَفْعِ الْعَارِعَنْهُ وَلِهَذَا لَا يَصِحُ رَجُوعُهُ بَعْدَ الْإِقْرَارِ وَالتَّقَادُمُ غَيْرُ مَانِعِ فِي حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ لِاَنَّ الدَّعْوَى فِيهِ شَرط فَيَحْتَمِلُ تَاخِيرُ هُمْ عَلَى إِنْعِدَامِ الدَّعْوَى فَلَا يُوجِبُ تَفْسِيقَهُمْ بِخِلَافِ حَةِ السَّرِقَةِ لِأَنَّ الدَّعْوَى لَيْسَتْ بِشَرْطٍ لِلْحَدِلَانَّهُ خَالِصُ حَقِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَىٰ عَلَى مَامَرَّ وَإِنَّمَا شُرِطَتْ لِلْمَالِ وَلَانَّ الْحُكْمَ يُدَارُ عَلَى كَوْنِ الْحَدِ حَقًّا لِلَّهِ فَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ وُجُودُ التَّهْمَةِ فِي كُلِّ فَرْدِ وَّلَاتَ السَّرِقَةَ تُقَامُ عَلَى الْإِسْتِسْرَارِ عَلَى غِرَّةِ عَنِ الْمَالِكِ فَيَجِبُ عَلَى الشَّاهِدِ إِعْلَامُهُ وَبِالْكِتَمَانِ يَصِيرُ فَاسِقًا أَثِمَاثُمَّ التَّقَادُمُ كَمَا يَمْنَعُ قَبُولَ الشَّهَادَةِ فِي الْإِبْتِدَاءِ يَمْنَعُ الْإِقَامَةَ بَعْدَ الْقَضَاءِ عِنْدَنَا خَلَافًا لِزُفَرَ حَتَّى لَوْهَرَبَ بَعْدَ مَاضُرِبَ بَعْضَ التحدثُمَّ أُخِذَ بَعْدَ مَا تَقَادَمَ الزَّمَانُ لَايُقَامُ عَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ لِاَنَّ الْإِمْضَاءَ مِنَ الْقَضَاءِ فِى بَابِ الْحُدُودِ وَاخْتَلَفُوا فِي حَدِ التَّقَادُمِ وَأَشَارَ فِي الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ إِلى سِتَّةِ أَشْهُرٍ فَإِنَّهُ قَالَ بَعْدَ حِينٍ وَهَكَذَا أَشَارَ الطَّحَاوِي وَأَبُو حَنِيفَةَ لَمْ يُقَدِرْ فِي ذَالِكَ وَفَوَّضَهُ إِلَى رَأيِ الْقَاضِي فِى كُلَّ عَصْرٍ وَعَنْ مُحَمَّدٌ أَنَّهُ قَدَّرَهُ بِشَهْرٍ لَانَّ مَا دُونَهُ عَاجِلٌ وَ هُوَ رِوَايَةٌ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَابِى يُوسُفَ وَهُوَ الْأَصَحُ وَهَذَا إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ بَيْنَ الْقَاضِي وَبَيْنَهُمْ مَسِيْرَةُ شَهْرٍ أَمَّا إِذَا كَانَ تُقْبَلُ شَهَادَتْهُمْ لِاَنَّ الْمَانِعَ بُعْدُ هُمْ عَن الْإِمَامِ فَلَا يَتَحَقَّقُ السُّهُمَةُ وَالتَّقَادُمُ فِي حَدَ الشَّرْب
Chapter: Testimony on Zina and Retraction from It. Translation of chapter: Statement on giving testimony about zina and retracting from it. When is old hadd testimony accepted and when is it rejected? He (Quduri) said: When witnesses testify about a hadd that is old (mutqaddim), and [the time] did not prevent them from establishing it due to their distance from the Imam, their testimony is not accepted except specifically in the hadd of qadhf (false accusation). And in Al-Jami' al-Saghir: When witnesses testify against him about theft, or about drinking wine, or about zina after a time, he is not seized for it, and he guarantees the stolen property. Translation: Quduri (may Allah have mercy on him) said: If witnesses testify against someone that a hadd was carried out in the past, even though there was no obstacle to them testifying before the Imam at all times, such as being very far from the Imam, or suffering from a specific illness, or fear of the road, etc., then their testimony is not accepted. However, it is accepted specifically regarding hadd qadhf (meaning if someone accused another of zina, and there are witnesses to that, then the accused (maqdhuif) claimed after a period, and at that time the witnesses testified, their testimony is accepted because their immediate testimony was not obligatory earlier). And Chapter: Testimony on Zina and Retraction from It. In Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, volume six: In Al-Jami' al-Saghir, if witnesses testify against someone about committing theft, or drinking wine, or zina after many days, he is not seized based on it, but he is liable for the stolen property. That is, testimony that is delayed without excuse is not accepted for the hadd, but for the stolen property which is a right of a person, this testimony is accepted. However, when the hadd of theft is not established, he becomes liable for the stolen property. Then it must be known that the measure of delay (taqaddum) has detail: Regarding drinking wine, delay occurs when the smell of wine from the drinker's mouth has disappeared; for zina, theft, etc., delay occurs when one month passes without excuse, and this is the more correct view. If testimony about zina is given after such delay, some jurists say the witnesses should be given the hadd of qadhf, others say no. (al-Qadi Khan) Summary: When delay occurs and then witnesses testify, and the delay is without any valid excuse, their testimony is not accepted except for hadd qadhf and for the guarantee of stolen property. Explanation: 'He said: When witnesses testify about an old hadd...' etc. The meaning is clear from the translation. The hadd punishments that are purely the right of Allah are invalidated by delay, contrary to al-Shafi'i, who considers them like rights of people and like confession (iqrar), which is one of the two proofs. Our (Hanafi) proof: The witness has a choice between two rewards: giving testimony or concealing. If the delay was for the sake of concealment, then coming forward afterward is due to a petty matter that incited him or enmity that moved him, so suspicion arises. If the delay was not for concealment, he becomes a sinful wrongdoer, so we know for certain the obstacle. This is unlike confession because a person does not antagonize himself. So the hadd of zina, drinking wine, and theft are pure rights of Allah, such that retraction after confession is valid, so delay in them is an obstacle. The hadd of qadhf involves a right of a person (haqq al-'abd) because it removes disgrace from him, and therefore retraction after confession is not valid, and delay is not an obstacle in the rights of people because a claim (da'wa) is required, so their delay may be due to absence of claim, so it does not necessitate declaring them sinful. This is unlike the hadd of theft because a claim is not required for the hadd, as it is a pure right of Allah as above; it is required only for the property. And because the ruling revolves around the hadd being a right of Allah, the existence of suspicion is not considered in every individual case. The theft hadd is established on stealth without the owner's knowledge, so the witness must inform, and concealment makes him sinful. Then delay, as it prevents acceptance of testimony initially, also prevents execution after judgment according to us, contrary to Zufar. So if he flees after part of the hadd was executed, then is caught after time has passed, the hadd is not executed because execution is part of judgment in the chapter of hudud. They differed on the limit of delay. In Al-Jami' al-Saghir, it refers to six months, as he said 'after a time'. Similarly, al-Tahawi indicated. Abu Hanifa did not specify a limit and left it to the judge's opinion in every era. From Muhammad, he estimated it as one month because less than that is immediate. This is a report from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and it is the most correct. This is when there is not a month's journey between the judge and them. But if there is, their testimony is accepted because the obstacle is their distance from the Imam, so suspicion does not materialize. And delay in the hadd of drinking [is as described].
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school on the effect of delay in testimony for hudud punishments. It begins with the matn from Quduri: testimony about an old hadd (one that occurred long ago) is not accepted unless it is specifically for the hadd of qadhf (false accusation of zina). This is because the witness had a choice to conceal or reveal; if they delayed without excuse, their sudden testimony after a long time raises suspicion of personal motive or enmity, so it is rejected. The text then expands using Al-Jami' al-Saghir, adding that for theft, drinking wine, or zina, after a significant delay, the accused is not convicted of the hadd, but for theft, the witness's testimony is still accepted regarding the guarantee of the stolen property (since that is a personal right). The commentary defines 'delay' differently for different offenses: for drinking, it is when the smell has faded; for zina and theft, it is after one month without excuse. The relied-upon view (al-asahh) is one month. The passage then provides the legal reasoning (asl): hudud that are pure rights of Allah are invalidated by delay, contrary to Shafi'i. The Hanafi proof is rational: the witness's delay indicates a bad motive. The distinction between rights of Allah and rights of people is key: in qadhf, because it involves a personal right (clearing one's reputation), delay does not prevent acceptance. The text also notes a disagreement with Zufar: even after a judgment has been passed, if the culprit flees and is caught later after a long time, the hadd is not executed. Finally, it details the various opinions on the length of delay: Abu Hanifa left it to the judge; in Al-Jami' al-Saghir it was six months; but the most correct (al-asahh) is one month from Muhammad, also narrated from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The teacher should emphasize the underlying principle: hudud are established for deterrence and public interest, not for vengeance, and delay in testimony undermines reliability. Students should also note the exception for qadhf and the practical consequence for theft (guarantee).

Key Terms
تقادم (taqaddum): Delay or passage of time that makes the testimony 'old'; legal impediment for accepting testimony on hudud.
حد (hadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for specific crimes (zina, qadhf, theft, drinking wine).
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina; its hadd is 80 lashes and involves a personal right (clearing reputation).
شهادة (shahadah): Testimony given in court by witnesses; its acceptance depends on conditions including timeliness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if witnesses testify about a theft that occurred two months ago without any valid excuse, what is the ruling?
A) The testimony is accepted and the thief is punished with hadd (amputation).
B) The testimony is not accepted for hadd but the thief must guarantee the stolen property.
C) The testimony is accepted only if the thief confesses.
D) The witnesses themselves are punished for qadhf.

Key Takeaway
Delay in testimony for hudud pure to Allah invalidates it, except for hadd qadhf and property guarantee, due to the witness's potential motive and the distinction between rights of Allah and rights of people.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

Delay Invalidates Testimony for Pure Rights of Allah
Ruling on delay invalidating testimony for pure rights of Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on delay in testimony for hudud, distinguish between pure rights of Allah and rights of servants, and apply the rule to specific hadd cases (zina, shurb, sariqah, qadhf).

Core Idea
Delay in testimony invalidates hudud that are pure rights of Allah, but not rights of servants.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, the author explains how delay (taqādum) in presenting testimony affects the establishment of hadd punishments. The central principle distinguishes between hudud that are pure rights of Allah (ḥuqūq Allāh al-khāliṣah) and those that include a right of a servant (ḥaqq al-ʿabd). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rules of testimony in criminal cases. The passage also addresses the limits of delay and exceptions such as distance from the judge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Delayed testimony for a hadd punishment. The ruling: for pure rights of Allah, such testimony is invalidated. For rights of servants, it is not.
Note the key term 'taqādum' which means delay without valid excuse.
2
Understand the Hanafi proof
The witness has a choice between testifying and concealing. Delay implies either that the witness chose concealment (then later testifies due to hatred/enmity) or that he became a sinner (fāsiq) by delaying. Both scenarios make the testimony suspect or rejected.
This is a rational proof (dalīl ʿaqlī) based on the witness's motives.
3
Distinguish between hadd types
Identify which hudud are pure rights of Allah: ḥadd al-zinā, ḥadd al-shurb, ḥadd al-sariqah. Which include a servant's right: ḥadd al-qadhf (because it removes disgrace). The presence of a servant's right changes the ruling on delay.
For qadhf, delay does not invalidate testimony; also retraction after confession is not valid.
4
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf on duration
Abu Hanifa left the duration to the judge's discretion. Al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr indicates six months. Imam Muhammad's view (also narrated from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) specifies one month, which is the most correct (al-aṣaḥḥ).
If witnesses are a month's travel away, distance excuses the delay.

باب الشهادة على الزناء والرجوع عنها. قَالَ وَإِذَا شَهِدَ الشُّهُودُ بِحَدٍ مُتَقَادَمٍ لَمْ يَمْنَعُهُمْ عَنْ إِقَامَتِهِ بُعْدُهُمْ عَنِ الْإِمَامِ. وَالْأَصْلُ أَنَّ الْحُدُودَ الْخَالِصَةَ حَقًّا لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى تَبْطُلُ بِالتَّقَادُمِ خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِيِّ، وَهُوَ يَعْتَبِرُهَا بِحُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ وَبِالْإِقْرَارِ الَّذِي هُوَ إِحْدَى الْحُجَّتَيْنِ. وَلَنَا أَنَّ الشَّاهِدَ مُخَيَّرٌ بَيْنَ الْحَسْبَتَيْنِ مِنْ أَدَاءِ الشَّهَادَةِ وَالسَّتْرِ، فَالتَّاخِيرُ إِنْ كَانَ لِاخْتِيَارِ السَّتْرِ فَالْإِقْدَامُ عَلَى الْأَدَاءِ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ لِصَغِينَةٍ هَيَّجَتْهُ وَلِعَدَاوَةٍ حَرَّكَتْهُ فَيُتَّهَمُ فِيهَا، وَإِنْ كَانَ التَّاخِيرُ لَا لِلسَّتْرِ يَصِيرُ فَاسِقًا آثِمًا، فَتَيَقَّنَّا بِالْمَانِعِ. بِخِلَافِ الْإِقْرَارِ لِأَنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ لَا يُعَادِي نَفْسَهُ. فَحَدُّ الزِّنَاءِ وَشُرْبِ الْخَمْرِ وَالسَّرِقَةِ خَالِصُ حَقِّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى حَتَّى يَصِحَّ الرَّجُوعُ عَنْهَا بَعْدَ الْإِقْرَارِ، فَيَكُونُ التَّقَادُمُ فِيهِ مَانِعًا. وَحَدُّ الْقَذْفِ فِيهِ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنْ دَفْعِ الْعَارِ عَنْهُ، وَلِهَذَا لَا يَصِحُّ رُجُوعُهُ بَعْدَ الْإِقْرَارِ، وَالتَّقَادُمُ غَيْرُ مَانِعٍ فِي حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ لِأَنَّ الدَّعْوَى فِيهِ شَرْطٌ فَيَحْتَمِلُ تَأْخِيرُهُمْ عَلَى انْعِدَامِ الدَّعْوَى فَلَا يُوجِبُ تَفْسِيقَهُمْ. بِخِلَافِ حَدِّ السَّرِقَةِ لِأَنَّ الدَّعْوَى لَيْسَتْ بِشَرْطٍ لِلْحَدِّ لِأَنَّهُ خَالِصُ حَقِّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى، وَإِنَّمَا شُرِطَتْ لِلْمَالِ. وَلِأَنَّ الْحُكْمَ يُدَارُ عَلَى كَوْنِ الْحَدِّ حَقًّا لِلَّهِ فَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ وُجُودُ التُّهْمَةِ فِي كُلِّ فَرْدٍ. وَلِأَنَّ السَّرِقَةَ تُقَامُ عَلَى الِاسْتِسْرَارِ عَلَى غِرَّةٍ مِنَ الْمَالِكِ فَيَجِبُ عَلَى الشَّاهِدِ إِعْلَامُهُ، وَبِالْكِتْمَانِ يَصِيرُ فَاسِقًا آثِمًا. ثُمَّ التَّقَادُمُ كَمَا يَمْنَعُ قَبُولَ الشَّهَادَةِ فِي الِابْتِدَاءِ يَمْنَعُ الْإِقَامَةَ بَعْدَ الْقَضَاءِ عِنْدَنَا خِلَافًا لِزُفَرَ، حَتَّى لَوْ هَرَبَ بَعْدَ مَا ضُرِبَ بَعْضُ الْحَدِّ ثُمَّ أُخِذَ بَعْدَ مَا تَقَادَمَ الزَّمَانُ لَا يُقَامُ عَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ لِأَنَّ الْإِمْضَاءَ مِنَ الْقَضَاءِ فِي بَابِ الْحُدُودِ. وَاخْتَلَفُوا فِي حَدِّ التَّقَادُمِ، وَأَشَارَ فِي الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ إِلَى سِتَّةِ أَشْهُرٍ فَإِنَّهُ قَالَ بَعْدَ حِينٍ، وَهَكَذَا أَشَارَ الطَّحَاوِي. وَأَبُو حَنِيفَةَ لَمْ يُقَدِّرْ فِي ذَلِكَ وَفَوَّضَهُ إِلَى رَأْيِ الْقَاضِي فِي كُلِّ عَصْرٍ، وَعَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّهُ قَدَّرَهُ بِشَهْرٍ لِأَنَّ مَا دُونَهُ عَاجِلٌ، وَهُوَ رِوَايَةٌ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ وَهُوَ الْأَصَحُ. وَهَذَا إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ بَيْنَ الْقَاضِي وَبَيْنَهُمْ مَسِيرَةُ شَهْرٍ، أَمَّا إِذَا كَانَ تُقْبَلُ شَهَادَتُهُمْ لِأَنَّ الْمَانِعَ بُعْدُهُمْ عَنِ الْإِمَامِ فَلَا يَتَحَقَّقُ التُّهْمَةُ. وَالتَّقَادُمُ فِي حَدِّ الشُّرْبِ كَذَلِكَ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ، وَعِنْدَهُمَا يُقَدَّرُ بِزَوَالِ الرَّائِحَةِ عَلَى مَا يَأْتِي فِي بَابِهِ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى.
Chapter: Testimony regarding adultery and retraction from it. He said: When witnesses testify regarding a delayed hadd, their distance from the imam does not prevent them from establishing it. The principle is that the hadds that are pure right of Allah Almighty are invalidated by delay, contrary to al-Shafi'i, and he considers them like the rights of servants and like the confession which is one of the two proofs. Our proof: the witness is given a choice between two rewards: performing testimony and concealing, so if the delay was for choosing concealment, then proceeding to testimony after that is due to a hatred that provoked him or an enmity that moved him, so he is suspected in it; and if the delay was not for concealment, he becomes a transgressor, a sinner, so we are certain of the preventing factor. Unlike confession, because a person does not become an enemy of himself. So the hadd of adultery, drinking wine, and theft are pure right of Allah Almighty, such that retraction from them is valid after confession, so delay in them is a preventing factor. The hadd of qadhf has a right of the servant because it involves removing disgrace from him, and therefore retraction from it after confession is not valid, and delay is not a preventing factor in the rights of servants because claim is a condition in it, so their delay can be attributed to the absence of claim, so it does not necessitate declaring them transgressors. Unlike the hadd of theft, because claim is not a condition for the hadd, as it is pure right of Allah Almighty, and it is only conditioned for the property. And because the ruling is based on the hadd being right of Allah, so the presence of suspicion is not considered in every individual. And because theft is committed secretly, catching the owner unaware, so it is obligatory on the witness to inform him, and by concealment he becomes a transgressor, a sinner. Then delay, just as it prevents acceptance of testimony initially, prevents execution after judgment according to us, contrary to Zufar; such that if one fled after some of the hadd was inflicted, then was caught after a long time, the hadd is not executed upon him, because implementation is part of judgment in the chapter of hadds. They differed on the limit of delay: al-Jami' al-Saghir indicated six months, for he said 'after a time', and al-Tahawi indicated likewise. Abu Hanifa did not specify it and delegated it to the opinion of the judge in every age. From Muhammad it is reported that he specified it as a month, because less than that is immediate, and this is a narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and it is the most correct. This is if there is not between the judge and them a month's journey; but if there is, their testimony is accepted because the preventing factor is their distance from the imam, so suspicion does not materialize. The delay in the hadd of drinking is similar according to Muhammad, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is determined by the disappearance of the odor, as will come in its chapter, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya addresses the effect of delay (taqadum) in testimony for hadd punishments. The author begins by stating the ruling: if witnesses testify regarding a hadd that is delayed (i.e., they delayed in coming forward without a valid excuse), their distance from the imam is not a valid excuse. The fundamental principle is that hadds which are pure rights of Allah (huquq Allah al-khalisah) are invalidated by delay. This is contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i, who analogizes such hadds to rights of servants and to confession (iqrar). The Hanafi proof is that a witness is given two options: to testify or to conceal. If he chooses concealment and then later testifies, it is likely due to personal hatred or enmity, so his testimony is suspect. If his delay was not for concealment, he becomes a sinner (fasiq), and thus his testimony is rejected. Confession, however, is different because a person does not harm himself. The hadds of zina, shurb al-khamr, and sariqah are pure rights of Allah, so delay prevents their acceptance. In contrast, the hadd of qadhf involves a right of the servant (haqq al-'abd) because it removes disgrace; thus delay does not prevent acceptance, and retraction after confession is invalid. For theft, unlike other hudud, a claim (da'wa) is not required for the hadd itself but only for the property. The witness is obligated to inform the owner; concealing makes him a fasiq. Delay also prevents execution of the hadd after a judgment has been passed, according to the Hanafis, unlike Zufar. The scholars differed on the definition of delay: indications from Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir suggest six months; Abu Hanifa left it to the judge's discretion; Muhammad's own view, also narrated from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, specifies one month, which is the most correct. An exception is made if the witnesses are a month's travel away, as then the delay is due to distance, not suspicion. For the hadd of drinking, Muhammad says the same rule applies, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (together) specify that delay is determined by the disappearance of the alcohol odor from the mouth.

Key Terms
تقادم (taqādum): Delay in presenting testimony after witnessing an act without a valid excuse.
حق الله (ḥaqq Allāh): A right belonging exclusively to Allah, such as hadd penalties, where the state prosecutes without a private claimant.
حق العبد (ḥaqq al-ʿabd): A right belonging to an individual, such as the right to have qadhf punished, which includes a private interest.
حد القذف (ḥadd al-qadhf): The prescribed punishment for falsely accusing a chaste person of adultery.
اقرار (iqrār): Confession of a crime by the accused.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the most correct (al-asahh) duration for delay that invalidates testimony for hudud according to the Hanafi school?
A) One month
B) Six months
C) One year
D) Left to the judge's discretion

Key Takeaway
Hudud that are pure rights of Allah are invalidated by delay in testimony because delay indicates either malice or sinfulness of the witness, but this does not apply to hudud involving a servant's right like qadhf.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
Invalidation of Hudud by Delay and Definition of Long Period
States the principle that pure Hudud are invalidated by delay and defines the long period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why pure Hudud are invalidated by delay, state the most correct Hanafi definition of a long period, and compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on this issue.

Core Idea
Pure Hudud are invalidated by delay; the most correct Hanafi view defines a long period as one month absent travel distance.

In the chapter on testimony for zina, the author establishes a key principle: pure rights of Allah (Hudud) become invalid if testimony is delayed. The passage then navigates an intra-Hanafi debate on what constitutes a 'long period' and contrasts the Shafi'i position that accepts delayed testimony. Understanding this principle is crucial for determining when Hudud punishments can be enforced.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Read the opening statement: pure Hudud are invalidated by delay (تقادم). Understand that until the hadd is fully executed, the qadi's judgment is incomplete.
This fundamental rule distinguishes rights of Allah from rights of people.
2
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Three positions are presented: Imam Muhammad (6 months in al-Jami' al-Saghir), Imam Abu Hanifa (no fixed duration, left to qadi), and another narration from Imam Muhammad (1 month). Determine which view is deemed 'most correct' (الأصح).
The text explicitly states that 1 month is الأصح, provided there is no travel distance between qadi and witnesses.
3
Apply the Condition of Travel Distance
The long period (1 month) is only considered if the witnesses are not at a one-month travel distance from the qadi. If they are that far, the delay is excused because the distance itself is an obstacle.
This condition protects witnesses from accusations of malice when distance causes delay.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i Position
The Shafi'i school holds that Hudud are not invalidated by delay, comparing them to rights of people. Contrast this with the Hanafi stance that delay makes testimony suspect.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Hanafis reject delayed testimony for Hudud; Shafi'is accept it.
5
Examine the Benefit on Confession
The passage notes that if a fornicator confesses after a long period, his confession is accepted. This is because there is no suspicion of coercion or false accusation (tuhmah) in self-confession.
This exception highlights the rationale behind the rule: suspicion (tuhmah) is the basis for invalidation.

باب الشهادة على الزناء والرجوع عنها. . اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم ضروری ہے کہ اس کے بارے میں فیصلہ سنائے اسی طرح یہ بھی لازم ہے کہ اسے نافذ بھی کر دیے یا حد نکا دے۔ بس جب تک کہ حد کمل طور پر جاری نہیں کی گئی اس وقت تک قاضی کا فیصلہ اور اس کا حکم بھی مکمل نہیں ہوا ہے۔ پھر تصادم یا تاخیر کی تعین کے بارے میں کتنی مدت کو زمانہ دراز کہا جائے گا فقہاء کا اختلاف ہے۔ امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ نے اس کی طرف جامع صغیر میں یہ اشارہ کیا ہے کہ چھ ماہ ۔ جیسا کہ قسم کے باب میں گزر گیا ہے۔ اور امام طحاوی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے بھی اسی بات کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے اور امام ابو حنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے اس کے لئے کسی نے مدت کی بھی تعین نہیں کی ہے۔ بلکہ اس کا فیصلہ ہر زمانہ کے قاضی کی رائے پر چھوڑ دیا ہے۔ اور امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے ایک روایت میں ایک ماہ کی مدت کو زمانہ دراز کہا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس سے بھی کم مدت کو قریبی زمانہ کہا جاتا ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ اور ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ سے بھی یہی ایک روایتہ ہے۔ اور یہی قول اصح ہے اور اتنی مدت کو زمانه در از اسی صورت میں کہا جائے گا جب کہ قاضی اور گواہوں کے درمیان ایک ماہ کی مسافت ( فاصلہ ) نہ ہو اور اگر اتنی ہی دوری ہو تو ان کی گواہی فوز اقبول کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ امام سے اتنے فاصلہ پر رہنا ادائیگی گواہی میں در حقیقت ایک رکاوٹ ہے یعنی انہوں نے اپنے طور پر ادائیگی گواہی میں دیر نہیں کی ہے۔ اس لئے ان پر کینہ اور دشمنی وغیرہ کی تہمت نہیں لگ سکتی اور شراب پینے کی حد میں زمانہ دراز ہونے کی مقدار بھی امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے یہاں ایک ماہ ہے۔ لیکن امام ابو حنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ وامام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک دیر ہونے کی مدت یہ ہوگی کہ شراب پینے والے کے منہ سے شراب کی بدبو جاتی رہے۔ چنانچہ اس کا بیان انشاء اللہ تعالی شراب خوری کے بیان میں آئے گا۔ (فائدہ اگر زانی نے زمانہ دراز گزرنے کے بعد اپنے زنا کا اقرار کیا تو بھی اس کا اقرار مان لیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس میں تہمت کا کوئی موقع نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ مصنف رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے پہلے بیان کر دیا ہے )۔
Chapter on Testimony for Zina and Retraction from It. Ashraf al-Bidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 6. It is necessary that the qadi passes a verdict regarding it, and also that he implements it or executes the hadd. As long as the hadd is not fully carried out, the qadi's verdict and his order are not complete. Then, regarding the determination of collision or delay, there is disagreement among the jurists as to what duration is considered a long period. Imam Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, indicated in al-Jami' al-Saghir that it is six months, as passed in the chapter on oaths. Imam Tahawi, may Allah have mercy on him, also indicated the same. Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, did not fix any duration for it; rather, he left its decision to the discretion of the qadi of each time. Imam Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, in one narration, called a period of one month a long period, because a shorter period is called a near period. This same narration is also from Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on them. And this is the most correct view. And such a duration will be considered a long period only when there is not a distance of one month between the qadi and the witnesses. If there is such a distance, their testimony will be accepted, because living at such a distance from the imam is actually an obstacle in giving testimony, meaning they did not delay giving testimony on their own accord. Therefore, they cannot be accused of malice, enmity, etc. And for the hadd of drinking wine, the measure of a long period according to Imam Muhammad is also one month. But according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, the duration of delay is that the smell of wine from the drinker's mouth disappears. So its explanation will come in the chapter on wine-drinking, Allah willing. (Benefit: If a fornicator confesses his zina after a long period has passed, his confession will still be accepted, because there is no opportunity for accusation. As the author, may Allah have mercy on him, has explained earlier.)
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on testimony for zina and retraction. It states a foundational principle: Hudud that are pure rights of Allah are invalidated by delay (تقادم). The author then explains that until the hadd is fully executed, the qadi's judgment is not complete. The main issue here is defining what constitutes a 'long period' of delay, which affects the validity of testimony. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir says six months; Imam Tahawi agrees. Imam Abu Hanifa leaves it to the qadi's discretion without fixing a duration. In another narration, Imam Muhammad says one month, and that is deemed the most correct view (قول اصح). The long period is only considered when there is not a one-month travel distance between the qadi and witnesses; otherwise, the delay is excused. For the hadd of wine, the duration for delay is one month according to Imam Muhammad, but according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it is until the smell of wine from the drinker's mouth disappears. Finally, a benefit: if a fornicator confesses after a long period, his confession is accepted because there is no suspicion of coercion or false accusation.

Key Terms
حدود خالصہ (hudud khalisah): Pure Hudud that are exclusively rights of Allah, such as hadd for zina, wine, theft.
زمانہ دراز (zamana daraaz): A long period of delay that invalidates testimony or hadd.
تقادم (taqadum): Delay or lapse of time that causes invalidation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view in the Hanafi school, what duration is considered a 'long period' (زمانہ دراز) for invalidating testimony in hudud?
A) Six months
B) One month
C) Until the wine smell disappears
D) Left entirely to the qadi's discretion

Key Takeaway
Pure Hudud are invalidated by delay; the most correct Hanafi view defines a long period as one month absent travel distance, and confession remains valid even after delay.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

Retraction from Testimony in Hudud: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Analyzes the invalidation of pure Hudud by delay in testimony, with four-fold analysis of delay, testimony, retraction, and confession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that retraction from testimony after delay invalidates pure Hudud, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Delay in testimony reveals suspect motives; retraction invalidates Hudud because it contradicts prompt establishment of testimony.

This passage delves into a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the effect of delay in testimony in Hudud cases. The Hanafi position, grounded in the Quranic command to establish testimony promptly, holds that any delay invalidates the hadd. The Shafi'i school analogizes to confession, arguing that just as a delayed confession still leads to hadd, so should delayed testimony. Understanding this dispute reveals deeper principles about the nature of rights of Allah versus rights of people, and the role of witness credibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
The disagreement between Hanafis and Shafi'is on whether pure Hudud are invalidated by delay in testimony.
Focus on the term 'pure Hudud' (حدود خالصة) which are rights of Allah, not involving any private claim.
2
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The Quranic verse 65:2 (وَأَقِيمُوا الشَّهَادَةَ لِلَّهِ) and the analysis of witness motives: either remaining silent for reward (then testifying out of enmity) or for concealment (then retracting, which is fault-finding).
Both motives lead to accusation or fisq, invalidating the testimony.
3
Understand the Shafi'i analogy
The Shafi'i school analogizes testimony to confession: if a delayed confession leads to hadd, why not delayed testimony?
This is a qiyas (analogy) based on the shared outcome (hadd).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis distinguish testimony from confession: testimony involves a third party with potential ulterior motives, while confession is against self-interest (no one is enemy to his own self).
Also, in zina there is no claimant (دعویٰ), while theft requires a claim, affecting the application of hadd.

یہاں وجود شبہ کا وہم پایا جاتا ہے ۔ یہاں وہم شبہ کو زیادہ سے زیادہ شبہ نشہ کا درجہ دیا جا سکتا ہے۔ جونس شبہ سے کم مرتبہ کا حامل ہے جو کہ غیر معتبر ہے۔ جب کہ چوری میں دعوئی شرط ہے۔ اس لئے سرقہ کے اقرار کے بعد رجوع سے حد سرقہ ( قطع ید ) ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ مگر دوسرے کے
Explanation: The principle is that Hudud that are pure rights of Allah are invalidated by delay, contrary to al-Shafi'i, who considers them (not invalidated). The case is: if a person delays in giving testimony related to those Hudud that fall purely under the rights of Allah, those (rights of Allah) become invalid despite the delay in testimony, because in rights of Allah, retracting from testimony after a confession is valid, and delay is a hindrance to acceptance of testimony. But Imam al-Shafi'i says that rights of Allah are not invalidated like rights of people, because in the hadd of zina, etc., if the perpetrator confesses voluntarily after delay, the hadd is carried out. Similarly, if the crime is proven by witnesses' testimony, the hadd will also be carried out. In response to Imam al-Shafi'i, our (Hanafi) argument is that in delaying testimony, the witness had one of two options: either he remained silent with the intention of reward, or he remained silent for concealment. So if it is for reward, after delay his willingness to testify is due to enmity and malice, so in that case he has turned to testimony due to accusation (imputation). If there is general permission for this... (a) The status of rights of Allah and Hudud becomes like play and amusement, which is not befitting for Allah. This situation leads to disrespect for Allah and His rights and limits. (b) Man is prone to error; a crime may occur. But in the given situation, self-interested people use it as a tool for personal gain due to rivalry, as in the present era, legal tactics are used to subdue opponents. All such actions fall under corruption of inner self (fasad al-batin). Therefore, due to the presence of fasad al-batin, retraction from testimony after delay is valid. If the reason for delay was concealment, then retraction in that case is based on sin (fisq), because finding fault in someone is a sin. So retracting from testimony due to delay (for concealment) is considered fault-finding, which is fisq, and a fasiq's testimony is not credible. Therefore, after delay in testimony, retraction from testimony due to fisq is not correct. The execution of hadd (which is a pure right of Allah) will become invalid, because Allah says: 'And establish the testimony for Allah.' So delay in testimony is a hindrance to its acceptance. Unlike confession, because no one is an enemy to his own self. So after confession, retraction from hadd of zina, wine, etc., is valid, because the hadd of zina, wine-drinking, and theft are pure rights of Allah. Therefore, after confession, the invalidity of rights of Allah becomes necessary. So Imam al-Shafi'i's analogy of rights of Allah to confession with regard to delay in testimony is questionable. If we consider the issue of retraction from testimony after delay, four matters come into existence: (1) delay, (2) testimony, (3) retraction, (4) confession. Delay means postponement in any matter, irrespective of whether the delay is due to fasad al-batin or concealment; in both cases, retraction from testimony after delay is not correct. Retraction from testimony is specific to the court of judgment, and if this retraction is in rights of Allah, then rights of Allah become invalid; if it is in rights of people, it will not be valid. If retraction causes loss to the plaintiff or defendant, the witnesses will be liable for compensation; otherwise not. Confession means saying 'yes', admitting. When a criminal admits a crime voluntarily, it is called confession. There are two ways to prove a crime: (a) by witnesses' testimony, (b) by the criminal's confession. If the crime is proven by witnesses' testimony, in that case the criminal's hidden denial exists, which is proven by witnesses' testimony. In confession, the criminal's hidden denial does not exist. Therefore, there is a clear difference between a crime proven by witnesses' testimony and a crime proven by the criminal's confession. So after delay in testimony, retraction from the testimony that was given to prove that crime is not correct, because the latter (retracted) statement contradicts the earlier one. So in this, retraction is related to fasad al-batin or concealment. So if it is fasad al-batin, the retracting witness becomes accused in his testimony; if it is concealment, he becomes a fasiq. So in both cases of accusation and fisq, retraction from testimony is not acceptable. If we consider the restrictions of the testimony itself, it becomes clear that the retraction after delay loses its status. So the presence of delay and retraction renders the testimony meaningless, whereas all judicial decisions depend on testimony. Thus, delay in testimony and retraction do not leave the importance of the testimony. Similarly, if we consider the reality of confession, it becomes clear from its nature that delay in testimony and retraction have no effect on the testimony itself. So analogizing the issue to confession is questionable. Because there is a difference between zina and theft: in zina, due to the absence of the female adulterer, there is no claim; since in zina a claim is not a condition, therefore after delay, the hadd will not be carried out like in confession. If it is doubted that despite the absence of the female adulterer, there is a possibility of claiming doubt from her side, then the remedy for this doubt is that probability does not necessitate the ruling of existence of doubt, which would cause the hadd to be dropped. Rather, here there is only a suspicion of doubt. Here, the suspicion of doubt can be given at most the level of doubt of intoxication, which has a lower rank than actual doubt and is not valid. While in theft, a claim is a condition. Therefore, after confession in theft, retraction causes the hadd of theft (cutting of hand) to be dropped, but for the other...
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This is a detailed commentary (تشريح) on the principle that pure Hudud are invalidated by delay, continuing the debate with Imam al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi argument is that when a witness delays testimony in a hadd case, he had two possible motives: (1) remaining silent for reward, meaning he did not want to be involved, but later comes forward due to enmity—thus his testimony is suspect; (2) remaining silent to conceal the sin, but later retracting—this is fault-finding (عیب جوئی) which is sinful (فسق), and the testimony of a fasiq is rejected. In both cases, the retraction after delay is invalid. The author then lists four elements: delay, testimony, retraction, and confession. Delay can be due to inner corruption or concealment, but in both cases retraction is invalid. Retraction in rights of Allah invalidates the hadd; in rights of people it does not, but may incur liability if loss occurs. The difference between testimony and confession is crucial: in testimony, the witness is an outsider and his retraction creates contradiction; in confession, the accused is admitting against himself, and no one is enemy to his own self, so retraction from confession is valid. The author criticizes Shafi'i's analogy between testimony and confession. Finally, a distinction is made between zina and theft: in zina, there is no claimant (دعویٰ) because the woman may not be present, so after delay, execution of hadd is not certain. In theft, there is a claimant (the owner), so retraction after confession nullifies the hadd. The passage provides a thorough analysis of the rules of retraction in Hudud cases, emphasizing the Hanafi position that delay in testimony creates suspicion, leading to invalidation of the hadd.

Key Terms
تاخیر (ta'kheer): Delay in giving testimony in a hadd case.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction from testimony after it has been given.
اقرار (iqrar): Confession of a crime by the accused.
فساد باطن (fasad al-batin): Inner corruption or malicious intent that disqualifies a witness.
دعویٰ (da'wa): Claim or allegation in a case.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in this passage, why is retraction from testimony after delay in Hudud not valid?
A) Because the witness is always lying.
B) Because the delay indicates the witness had a motive of reward or concealment, making his testimony suspect.
C) Because the hadd is already executed.
D) Because the qadi's judgment is final.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, delay in testimony in pure Hudud invalidates the hadd because it contradicts the Quranic command for prompt testimony and reveals suspect motives.

Conflicting Testimony in Zina: Rape vs Consent
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on contradictory testimony about rape vs consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on contradictory testimony in zina regarding rape and consent, and explain the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Contradictory testimony on consent vs force voids hadd for both per Abu Hanifa.

In a zina case, four witnesses must testify to the same act with consensus. What happens when two say the man raped the woman and two say she consented? This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, focusing on the legal reasoning that leads to different conclusions about who should receive the hadd punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting testimonies
Two witnesses claim rape (istikrāh), two claim consent (tawā'ah). Note that both groups agree the act of zina occurred, but disagree on the element of compulsion.
Zina requires four witnesses to the act itself; here the contradiction is on the nature of the act.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa rules that the hadd is averted from both the man and the woman because the witnesses contradict each other on the nature of the act – it cannot be both consensual and forced. Also, each set of witnesses becomes an accuser (tuhma) against the other.
Key reasoning: the act of zina is a single, unified event; its legal classification (consent vs force) is integral to the hadd.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani argue that the man should receive hadd because both groups agree he committed zina; the only disagreement is about the woman's state. The woman does not receive hadd due to the contradiction.
They see the testimony about the man's act as consistent – only the additional claim of force differs.
4
Analyse the proof (illat)
Abu Hanifa's proof: the contradiction directly prevents the proof of zina, as the witnesses' statements are mutually exclusive regarding the essential element of consent. Additionally, each group becomes a qādhif (slanderer) against the other, so their testimony is not reliable. The Sahibayn focus on the common agreement that the man performed the act.
The difference hinges on whether the testimony is seen as one whole (Abu Hanifa) or separable (Sahibayn).
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's: no hadd on either party. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is supported by the commentary with detailed proof.
Students should be able to cite which view is operative for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَ إِثْنَانِ أَنَّهُ زَنَى بِفُلَانَةٍ فَاسْتَكْرَهَهَا وَأَخَرَانِ أَنَّهَا طَاوَعَتْهُ دُرِئَ الْحَدُّ عَنْهُمَا جَمِيعًا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ ... الخ
If two testify that he committed zina with so-and-so and forced her, and two others that she consented, the hadd is averted from both of them according to Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute on testimony about zina where the witnesses disagree on whether there was consent or force. Abu Hanifa holds that the hadd for zina is dropped for both the man and the woman because the witnesses contradict each other on the nature of the act; zina is a single act that cannot be both consensual and forced. Additionally, both sets of witnesses become accusers (tuhma). Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that the man should receive hadd because both groups agree he committed zina; only the additional claim of force differs. The woman does not receive hadd because the witnesses differ regarding her. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view, as it appears in the text with his proof being the impossibility of combining consent and force in one act.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahāda): Testimony given in court; here, conflicting testimonies about the same act of zina
استكراه (istikrāh): Coercion or compulsion; here, the claim that the woman was forced
دُرِئَ (duri'a): Averted or warded off; used to describe the hadd punishment being dropped

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is Abu Hanifa's ruling when two witnesses say the man raped the woman and two say she consented?
A) The man receives hadd for zina, the woman is acquitted
B) Both man and woman receive hadd for zina
C) Neither man nor woman receives hadd for zina
D) Both sets of witnesses receive hadd for qadhf

Key Takeaway
Contradictory testimony on consent vs force in zina voids the proof of zina, so no hadd is applied to either party per the mufta bihi (Abu Hanifa).

Contradictory Location Testimony in Zina Cases
Ruling on contradictory testimony about the location of zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why hadd is not applied when testimony splits by location and state the Hanafi position on punishing witnesses, including the intra-madhhab disagreement with Zufar.

Core Idea
Place difference splits the act; each location lacks four witnesses, so no hadd.

When witnesses testify about zina but disagree on the location, the legal outcome changes. This lesson examines a classic scenario: two witnesses say Kufa, two say Basra. We will see why the hadd punishment is averted from both the accused and the witnesses, and how Imam Zufar differed. Understanding this ruling deepens your grasp of the testimonial requirements for hudud punishments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is zina. The ruling stated: the hadd punishment is averted from both the man and the woman, and the witnesses are not punished for qadhf.
This is the default Hanafi position.
2
Analyze the Proof: Why Hadd is Averted from Accused
Because testimony on zina requires four witnesses on the same act. Here, the place difference makes each act distinct: zina in Kufa vs. zina in Basra. Thus, for each location, only two witnesses are available, failing the nisab.
The act testified to differs with the place.
3
Analyze the Proof: Why Witnesses Are Not Punished
The witnesses are not punished because of shubhat al-ittihad – doubt that the testimonies refer to the same act. The unity of the woman and the form of zina creates a possibility that the act is one, so the witnesses are not liars.
Shubha averts hadd even from witnesses.
4
Note the Intra-Madhhab Ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar disagreed and held that the witnesses should receive hadd for qadhf (false accusation), because the place difference proves they cannot all be truthful.
The relied-upon (muftā bihi) position is that witnesses are not punished.
5
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: under Zufar's view, the witnesses would be flogged; under the majority Hanafi view, they are left unpunished.
This highlights how shubha protects witnesses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَ إِثْنَانِ أَنَّهُ زَنَى بِامْرَأَةٍ بِالْكُوفَةِ وَاخَرَانِ أَنَّهُ زَنَى بِهَا بِالْبَصْرَةِ دُرِئَ الْحَدُّ عَنْهُمَا لِأَنَّ الْمَشْهُودَ بِهِ فِعْلُ الزِّنَاءِ وَقَدِ اخْتَلَفَ بِاخْتِلَافِ الْمَكَانِ وَلَمْ يَتِمَّ عَلَى كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا نِصَابُ الشَّهَادَةِ وَلَا يُحَدُّ الشُّهُودُ خِلَافًا لِزُفَرَ لِشُبْهَةِ الِاتِّحَادِ نَظَرًا إِلَى اتِّحَادِ الصُّورَةِ وَالْمَرْأَةِ
And if two testify that he committed zina with a woman in Kufa, and two others that he committed zina with her in Basra, the hadd is averted from both of them because the act testified to differs with the difference of place and the nisab of testimony is not completed for each one, and the witnesses are not punished, contrary to Zufar, due to the shubha of unity considering the unity of form and woman.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This ruling addresses a scenario where two witnesses say zina occurred in Kufa, and two say in Basra, presumably at the same time. Since the place differs, the act itself is considered different—zina in Kufa is a different event from zina in Basra. Therefore, for each location, only two witnesses are available, which is insufficient for hadd. The man and woman are not punished. The witnesses are also not given hadd for false testimony because there is a shubha (doubt) that the act might be unified—the same woman and same physical act—even though the location differs. Imam Zufar disagrees and would punish the witnesses, but the relied-upon position is that they are not punished.

Key Terms
نصاب الشهادة (niṣāb al-shahāda): The required number of witnesses (4 for zina)
شبهة الاتحاد (shubhat al-ittiḥād): Doubt that the two testimonies refer to the same act despite place difference

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the hadd is not applied when two witnesses say zina in Kufa and two say in Basra?
A) The witnesses are lying
B) The act of zina differs with the place, so each location lacks the required four witnesses
C) The woman cannot be punished if she is unmarried
D) The man confessed to only one act

Key Takeaway
Contradictory testimony on the location of zina splits the act, preventing hadd on the accused; additionally, shubha protects the witnesses from punishment.

Istihsan Overrides Qiyas: Reconciling Testimony on a Single Act
Ruling on contradictory testimony about corners of the same house

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of istihsan to reconcile seemingly contradictory testimonies in hudud cases.

Core Idea
Istihsan reconciles testimonies when reconciliation is possible, overriding qiyas.

In hudud cases, the strict requirement of unanimity in testimony can be relaxed by istihsan if the differences are reconcilable. This lesson explores a classic example: four witnesses testify in pairs about zina in different corners of the same house. By qiyas, the difference in place voids the testimony, but by istihsan, the act could have begun in one corner and ended in another, so the testimonies are accepted and hadd is applied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
When witnesses testify about the same act but differ on the precise location (e.g., corner of a house), does the difference invalidate the testimony?
This is a case of apparent contradiction.
2
Apply qiyas (analogy)
By analogy to cases where the locations are truly distinct (e.g., Kufa vs Basra), the difference in corner could be treated as a difference in place, thus weakening the testimony.
Qiyas would lead to no hadd.
3
Consider istihsan (juristic preference)
Istihsan asks whether the testimonies can be reconciled. Here, the act of zina might have started in one corner and ended in another, or observers might have differed due to angle.
Reconciliation is possible, so the testimonies are accepted.
4
Derive the ruling
Since istihsan overrides qiyas, the hadd punishment is applied to both the man and woman.
This is the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنِ اخْتَلَفُوا فِي بَيْتٍ وَاحِدٍ حُدَّ الرَّجُلُ وَالْمَرْأَةُ مَعْنَاهُ أَنْ يَشْهَدَ كُلُّ اثْنَيْنِ عَلَى الزِّنَاءِ فِي زَاوِيَةٍ وَهَذَا اسْتِحْسَانٌ وَالْقِيَاسُ أَنْ لَا يُحَدَّ لِاخْتِلَافِ الْمَكَانِ حَقِيقَةً وَجْهُ الِاسْتِحْسَانِ أَنَّ التَّوْفِيقَ مُمْكِنٌ بِأَنْ يَكُونَ ابْتِدَاءُ الْفِعْلِ فِي زَاوِيَةٍ وَالِانْتِهَاءُ فِي زَاوِيَةٍ أُخْرَى
And if they disagree within one house, the man and woman are punished. Its meaning is that each pair testifies to zina in a corner. This is istihsan, and qiyas is that they should not be punished due to actual difference of place. The face of istihsan is that reconciliation is possible: the beginning of the act might have been in one corner and the ending in another corner.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This ruling distinguishes between a real difference in place (like Kufa vs Basra) and a difference within the same room. If two witnesses say zina occurred in one corner and two say in another corner of the same house, by qiyas (analogy) no hadd should apply because the place is different. However, by istihsan (juristic preference), hadd is applied because it is possible that the act started in one corner and ended in another due to movement, or that observers misjudged the location. Since reconciliation is possible, the testimony is not considered contradictory, and the full nisab is achieved for a single act. This is the Hanafi position: istihsan overrides qiyas here.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference based on accommodating possibility of reconciliation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does istihsan allow hadd when witnesses differ on the corner of the same house?
A) Because the witnesses are all truthful
B) Because the act could have moved from one corner to another, making the testimonies reconcilable
C) Because the house is considered one location overall
D) Because qiyas also supports applying hadd

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, istihsan can override qiyas to reconcile seemingly contradictory testimonies if reconciliation is possible, ensuring that hudud punishments are not avoided on technicalities.
