Two Sets of Four Witnesses: Hadd Averted Due to Ta'āruḍ al-Bayyināt
Ruling on eight witnesses testifying to zina in two different places at the same time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling of ta'āruḍ al-bayyināt (conflicting proofs) in hudud cases to determine that hadd is averted when two equally valid sets of witnesses contradict each other on a material fact.

Core Idea
When two full sets of four witnesses contradict on same time different places, certainty of lying by one group averts hadd from all.

In hudud cases, the testimony of four upright male eyewitnesses is normally sufficient to establish zina and apply the hadd. But what happens when two complete sets of four witnesses each testify to the same act at the same time but in different, distant places? The Hanafi school addresses this rare but instructive scenario, demonstrating that certainty (yaqīn) is the bedrock of hudud, and any unresolved contradiction that negates the required level of certainty protects both the accused and the witnesses from punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two testimonies
Two groups of four witnesses each testify that the same man and woman committed zina. Both groups state the same time (sunrise), but one group places the act in Nukhayla and the other in Dayr Hind.
The places are far apart, making simultaneous occurrence impossible.
2
Recognise the contradiction (ta'āruḍ)
Since the same time and two distant locations are given, the man cannot have been in both places. Therefore, one group must be lying – but we do not know which.
This is a clear case of ta'āruḍ al-bayyināt – conflicting proofs of equal weight.
3
Apply the principle of certainty in hudud
Hudud require absolute certainty (yaqīn) for punishment. Here, we are certain that one group is false, but we cannot identify which one. Thus, the required certainty for applying hadd is absent.
The famous principle: 'Avert hadd with doubts' (dar' al-hudūd bi al-shubuhāt).
4
Derive the ruling for the accused
Both the man and the woman cannot be punished because their guilt is not established with certainty. The existence of a possible false accusation from one group creates a shubha (doubt) that blocks the hadd.
Even though eight witnesses total, the contradiction nullifies the proof.
5
Derive the ruling for the witnesses
The witnesses themselves are not punished because each group could be telling the truth from their own perspective – they might have been mistaken about the time or place, or there is a remote possibility of a miracle. Since there is a possibility of truth for each, they are protected from hadd for false testimony (qadhf).
Punishing them would require certainty that they lied, which is absent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَ أَرْبَعَةٌ أَنَّهُ زَنَى بِامْرَأَةٍ بِالنُّخَيْلَةِ عِنْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ وَأَرْبَعَةٌ أَنَّهُ زَنَى بِهَا عِنْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ بِدَيْرِ هِنْدٍ دُرِئَ الْحَدُّ عَنْهُمْ جَمِيعًا أَمَّا عَنْهُمَا فَلِأَنَّا نَتَيَقَّنُ بِكَذِبِ أَحَدِ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ مِنْ غَيْرِ عَيْنٍ وَأَمَّا عَنِ الشُّهُودِ فَلِاحْتِمَالِ صِدْقِ كُلِّ فَرِيقٍ
And if four testify that he committed zina with a woman in Nukhayla at sunrise, and four that he committed zina with her at sunrise in Dayr Hind, the hadd is averted from all of them. As for the two (the man and woman), because we are certain that one of the two groups is lying without identification; as for the witnesses, because of the possibility of truth of each group.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This scenario involves two complete sets of four witnesses each, but they testify to zina in different places at the same time. Since a man cannot be in two distant places simultaneously, one group must be lying. However, we cannot determine which group is lying. Therefore, hadd cannot be applied to the accused because punishment requires certainty, and here there is certainty that someone is lying, but not who. The witnesses themselves are not punished because each group might be telling the truth from their perspective (they may have been mistaken about the location or time, or there might be a valid possibility of the act occurring in both places if the times were different, but here the same time creates impossibility). The ruling protects against punishing an innocent person.

Key Terms
تعارض البينات (ta'āruḍ al-bayyināt): Conflict of proofs; here two sets of four witnesses contradict each other
درء الحدود بالشبهات (dar' al-hudūd bi al-shubuhāt): Avert hadd punishments by doubts

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in the passage, why are the two sets of witnesses not punished for false testimony (qadhf) when their testimonies conflict?
A) Because they are all truthful.
B) Because each group may be truthful from their perspective, so there is a possibility of truth.
C) Because the judge cannot determine which set is lying.
D) Because the accused confessed.

Key Takeaway
When two complete sets of four witnesses contradict each other in a manner that makes the act impossible, the hadd is averted from all – both accused and witnesses – because certainty of the crime is destroyed.

Zina Testimony Against a Virgin Woman
Ruling when four witnesses testify against a virgin woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when four witnesses testify against a woman who is a virgin and explain the role of physical evidence in creating doubt (shubha) to avert the hadd penalty.

Core Idea
Virginity creates doubt that averts the hadd penalty for zina.

This lesson examines a unique scenario where four witnesses accuse a woman of zina, but her physical state—virginity—contradicts the accusation. The Hanafi ruling shows that hadd is averted from all parties because the claim is physically impossible. This demonstrates the powerful principle that doubt (shubha) prevents punishment in Islamic criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage to understand the facts: four male witnesses testify against a woman for zina, but the woman is a virgin (hymen intact).
2
State the ruling
The hadd penalty is dropped from both the man and the woman, and also from the witnesses. No one is punished.
3
Analyze the proof (talil)
The reasoning is that zina requires penetration, which breaks the hymen. Since the woman is a virgin, the act could not have occurred, creating doubt (shubha). Women inspectors are called to confirm virginity, and their testimony is accepted to drop hadd but not to impose it.
This is a logical proof (talil) based on physical impossibility.
4
Apply the principle of shubha
The principle that 'hadd is averted by doubts' (al-hudud tudra'u bish-shubah) operates here. The physical evidence creates a strong doubt that overrides the testimony of four apparently credible witnesses.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah)
The witnesses are not punished for qadhf (false accusation) because they may have been mistaken; the persistent virginity suggests they could not have seen full penetration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَ أَرْبَعَةٌ عَلَى امْرَأَةٍ بِالزِّنَاءِ وَهِيَ بِكْرٌ دُرِئَ الْحَدُّ عَنْهُمَا وَعَنْهُمْ لِأَنَّ الزِّنَاءَ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ مَعَ بَقَاءِ الْبَكَارَةِ وَمَعْنَى الْمَسْأَلَةِ أَنَّ النِّسَاءَ نَظَرْنَ إِلَيْهَا فَقُلْنَ إِنَّهَا بِكْرٌ وَشَهَادَتُهُنَّ حُجَّةٌ فِي إِسْقَاطِ الْحَدِّ وَلَيْسَتْ حُجَّةً فِي إِيجَابِهِ فَلِهَذَا سَقَطَ الْحَدُّ عَنْهَا وَلَا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِمْ
And if four testify against a woman for zina while she is a virgin, the hadd is averted from both (man and woman) and from them (the witnesses) because zina cannot be verified with the virginity intact. The meaning of the issue is that women examined her and said she is a virgin, and their testimony is proof for dropping the hadd but not proof for imposing it. For this reason hadd is dropped from her, and it is not obligatory upon them.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This ruling involves a woman who is accused of zina by four witnesses, but she is still a virgin. Women inspectors confirm her virginity. Since zina would break the hymen, virginity contradicts the claim of zina. The testimony of the women is accepted to drop the hadd because it is a form of evidence that creates doubt (shubha), but it is not sufficient to impose hadd on anyone. The man and woman are not punished, and the witnesses are not punished because they may have been mistaken—the hymen could be intact if the act did not involve full penetration or if the woman was previously a virgin but restored, but here the inspection shows virginity. This illustrates the principle that doubt (shubha) averts punishment.

Key Terms
بكر (bikr): A woman whose hymen is intact, i.e., she has not had sexual intercourse

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for dropping hadd when four witnesses testify against a woman who is still a virgin?
A) The witnesses are lying
B) Zina cannot be verified with virginity intact, creating doubt
C) The woman confessed to something else
D) The man is unknown

Key Takeaway
Virginity after four witnesses creates a shubha that averts hadd from all parties.

Conflicting Testimonies on Zina Location: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Ruling on conflicting testimonies about zina location within one house

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that istihsan overrides qiyas in conflicting testimonies about the location of zina, and state that hadd is wajib on both parties.

Core Idea
When four witnesses disagree on the exact corner but agree on the same house, hadd is still applied by istihsan.

This passage tackles a classic problem: four eyewitnesses to zina all agree it happened inside the same room, but they disagree on which corner. The apparent contradiction threatens to undermine the testimony. The Hanafi school resolves this through istihsan (juridical preference) rather than strict qiyas, preserving the hadd punishment. Understanding this ruling reveals how Hanafi usul balances textual requirements with practical possibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the passage and determine the final hukm: what happens to the man and woman when witnesses differ on the corner?
The ruling is that both are punished with hadd.
2
Contrast with qiyas
The text states that qiyas would lead to dropping the hadd. Understand why: any material contradiction (here, place) creates doubt (shubha) which bars the hadd in normal circumstances.
Qiyas: if witnesses disagree on a necessary detail, their testimony becomes unreliable.
3
Analyze the istihsan reasoning
The author provides two possible reconciliations: (a) the act began in one corner and moved to another; (b) different witnesses had different vantage points. Both show that the testimonies can be true simultaneously.
Istihsan prefers a result that upholds the objective of the law (deterrence) over a mechanical application of doubt.
4
Extract the epistemological weight
Note that this ruling is from zahir al-riwayah and is the mufta bihi position. Istihsan here is a valid source of law in the Hanafi school, overriding qiyas.
Authority: zahir_riwayah; cross-madhhab status: mukhtalaf fih (some schools may require unanimity).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الشهادة على الزناء والرجوع عنها
ابْتِدَاءُ الْفِعْلِ فِى زَاوِيَةٍ وَالْاِنْتِهَاءُ فِي زَاوِيَةٍ أُخْرَى بِالْاِضْطِرَابِ اَوْلَادَّ الْوَاقِعَ فِي وَسَطِ الْبَيْتِ فَيَحْسِبُهُ مَنْ فِي الْمُقَدَّمِ فِى الْمُقَدَّمِ وَمَنْ فِى الْمُؤَخَّرِ فِى الْمُؤَخَّرِ فَيَشْهَدُ بِحَسْبِ مَا عِنْدَهُ.
ترجمہ: اور اگر گواہوں نے ان دونوں کے ایک کمرہ میں (ہونے کے باوجود) جگہ کے بارے میں ایسا ہی اختلاف کیا تو اس مرد اور عورت دونوں کو حد لگائی جائے گی۔ اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ دو گواہوں نے اس ایک کو نہ میں اور دوسرے دو نے دوسرے کو نہ میں زنا کرنے کی گواہی دی ہو۔ یہ حکم استحسان کے طور پر ہے اور قیاس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ انہیں حد نہیں لگائی جائے۔ کیونکہ حقیقت جگہ میں اختلاف ہے اور استحسان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دونوں باتوں کا ہونا ممکن ہے۔ اس طرح ہے کہ اس کام کی ابتداء ایک حصہ میں شروع ہوئی ہو۔ لیکن بعد میں کسی الجھن سے جگہ بدل کر دوسرے کو نہ میں چلے گئے ہوں۔ یا اس طرح سے کہ واقعہ تو کمرہ کے پچھلے حصہ میں ہوا ہو لیکن اس کمرہ کے اگلے حصہ میں رہنے والے نے یہ خیال کیا ہو کہ یہ بھی اگلے حصہ میں ہیں اور دوسروں نے پچھلے حصہ میں ان کے پچھلے حصہ میں ہونے کا خیال کیا ہو۔ پھر اپنے اپنے خیال کے مطابق ان لوگوں نے گواہی دی ہو۔
Chapter on testimony for zina and withdrawal from it. The beginning of the act in a corner and the ending in another corner due to agitation, or the event occurring in the middle of the house: the one in the front thinks it was in the front, the one in the back thinks it was in the back, so each testifies according to what he perceives. Translation: If the witnesses differed about a single room in this way, both the man and the woman are to be punished with hadd. The meaning is that two witnesses testified that the zina occurred in one corner and the other two in another corner. This ruling is by istihsan. Qiyas requires that they not be punished because there is a real disagreement about the place. The proof of istihsan is that both scenarios are possible. It could be that the act began in one corner but due to agitation they moved to another, or that the event occurred in the back of the room but those in the front thought it was in the front and those in the back thought it was in the back, and each testified according to his perception.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding conflicting testimonies about the location of zina within a single house. The passage opens with a ruling: if two witnesses say the act began in one corner and ended in another, or if there is confusion about the exact spot, the hadd punishment is applied to both the man and the woman. This is based on istihsan (juridical preference), not qiyas. Under qiyas, the hadd would be dropped because the witnesses disagree on the location, creating doubt. However, istihsan considers the possibility that both accounts could be true: the act may have started in one corner and moved to another. Alternatively, the witnesses may have perceived the location based on their vantage points. The Hanafi school adopts istihsan here to uphold the punishment despite apparent contradiction.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juridical preference that overrides qiyas due to a more suitable outcome.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning that would drop the hadd due to contradiction in testimonies.
حد (hadd): The fixed corporal punishment for zina (flogging or stoning).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two witnesses say zina occurred in the front corner and two say it occurred in the back corner of the same room, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) Hadd is not applied because of the contradiction.
B) Hadd is applied to both the man and the woman due to istihsan.
C) The witnesses are punished for qadhf.
D) Only the man is punished.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, istihsan overrides qiyas when conflicting witness testimonies on location can be reconciled, preserving the hadd punishment.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

Conflicting Testimonies in Hudud: Dropping the Penalty
Ruling when two sets of four witnesses testify for different locations and times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two conflicting sets of four witnesses testify for zina and explain the rationale based on the principle of Dar' al-Hudud.

Core Idea
When two sets of four witnesses give contradictory testimonies, the hudud penalty is dropped from all parties due to unresolved certainty.

This lesson examines a case where two complete sets of four credible witnesses testify that the same couple committed zina at the same time but in different locations. The Hanafi school rules that no hadd punishment is applied to the accused or the witnesses. Understanding this ruling reveals the high standard of certainty required for hudud punishments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Note that there are two groups of four witnesses each, both testifying to zina by the same couple at the same time but in different places.
The contradiction makes it impossible for both testimonies to be true simultaneously.
2
State the ruling
The Hanafi ruling is that no hadd is applied to the accused man, the accused woman, or any of the witnesses.
3
Trace the dalil 'aqli for the accused
Since one group must be lying (the couple cannot be in two places at once), but it is unknown which group, the certainty required for hadd is absent. Thus, the penalty is dropped from the couple due to unresolved doubt.
This applies the principle of Dar' al-Hudud (avert hudud punishments with doubts).
4
Trace the dalil 'aqli for the witnesses
The witnesses are not punished because each group could be truthful (e.g., they may have mistaken the location). There is a possibility of truth, so certainty of falsehood (required for qadhf) is lacking.
5
Consider the cross-madhhab position
Some other schools might punish the witnesses for qadhf since the contradiction implies one group is falsely accusing. However, the Hanafi school prioritizes the possibility of truth over probability of lying.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether witnesses are punished; Hanafi drops all hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَ ارْبَعَةٌ أَنَّهُ زَنَى بِإِمْرَأَةِ بِالْنُّخَيْلَةِ عِنْدَطُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ وَارْبَعَةٌ إِنَّهُ زَنَى بِهَا عِنْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ بِدَيْرَهِندَ. دَرِنَى اَلْحَدُّ عَنْهُمْ جَمِيعًا اَمَّا عَنْهُمَا فِلانًا تيقنا بِكِذَبِ اَحَدِ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ مِنْ غَيْرِ عَيْنٍ وَأَمَّا عَنِ الشُّهُودِ فَلِاحْتِمَالِ صِدْقٍ كُلّ فَرِيقٍ.
ترجمہ: اور اگر چار آدمیوں نے اس بات کی گواہی دی کہ مرد نے فلاں عورت سے موضع نخیلہ (کوفہ کے قریب ایک جگہ) میں طلوع آفتاب کے وقت زنا کیا ہے اور دوسرے چار گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ اس نے اس عورت کے ساتھ موضع دیر ہند میں زنا کیا ہے۔ تو ان دونوں مرد و عورت کے علاوہ کسی گواہ پر بھی حد نہیں جاری کی جائے گی۔ ان میں سے مرد اور عورت پر اس لئے حد جاری نہیں ہوگی کہ ان دونوں فریق کے ہر فریق میں بغیر کسی تعین کے یہ احتمال بھی رہتا ہے کہ وہ جھوٹا ہے۔ اس طرح گواہوں کے دونوں فریق سے اس لئے حد ختم ہوگئی کہ ہر فریق میں بغیر کسی تعین کے اس کے سچے ہونے کا بھی احتمال رہتا ہے۔
And if four testify that he committed zina with a woman in Nukhaylah at sunrise, and another four testify that he committed zina with her at sunrise in Dayr Hind, then the hadd is dropped from all of them. As for the two (man and woman), because it is certain that one of the two groups is lying, without specification. As for the witnesses, because there is a possibility that each group is truthful. Translation: If four men testify that the man committed zina with a certain woman in Nukhaylah near Kufa at sunrise, and another four witnesses testify that he committed zina with her in Dayr Hind at sunrise, then hadd is not executed on the man, the woman, or any witness. The hadd is dropped from the man and woman because it is certain that one of the two groups is lying, but not specified which. The hadd is dropped from the witnesses because there is a possibility that each group is truthful.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage addresses a case where two separate sets of four credible witnesses testify to zina, but with contradictory times or places. The ruling is that no hadd is applied to the accused (man and woman) nor to the witnesses. The reasoning is that it is logically impossible for both testimonies to be true simultaneously (the same couple cannot be in two places at the same time), so one group must be lying. However, since it is unknown which group is lying, the hadd is dropped from the accused to avoid punishing based on potential falsehood. The witnesses are not punished for qadhf because there is a possibility that each group is truthful (they may have honestly mistaken the location or time). This ruling reflects Hanafi caution in hudud punishments, where certainty is required.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahadah): Testimony of four adult male Muslim witnesses required for proving zina.
حد (hadd): The fixed punishment for zina (100 lashes for unmarried, stoning for married).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two groups of four witnesses each testify that the same couple committed zina at the same time but in two different cities. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The couple is punished based on the first group's testimony.
B) Both groups of witnesses are punished for qadhf.
C) No hadd is applied to the couple or the witnesses.
D) The couple is stoned.

Key Takeaway
When conflicting testimonies create uncertainty in hudud cases, the penalty is dropped entirely.

Testimony Against a Virgin Woman: Hadd Dropped Due to Physical Impossibility
Ruling when four witnesses testify against a woman found to be a virgin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when four witnesses testify against a virgin woman and explain why hadd is dropped from all parties.

Core Idea
Virginity is physical proof that zina did not occur, so hadd is lifted from everyone.

This lesson examines a unique scenario in Hanafi hudud law: four men testify against a woman for zina, but a physical examination by women confirms she is still a virgin. The ruling is that the hadd punishment is dropped from both the accused man and woman, and the witnesses are not punished for qadhf. The underlying reasoning relies on a rational proof (dalil 'aqli) and the specific rule that women's testimony is accepted for dropping hadd but not for establishing it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is testimony of four male witnesses accusing a woman of zina. The woman is examined and found to be a virgin (bikr). The ruling: hadd is dropped from the accused man, the accused woman, and the witnesses.
The ruling is not about punishment but about dropping it.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is rational (dalil 'aqli). The preservation of virginity is a physical indicator that contradicts the occurrence of zina. Zina, by definition, involves penetration which would break the hymen.
This is a definitive proof (qati' al-dalalah).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The logical link: since zina cannot be confirmed with an intact hymen, the hadd punishment cannot be established. The physical fact overrides the testimony.
Women's testimony regarding virginity is accepted as proof for dropping hadd.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may not accept women's testimony for virginity in such cases, but the Hanafi school does for dropping the hadd. This is a valid ikhtilaf within the broader madhhab framework.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The ruling given is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah. It relies on the principle that women's testimony is authoritative for matters not usually seen by men.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَ اَرْبَعَةٌ عَلَى امْرَأَةِ بِالزِّنَاءِ وَهِيَ بِكُرِّ دُرِى الْحَدُّ عَنْهُمَا وَ عَنْهُمْ لِاَنَّ الزِنَاءَ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ مَعَ بَقَاءِ الْبَكَارَةِ وَمَعْنَى الْمَسْأَلَةِ أَنَّ النِّسَاءَ نَظَرْنَ إِلَيْهَا فَقُلْنَ إِنَّهَا بِكُرْ وَشَهَادَتْهُنَّ حُجَّةٌ فِي إِسْقَاطِ الْحَدِّ وَلَيْسَ بِجُحَّةٍ فِي إِيجَابِهِ فَلِهَذَا سَقَطَ الْحَدُّ عَنْهَا وَلَا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِمْ.
ترجمہ: اور اگر چار آدمیوں نے کسی عورت پر زنا کرنے کی گواہی دی، حالانکہ گواہی کے وقت وہ باکرہ ہے، تو عورت اور مرد اور تمام گواہوں سے بھی حد ختم ہوگی (نہیں لگائی جائے گی) کیونکہ پردہ بکارت کے رہتے ہوئے زنا ثابت نہیں ہوسکتا ہے۔ اس مسئلہ کی تحقیقی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ عورتوں نے اس کی شرم گاہ دیکھ کر کہا کہ وہ اب تک باکرہ ہے اور ان عورتوں کی گواہی ساقط کرنے میں تو حجت ہوتی ہے لیکن کسی پر حد جاری کرنے کی صورت میں ان کی گواہی حجت نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس عورت اور مرد سے حد ساقط ہوگئی اور گواہوں پر حد قذف جاری نہیں ہوئی۔
And if four testify against a woman for zina while she is a virgin, the hadd is averted from both (the man and woman) and from them (the witnesses) because zina cannot be confirmed with the preservation of virginity. The meaning of the issue is that women examined her and said she is a virgin. Their testimony is proof for dropping the hadd but not proof for establishing it. Therefore the hadd is dropped from her and it is not obligatory upon them (the witnesses). Translation: If four men testify against a woman for zina while she is a virgin at the time of testimony, then the hadd is lifted from the woman, the man, and all the witnesses because zina cannot be established while the hymen is intact. The reality of the issue is that women looked at her private parts and said she is still a virgin. Their testimony is authoritative (hujjah) for dropping the hadd, but not for establishing it. So the hadd is dropped from her and the man, and the witnesses are not punished for qadhf.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage deals with a situation where four male witnesses accuse a woman of zina, but it is discovered through physical examination by women that she is still a virgin (bikr). The ruling is that the hadd punishment is dropped from the accused man and woman, and the witnesses are not punished for qadhf (false accusation). The reason is that virginity is physically incompatible with zina; penetration would break the hymen. Women's testimony regarding virginity is accepted for dropping the hadd (as a defense) but not for establishing hadd (since women cannot testify for zina according to Hanafi school). Thus, the hadd falls due to the certainty that zina could not have occurred, and the witnesses are not punished because their testimony may have been a mistake, not deliberate falsehood.

Key Terms
بكر (bikr): A virgin woman whose hymen is intact.
شهادة النساء (shahadat al-nisa): Women's testimony; accepted for matters not usually seen by men, like virginity examination.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The man is stoned, the woman is flogged.
B) The witnesses are flogged for qadhf.
C) Hadd is dropped from the man, woman, and witnesses.
D) The woman is flogged but the man is freed.

Key Takeaway
When physical evidence contradicts testimony, hadd is dropped; women's testimony is accepted for defense but not for conviction.

Testimony by Blind, Qadhf-Punished, or Slave Witnesses
Ruling when witnesses are not qualified due to blindness, past qadhf, or slavery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when disqualified witnesses testify for zina and explain the Hanafi reasoning that their testimony becomes qadhf.

Core Idea
Invalid witnesses become slanderers — the accused goes free, the accusers are flogged.

This passage deals with the qualification of witnesses for zina testimony. Hanafi law requires that witnesses be competent and that their testimony directly establish the act. If witnesses are blind, have been punished for qadhf, or are slaves, their testimony is void. Consequently, their accusation becomes qadhf (false accusation) and they themselves face the fixed punishment, while the accused is released. The ruling is derived from a rational proof: if such witnesses cannot even establish a property right, a fortiori they cannot establish hadd, which demands a higher standard of proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is four disqualified witnesses testifying for zina. The ruling: the witnesses are punished with hadd for qadhf (80 lashes) and the accused is not punished.
The accused must demand punishment for qadhf to be applied, as per the text.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a priori reasoning (dalil 'aqli): the text states that their testimony cannot even establish a property claim, so it cannot establish hadd, which requires a stricter standard.
This is a qiyas awla (a fortiori) argument.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The reasoning proceeds from the lesser (mal) to the greater (hadd). If the witnesses are not qualified to testify for property, they are certainly not qualified for hudud, which demand even more rigorous proof.
The key is that hudud are established only by testimony that meets strict conditions: free, morally upright, sighted witnesses.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: the accused is protected from false accusation, while the false accusers are punished. This upholds the high evidentiary standard for zina and deters false testimony.
Some other schools might accept blind testimony if the witness heard the act, but Hanafi insists on visual observation for zina.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَارْبَعَةٌ عَلَى رَجُلٍ بِالزِّنَاءِ وَهُمْ عُمْيَانٌ أَوْ مَحْدُودُونَ فِي قَذَفٍ أَوْ أَحَدُهُمْ عَبْدًا وَمَحْدُودٌ فِي قَذَفٍ فَإِنَّهُمْ يُحَدُّونَ وَلَا يُحَدُّ الْمَشْهُودُ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَثْبُتُ بِشَهَادَتِهِمُ الْمَالُ فَكَيْفَ يَثْبُتُ الْحَدُّوَهُمْ لَيْسُوا مِنْ أَهْلِ آدَاءِ الشَّهَادَةِ وَالْعَبْدُ لَيْسَ بِأَهْلِ لِلتَّحَمُلِ وَالْآدَاءِ فَلَمْ يَثْبُتْ شُبْهَةُ الزِّنَاءِ لَانَّ الزِّنَاءَ يَثْبُتُ بِالْآدَاءِ.
ترجمہ: اور اگر چار آدمیوں نے کسی شخص کے خلاف زنا کرنے کی گواہی دی مگر وہ سب اندھے تھے یا ایسے تھے جن پر پہلے ہی حد قذف (تہمت کی حد) لگائی جاچکی ہے یا ان میں سے ایک بھی غلام ہو یا اس پر حد قذف لگائی جاچکی ہو تو تمام گواہوں پر حد لگائی جائے گی (بشرطیکہ جس پر زنا کی گواہی دی ہے وہ خود بھی دعویٰ کرے) لیکن جن پر الزام لگایا گیا ہے ان پر حد نہیں لگائی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ یہ تو ایسے ناقص گواہ ہیں کہ ان کی گواہی سے مال بھی ثابت نہیں ہوتا ہے تو حد کس طرح ثابت ہوگی اور غلام گواہ بنے اور ادا کرنے کے لائق نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے زنا کا شبہ بھی ثابت نہ ہوا۔ کیونکہ گواہی دینے کے بعد زنا ثابت ہوتا ہے اس کے بغیر نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ (ف) اور یہ بات معلوم ہو چکی ہے کہ ان میں سے کسی کو بھی گواہی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے ان کا کہنا گواہی دینا تو نہیں ہوا بلکہ الزام لگانا ہوا اسی لئے الزام اور تہمت لگانے کی حد میں ان میں سے ہر ایک کو ۸۰ کوڑے مارے جائیں گے۔
And if four testify against a man for zina while they are blind, or have been punished for qadhf, or one of them is a slave and has been punished for qadhf, then they are punished (with hadd for qadhf) and the accused is not punished. Because wealth is not established by their testimony, so how can hadd be established? They are not from the people qualified to give testimony. The slave is not qualified to bear or give testimony. Therefore, no suspicion of zina is established because zina is established by (valid) testimony. Translation: If four men testify against someone for zina but all are blind, or have previously been flogged for qadhf, or one of them is a slave or has been flogged for qadhf, then all the witnesses are punished (provided the accused demands it). But the accused is not punished. Because such deficient witnesses cannot even establish a property claim, so how can they establish hadd? A slave is not qualified to bear or give testimony. Therefore, no presumption of zina is established because zina is established through valid testimony. Since it is known that none of these are allowed to testify, their statement is not testimony but rather an accusation. Therefore, each is flogged 80 lashes for qadhf.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where four men testify against a man for zina, but the witnesses suffer from disqualifications: they are blind, have been previously punished for qadhf (false accusation), or are slaves. The Hanafi ruling is that these witnesses are punished with the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes), while the accused is not punished. The reasoning is that such individuals are not qualified to testify (shahadah) at all. Their testimony cannot even establish a property right, so a fortiori it cannot establish hadd, which requires a higher standard of proof. Since they are incompetent witnesses, their statement is not considered testimony but rather an accusation (qadhf), and they are subject to the fixed punishment for false accusation. Note that the text specifies that the accused must demand the punishment for the hadd of qadhf to be applied.

Key Terms
أعمى (a'ma): A blind person; not qualified to testify for zina because visual observation is required.
محدود في القذف (mahdud fi al-qadhf): A person who has been punished for false accusation of zina; their testimony is rejected permanently.
عبد ('abd): A slave; not qualified to testify in hudud cases because of incomplete legal capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The accused is flogged for zina if the judge believes the witnesses.
B) The witnesses are flogged for qadhf, and the accused is freed.
C) The case is dismissed and no one is punished.
D) The witnesses are imprisoned until they regain sight.

Key Takeaway
Disqualified witnesses in zina cases turn the accusation into qadhf, resulting in their own punishment and the accused's freedom.

Testimony by Fasiq Witnesses: Hadd Averted by Competing Suspicions
Ruling when witnesses are fasiq at the time of testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school drops both zina and qadhf hadd when fasiq witnesses testify, and apply the principle of shubhah to similar cases.

Core Idea
Fisq creates a shubhah that cancels the shubhah of zina, so both hadd are dropped.

The testimony of open sinners (fasiq) in hudud cases presents a unique legal puzzle. The Hanafi school balances two competing suspicions: the testimony itself suggests zina, but the moral deficiency of the witnesses casts doubt on its truth. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind dropping both the hadd for zina and the hadd for qadhf (false accusation), and explores the enforceability of a judge's verdict based on such testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal ruling
Determine what the passage rules when four fasiq witnesses testify to zina. Note that no hadd is applied either to the accused (for zina) or to the witnesses (for qadhf).
The ruling is clear: both punishments are averted.
2
Analyze the rational proof (dalil 'aqli)
The passage uses rational reasoning: a fasiq is unreliable, creating a deficiency in testimony. This deficiency generates a suspicion (shubhah) that the zina did not occur. Since hadd is averted by any doubt, the hadd for zina is dropped. Additionally, the witnesses are not punished for qadhf because their testimony, though flawed, still raised a suspicion of zina.
Two competing shubhahs: one for zina (from the testimony) and one against (from fisq).
3
Note the nuance on judge's verdict
If a judge accepts the fasiq's testimony and rules based on it, that verdict is enforceable (nāfidh) in the Hanafi school. The ruling on hadd is separate from the validity of the judgment.
This shows the distinction between evidentiary admissibility and the triggering of punishment.
4
Contrast with other schools
Recognize that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) generally reject fasiq testimony entirely. The Hanafi position is unique in allowing enforcement while still averting the hadd.
This is a mukhtalaf fih issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدُوا بِذَالِكَ وَهُمْ فُسَّاقَ اَوْظَهَرَ انَّهُمْ فُسَّاقَ لَمْ يُحَدُّوالتَّ الْفَاسِقَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْآدَاءِ وَالتَّحَمُلِ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي آدَائِهِ نَوْعُ قُصُورٍ لِتُهُمَةِ الْفِسْقِ وَلِهَذَا لَوْ قَضَى الْقَاضِي بِشَهَادَةِ فَاسِقٍ يَنْفُذُ عِنْدَنَا فَيَثْبُتُ بِشَهَادَتِهِمْ شُبْهَةً الزِّنَاءِ وَبِاعْتِبَارِ قُصُورٍ فِي الْآدَاءِ لِتُهُمَةِ الْفِسْقِ يَثْبُتُ شُبْهَةُ عَدَمِ الزِّنَاءِ فَلِهَذَا امْتَنَعَ الْحَدَّانِ وَسَيَأْتِي فِيْهِ.
ترجمہ: اور اگر انہوں نے اس طرح گواہی دی اور وہ فاسق ہوں یا ان کے فاسق ہونے کا پتہ چلے تو حد جاری نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ فاسق (گناہگار) ادائے شہادت اور تحمل کے اہل نہیں ہوتا۔ اگرچہ اس کی ادائیگی میں فسق کی تہمت کی وجہ سے ایک قسم کی کمی ہے۔ اسی لئے اگر قاضی کسی فاسق کی گواہی سے فیصلہ کرے تو ہمارے نزدیک وہ نافذ ہوتا ہے۔ تو ان کی گواہی سے زنا کا شبہ ثابت ہوتا ہے اور اداء میں کمی (فسق کی وجہ سے) کے اعتبار سے عدم زنا کا شبہ ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں حدیں (زنا اور قذف) ساقط ہوگئیں اور اس کی تفصیل آئے گی۔
And if they testify about that while they are fasiq (open sinners), or it becomes apparent that they are fasiq, then they are not punished (with hadd). Because the fasiq is not among the people qualified to give or bear testimony. Even though in his testimony there is a kind of deficiency due to the suspicion of fisq. Therefore, if a judge passes judgment based on the testimony of a fasiq, it is enforceable in our school. So by their testimony, the suspicion of zina is established, and by considering the deficiency in testimony due to suspicion of fisq, the suspicion of non-zina is established. Therefore, both hadd (for zina and for qadhf) are prevented. Its detail will come later. Translation: And if they testify thus while they are fasiq, or it becomes clear that they are fasiq, then hadd is not applied. Because the fasiq is not qualified to give or bear testimony. There is a deficiency in his testimony due to the suspicion of sin. For this reason, if a judge passes a verdict based on a fasiq's testimony, it is enforceable in our school. So through their testimony, a suspicion of zina is established, and due to the deficiency (the suspicion of fisq), a suspicion of non-zina is established. Therefore, both hadd (for zina on the accused and for qadhf on the witnesses) are prevented. Details will follow.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of witness sinfulness (fisq) on zina testimony. The ruling: if the witnesses are fasiq (open sinners, e.g., known for lying or immorality) at the time of testimony, then no hadd is applied – neither on the accused for zina nor on the witnesses for qadhf. The reasoning is delicate: a fasiq is not a qualified witness for bearing or giving testimony due to the suspicion of untruthfulness. However, if a judge did accept such testimony and passed a verdict, that verdict would be enforceable (i.e., not overturned) according to the Hanafi school. The key point is that the testimony of fasiq witnesses creates two competing suspicions: (1) a suspicion that zina occurred (because they testified), and (2) a suspicion that it did not occur (because of their moral deficiency). Since hadd is averted by any doubt (shubhah), both punishments are dropped. The text notes that further detail will come later, indicating that this is a nuanced topic.

Key Terms
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, rendering them unreliable in testimony.
شبهة (shubhah): A doubt or ambiguity that averts hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The accused is stoned.
B) The witnesses are flogged for qadhf.
C) No hadd is applied to the accused or the witnesses.
D) The accused is flogged but the witnesses are freed.

Key Takeaway
Fisiq of witnesses creates a shubhah that cancels the shubhah of zina, so both hadd punishments are dropped, but the judge's verdict remains enforceable.

Hadd Averted by Virginity: The Case of Four Witnesses
Ruling on four witnesses and a virgin woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when four witnesses testify against a virgin woman for zina and explain why shubha averts hadd from both the accused and the witnesses.

Core Idea
Virginity creates shubha that drops hadd and protects both the accused and the witnesses.

The Hanafi school places great weight on shubha (doubt) in hudud cases. This short but important passage illustrates how the physical evidence of virginity, established by female witnesses, creates a doubt that completely averts the fixed penalty of zina. Not only are the man and woman spared, but the four male witnesses are also not punished for qadhf, because their testimony is not disproven—only suspended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the testimony of four qualified male witnesses against a woman for zina. The ruling is that if the woman is a virgin (proven by female witnesses), the hadd is averted from both the man and the woman, and the witnesses are not punished.
Focus on the outcome: no one receives hadd.
2
Understand the condition: virginity
The key condition (shart) for this ruling is that the woman is proven to be a virgin through the testimony of female witnesses. Her virginity contradicts the claim of zina, creating a doubt.
Virginity here is a physical state that can be established by women's testimony, which is accepted in this specific context.
3
Apply the principle: shubha averts hadd
The Hanafi legal maxim holds that hudud penalties are averted by doubts (al-hudud tudra'u bi al-shubuhat). The virginity evidence creates a shubha in the prosecution, making the hadd inapplicable.
This principle is from the Prophet ﷺ: 'Avert hudud by doubts.'
4
Note the consequence for the witnesses
The four male witnesses are not punished for qadhf (false accusation) because their testimony was not proven false; it was only rendered doubtful by the women's testimony. The doubt protects them as well.
If their testimony were clearly false, they would receive the hadd of qadhf. But here, the doubt prevents that.
5
Memorize the ruling as a memorization anchor
This ruling is a key example of how shubha operates in Hanafi fiqh. Commit it to memory: four witnesses + virginity = no hadd for anyone.
Remember: the condition is virginity proven by women's testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَ ارْبَعَةٌ عَلَى امْرَأَةِ بِالزِّنَاءِ وَهِيَ بِكَرْدُرِى الْحَدُّ عَنْهُمَا وَ عَنْهُمْ
And if four testify against a woman for zina, and she is a virgin, the hadd is averted from both of them and from them.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This is a Hanafi ruling statement on the effect of the woman being a virgin when four witnesses testify against her for zina. The presence of women's testimony that she is a virgin creates doubt (shubha) that prevents the hadd of zina from being imposed on both the man and the woman. Furthermore, the four male witnesses are not punished for qadhf because their testimony is not proven false by the women's testimony; rather, the women's testimony only prevents hadd. The ruling is based on the principle that hadd is averted by doubts (shubuhat).

Key Terms
حد (hadd): The fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Shariah for certain crimes, here for zina.
بكر (bikr): A virgin woman who has never had sexual intercourse.
شبهة (shubha): A doubt that prevents the application of hadd penalties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Both the man and woman are freed from hadd, and the male witnesses are not punished.
C) Only the woman receives hadd, the man is punished for false accusation.
D) The male witnesses are punished for qadhf, and the woman is freed.

Key Takeaway
Virginity proven by female testimony creates a doubt that averts hadd from all parties in a zina case with four witnesses.

Blind and Disqualified Witnesses in Zina Cases
Ruling on incompetent witnesses in zina cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi law punishes witnesses who are blind, previously punished for qadhf, or slaves for false accusation (qadhf) and why the accused is not punished, and apply the qiyas reasoning to similar cases.

Core Idea
Incompetent witnesses do not merely fail to prove zina; they become accusers liable for hadd.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a critical scenario: four witnesses come forward but suffer from legal incapacities. The Hanafi school rules that such witnesses are themselves punished for false accusation (qadhf), while the accused walks free. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling and the conditions for witness competence in hadd cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of incompetent witnesses
List the three types mentioned: blind persons (无法直接见证), those previously punished for qadhf (失去道德可信度), and slaves (缺乏作证资格). Note the common thread: they are not from 'ahl al-ada' (people capable of delivering testimony).
The slave is mentioned in combination with being punished, but the text implies slaves alone are also disqualified.
2
Determine the legal effect of their testimony
Analyze the text: their testimony does not even establish wealth (mal), so how could it establish hadd? This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) from lesser to greater.
Wealth is easier to prove than hadd, so if testimony fails for wealth, it certainly fails for hadd.
3
Apply the qiyas reasoning
Formalize the analogy: Asl (original case) = testimony regarding property; Hukm = invalid if witnesses are incompetent; Far' (new case) = testimony for zina; Illa (effective cause) = witnesses are not from ahl al-ada. Conclude: the accused is not punished.
The witnesses themselves become accusers without proper standing, so they are punished for qadhf.
4
State the final ruling
The witnesses are punished with the hadd for qadhf (80 lashes) at the demand of the accused; the accused is not punished and is innocent.
This is mufta bihi from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَارْبَعَةٌ عَلَى رَجُلٍ بِالزِّنَاءِ وَهُمْ عُمْيَانٌ أَوْ مَحْدُودُونَ فِي قَدَفٍ أَوْ أَحَدُهُمْ عَبْدًا وَمَحْدُودٌ فِي قَذَفٍ فَإِنَّهُمْ يُحَدُّونَ وَلَا يُحَدُّ الْمَشْهُودُ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَنبُتُ بِشَهَادَتِهِمُ الْمَالُ فَكَيْفَ يَبْتُ الْحَدُّوَهُمْ لَيَسُوا مِنْ أَهْلِ آدَاءِ الشَّهَادَةِ وَالْعَبْدُ لَيْسَ بِأَهْلِ لِلتَّحَمُلِ وَالْآدَاءِ فَلَمْ يَثْبُتْ شُبُهَةُ الزِّنَاءِ لَانَّ الزِّنَاءَ يَثْبُتُ بِالْآدَاءِ
And if four testify against a man for zina, while they are blind, or have been punished for qadhf, or one of them is a slave and has been punished for qadhf, then they are punished (for qadhf), and the one testified against is not punished, because wealth is not established by their testimony, so how could hadd be established? And they are not from the people capable of giving testimony, and the slave is not capable of bearing and giving testimony, so even the suspicion of zina is not established, because zina is established by (proper) testimony.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This is a Hanafi ruling statement with proof. The passage addresses witnesses who are inherently incompetent: blind persons (who cannot see the act), those previously punished for false accusation (qadhf) which disqualifies them from future testimony, and slaves (who are not qualified to bear testimony). Their testimony has no legal effect because it does not even establish property rights (which is easier to prove), so it certainly cannot establish a hadd punishment. The reasoning is based on analogy (qiyas): since their testimony is invalid for lesser claims, it is even more invalid for hadd. Therefore, the accused is free, and the witnesses are each punished for qadhf (false accusation) at the demand of the accused.

Key Terms
عميان (umyan): Blind persons; unable to directly witness the act of zina.
محدود في القذف (mahdud fi al-qadhf): A person who has been punished for false accusation of zina, thus disqualified from future testimony.
أهل الأداء (ahl al-ada'): People legally capable of delivering testimony in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The accused is punished, and the witnesses are punished for qadhf.
C) The accused is not punished, and the witnesses are punished for qadhf.
D) Both the accused and witnesses are punished.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, incompetent witnesses in zina cases are themselves punished for false accusation, and the accused is acquitted.

The Effect of Testimony by Fasiq Witnesses in Hudud Cases
Ruling on four fasiq witnesses and Hanafi-Shafi'i difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school drops both hadd punishments when fasiq witnesses testify in a zina case, and contrast this with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Fasiq witnesses create two conflicting suspicions (shubha), so both hadd of zina and hadd of qadhf are dropped.

This lesson explores a unique Hanafi ruling: when four fasiq (sinful) witnesses testify against someone for zina, neither the accused nor the witnesses are punished. This outcome hinges on the Hanafi view that a fasiq retains partial legal capacity to testify, creating a 'shubha' (doubt) that averts the hadd punishments. We will also examine the Shafi'i counterargument and the practical consequences of the disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the consequence for both the accused (zina hadd) and the witnesses (qadhf hadd) when fasiq witnesses testify.
The ruling is that no one is punished.
2
Identify the basis: fasiq as ahl al-ada' wa al-tahammul
Understand that Hanafis consider a fasiq partially qualified for testimony, unlike complete disqualification.
This partial qualification creates a legal effect.
3
Trace the two conflicting doubts
Testimony from a fasiq creates both a suspicion of zina (because they are qualified to testify) and a suspicion of non-zina (because their sinfulness undermines credibility).
These two shubhas conflict.
4
Apply the principle: shubha averts hadd
Because hadd punishments are averted by any doubt, both hadds are dropped entirely.
This is a core Hanafi maxim in hudud.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i considers a fasiq completely unqualified, like a slave, so testimony is void and witnesses are punished for qadhf.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدُوا بِذَالِكَ وَهُمْ فُسَّاقَ اَوْظَهَرَ انَّهُمْ فُسَّاقَ لَمْ يُحَدُّوالَاتَ الْفَاسِقَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْآدَاءِ وَالتَّحَمُلِ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي آدَائِهِ نَوْعُ قُصُورٍ لِتُهُمَةِ الْفِسْقِ وَلِهَذَا لَوْ قَضَى الْقَاضِي بِشَهادَةِ فَاسِقٍ يَنْفُذُ عِنْدَنَا فَيَثْبُتُ بِشَهَادَتِهِمْ شُبُهَةً الزِّنَاءِ وَبِاعْتِبَارِ قُصُورٍ فِي الْآدَاءِ لِتُهُمَةِ الْفِسْقِ يَثْبُتُ شُبْهَةُ عَدَمِ الزِّنَاءِ فَلِهَذَا امْتَنَعَ الْحَدَّانِ وَسَيَأْتِي فِيْهِ خِلافُ الشَّافِعِي بِنَاءً عَلَى أَصْلِهِ أَنَّ الْفَاسِقَ لَيْسَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الشَّهَادَةِ فَهُوَ كَالْعَبْدِ عِنْدَهُ
And if they testify to that while they are fasiqs, or it becomes apparent that they are fasiqs, they are not punished (for qadhf), because the fasiq is among the people capable of giving and bearing testimony, although there is a type of deficiency in his testimony due to suspicion of fisq. Therefore, if the judge passes judgment based on the testimony of a fasiq, it is enforceable in our school. So by their testimony, the suspicion of zina is established, and by considering the deficiency in testimony due to fisq, the suspicion of non-zina is established. Therefore, both hadds are prevented. And the difference of al-Shafi'i will come, based on his principle that the fasiq is not among the people of testimony, so he is like a slave in his view.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This is a Hanafi ruling with an inter-madhhab dispute. According to the Hanafi school, a fasiq (sinful person) is still legally capable of testifying; fisq does not entirely remove his qualification (ahliyyat al-ada'), though it introduces a defect (ta'hiyya). Therefore, if four fasiq witnesses testify, their testimony creates two conflicting doubts: (1) the possibility that zina occurred (since they are qualified to testify), and (2) the possibility that it did not (due to their sinfulness affecting credibility). Because hadd punishments are averted by doubts, both the hadd of zina for the accused and the hadd of qadhf for the witnesses are dropped. Furthermore, if a judge rules based on such testimony, his ruling is enforceable (nafidh) according to Hanafis. This contrasts with Imam al-Shafi'i, who considers a fasiq completely unqualified for testimony, treating him like a slave; thus in his school, such witnesses would be punished for qadhf. The practical consequence (thamarat al-khilaf) is that in Hanafi fiqh, a fasiq's testimony can have effect, while in Shafi'i it is void.

Key Terms
فاسق (fasiq): A Muslim who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, lacking full probity ('adalah).
شبهة (shubha): A legal doubt that averts hadd punishments.
أهل الأداء والتحمل (ahl al-ada' wa al-tahammul): Qualified for both bearing and delivering testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the result when four fasiq witnesses testify against someone for zina?
A) The accused is punished for zina, and the witnesses are punished for qadhf.
B) The accused is punished, and the witnesses are not punished.
C) The accused is not punished, and the witnesses are not punished.
D) The accused is not punished, but the witnesses are punished for qadhf.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, testimony by fasiq witnesses creates conflicting suspicions that avert both the hadd of zina and the hadd of qadhf, based on the principle that shubha averts hudud.

Testimony by Less Than Four Witnesses
Ruling when witnesses number less than four

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when witnesses for zina number fewer than four and explain the legal consequence of qadhf.

Core Idea
Less than four witnesses in zina makes the witnesses accusers, each punishable by the hadd of qadhf.

This lesson clarifies a fundamental Hudud rule: the strict requirement of four witnesses in zina cases. If the number falls short, the testimony is not simply invalid – it transforms into a false accusation, triggering the hadd penalty on the witnesses themselves. The source passage from Al-Hidayah states this rule concisely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Note that the ruling applies when the number of witnesses for zina is less than four. The condition is a numerical deficiency.
2
State the consequence
Each witness receives the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes). They are not considered witnesses but accusers.
3
Understand the rationale
The deficiency in number means the testimony has no legal weight; the act is treated as a false accusation (qadhf).
Imam al-Hidayah states: 'since there is no consideration of testimony at deficiency of number'.
4
Memorize the rule
This is a fixed rule with no exceptions: any number below four incurs the hadd on the witnesses.
This is a memorization anchor for the Hanafi hudud system.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ نَقَصَ عَدَدُ الشُّهُودِ عَنْ أَرْبَعَةٍ حُدُّوالِأَنَّهُمْ قَذَفَةٌ إِذْلَا حَسَبَةَ عِنْدَ نُقْصَانِ الْعَدَدِ وَخُرُوجُ الشَّهَادَةِ عَنِ لْقَذَفَ بِاعْتِبَارِهَا
And if the number of witnesses is less than four, they are punished (for qadhf) because they are accusers (qadhafa), since there is no (legal) consideration (of testimony) at the deficiency of number, and the testimony exits from (being) qadhf by virtue of it.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This is a clear Hanafi ruling: when the number of witnesses for zina is less than four, they cannot be considered witnesses for zina; instead, they become accusers (qadhafa). Therefore, each of them is punished with the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes). The reason is that the minimum number required for a valid zina testimony is four. With fewer, the testimony is legally ineffective for proving zina, and the accusers are treated as having made a false accusation. This ruling applies even if they claim to be testifying.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina, punishable by 80 lashes.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given in court, here specifically for zina.
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law, e.g., 80 lashes for qadhf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens when three men testify against someone for zina?
A) The case is dismissed with no punishment.
B) The three men are each given 80 lashes for qadhf.
C) The accused is given a reduced sentence.
D) The three men are called to produce a fourth witness or be punished.

Key Takeaway
In zina, the number of witnesses must be exactly four; any fewer, and the witnesses become liable to the hadd of qadhf.

Discovery of Defect After Hadd Execution
Ruling when a witness is discovered defective after hadd execution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a witness is discovered defective after hadd execution and explain the reasoning using the principle of effective witness count.

Core Idea
A defective witness retroactively reduces the count, making the testimony a false accusation.

This lesson addresses a delicate scenario in hudud: what happens if, after the hadd penalty has been carried out, it comes to light that one of the four witnesses to zina was actually disqualified (e.g., a slave or someone previously punished for qadhf)? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling that protects the integrity of the legal process while ensuring justice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the initial valid testimony
Four witnesses testify against a man for zina. Their testimony is accepted as valid, and the accused is flogged (hadd). At this point, all conditions for witnesses are assumed to be met.
The hadd is executed based on four valid witnesses.
2
Identify the discovered defect
Later, one of the four witnesses is found to be either a slave or a person who had been flogged for qadhf (false accusation) previously. Both are permanently disqualified from giving testimony in Hanafi law.
A slave's testimony is not accepted except in certain cases; a mahdud is forever barred as per Q. 24:4.
3
Apply the consequence: effective witness count
Since one witness is invalid, the remaining valid witnesses are three. Three witnesses are insufficient to prove zina, so the original testimony is treated as a false accusation.
The minimum for zina is four valid witnesses (Quran 24:13).
4
Determine the ruling for the witnesses
Because the testimony is now deemed false, all four witnesses (including the defective one) are liable for the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes). The defective witness is punished as part of the group.
The executed hadd on the accused is not reversed; it stands.
5
Distinguish from possible misconceptions
Some might think the accused's flogging should be reversed, but the ruling focuses only on punishing the witnesses. The limit of hadd is not overturned due to post-execution discovery.
This is consistent with Hanafi principle that a validly executed hadd is not rescinded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَ أَرْبَعَةٌ عَلى رَجُلٍ بِالزِّنَاءِ فَضُرِبَ بِشَهَادَتِهِمْ ثُمَّ وُجِدَ اَحَدُهُمْ عَبْدًا أَوْ مَحْدُودًا فِي قَذَفٍ فَإِنَّهُمْ يُحَدُّونَ لِأَنَّهُمْ قَذَفَةٌ إِذِ الشُّهُودُ ثَلَثَةٌ
And if four testify against a man for zina, and he is flogged on their testimony, then one of them is found to be a slave or one who has been punished for qadhf, then they are all punished (for qadhf) because they are accusers, since the witnesses (now effectively) are three.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This ruling addresses a scenario where zina witnesses are initially accepted by the court and the hadd is carried out, but later it is discovered that one of the four witnesses was not qualified (e.g., a slave or previously punished for qadhf). The discovery retroactively reduces the effective number of valid witnesses to three. Since three is insufficient to prove zina, the original testimony is treated as a false accusation. Consequently, all four witnesses (including the defective one) are now punishable for qadhf. Note: the hadd already executed on the accused stands (it is not reversed), but the witnesses incur the hadd of qadhf for their false accusation.

Key Terms
محدود في القذف (mahdud fi al-qadhf): One who has been flogged for false accusation, permanently disqualified from testifying.
شهود (shuhud): Witnesses; in this context, the four witnesses for zina.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina; punishable by 80 lashes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Four witnesses testify, the accused is flogged, then it is discovered that one witness is a slave. What happens?
A) The flogging is reversed, and the witnesses are punished.
B) The flogging stands, and the witnesses are punished for qadhf.
C) The flogging stands, and the witnesses are not punished.
D) The flogging is reversed, and the witnesses are not punished.

Key Takeaway
A defective witness discovered after hadd execution retroactively reduces the witness count, making the testimony a false accusation and punishing all witnesses.

Testimony of Fasiq Witnesses in Zina and the Effect of Shubha
Ruling on fasiq witnesses and the effect of shubha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony of fasiq witnesses in zina and explain the effect of shubha on hudud.

Core Idea
Four fasiq witnesses create doubt: neither accused nor witnesses face hadd.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced scenario: what if the witnesses testifying to zina are themselves fasiq (corrupt)? The ruling hinges on the Hanafi principle that hudud are warded off by doubts (al-hudud tudra'u bi al-shubahat). Even a deficient witness creates enough legal doubt to suspend the fixed penalties for both the accused and the witnesses, provided the required number of four is met. However, if the number falls short, the witnesses become slanderers and are liable for hadd qadhf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Four witnesses testify to zina, but they are fasiq (either known at the time or discovered later).
Fasiq means one who commits major sins or persists in minor sins.
2
Determine the Ruling for the Witnesses
If four fasiq witnesses, they are not punished with hadd qadhf. If fewer than four, they are punished as slanderers.
The number four is critical because it is the minimum for zina testimony.
3
Determine the Ruling for the Accused
Due to the deficiency (fisq) of the witnesses, doubt (shubha) arises, so no hadd is applied to the accused man and woman.
Hudud are suspended by any doubt.
4
Apply the Principle of Shubha
The fasiq still has capacity for testimony, but his fisq creates uncertainty. This doubt prevents the punishment.
Hanafi: even a defective witness can create shubha.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i Position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a fasiq is entirely disqualified (like a slave), so his testimony is invalid and produces no doubt.
Under Shafi'i, the accused would not be punished because no valid testimony exists, but the witnesses could be liable for qadhf if they falsely accused.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خِلَافُ الشَّافِعِي بِنَاءً عَلَى أَصْلِهِ أَنَّ الْفَاسِقَ لَيْسَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الشَّهَادَةِ فَهُوَ كَالْعَبْدِ عِنْدَهُ

ترجمہ: اور اگر گواہوں نے زنا کی گواہی دی حالانکہ وہ فاسق ہوں یا گواہی دینے کے بعد معلوم ہوا کہ وہ فاسق ہیں تو ان کو حد قذف نہیں لگائی جائے گی کیونکہ ان میں فسیق ہونے کی وجہ سے اگر چہ ان میں عیب ضرور ہے پھر بھی گواہ بنے اور گواہی دینے کی ان میں صلاحیت موجود ہے۔ اس لئے اگر فاسق کی گواہی پر قاضی نے حد لگانے کا حکم دے دیا تو ہمارے نزدیک وہ واجب العمل ہوگا۔ اور فاسق کی گواہی سے زنا کا شبہ بھی ہو جائے گا اور چونکہ فسق کا عیب رہتے ہوئے گواہی دینے میں کچھ کمی بھی ہے۔ اس لئے یہ بھی شبہ پیدا ہو گا کہ اس نے جس کے خلاف گواہی دی ہے اس نے زنا نہیں کیا ہو۔ اس لئے ان دونوں مرد و عورت پر حد واجب نہیں ہوگی۔ اس مسئلہ میں امام شافعی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کا اختلاف ہے جو عنقریب بیان کیا جائے گا اور اختلاف کی اصل یہ ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک فاسق شخص گواہی کے لائق نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ یہ ان کے نزدیک ایک فاسق غلام کے حکم میں ہوتا ہے۔

تشریح: وَإِنْ شَهِدُوا بِذَلِكَ وَهُمْ فُسَّاقٌ أَوْ ظَهَرَ أَنَّهُمْ فُسَّاقٌ لَمْ يُحَدُّوا لِأَنَّ الْفَاسِقَ لَيْسَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الشَّهَادَةِ فَهُوَ كَالْعَبْدِ عِنْدَهُ

تعداد شہود چار سے کم ہو تو بقیہ کو حد لگائی جائے گی:

وَإِنْ نَقَصَ عَدَدُ الشُّهُودِ عَنْ أَرْبَعَةٍ حُدُّوا لِأَنَّهُمْ قَذَفَةٌ إِذْ لَا حَسَبَةَ عِنْدَ نُقْصَانِ الْعَدَدِ وَخُرُوجُ الشَّهَادَةِ عَنِ الْقَذَفِ بِاعْتِبَارِهَا

رجمہ: اور اگر گواہوں کی تعداد چار سے کم ہو تو سب کو حد قذف ماری جائے گی کیونکہ یہ سب تہمت لگانے والے ہوئے۔ کیونکہ ان گواہوں کی تعداد کم ہونے کی وجہ سے شرعی ثواب کے لئے گواہی نہیں ہو سکتی ہے اور اس گواہی کا بہتان لگانے سے خارج ہونا (گواہی کو بہتان نہ کہنا)، اسی بناء پر ہے کہ گواہی بھی ایک شرعی کام ہے۔
Contrary to al-Shafi'i based on his principle that the fasiq is not from the people of testimony, so he is like a slave according to him.

Translation: And if witnesses testify to that while they are fasiq, or it becomes apparent that they are fasiq, they are not punished with hadd qadhf because despite the defect of fisq in them, they still become witnesses and have capacity for testimony. Therefore, if the judge gives the ruling of hadd based on the testimony of the fasiq, in our view it is effective and valid. And the testimony of the fasiq creates doubt about zina, and because there is deficiency due to fisq, doubt also arises that the accused may not have committed zina. Thus, hadd is not obligatory on the man and woman. In this issue, Imam al-Shafi'i has a dispute which will be mentioned soon, and the basis of the dispute is that in his view, the fasiq is not fit for testimony; he is like a slave according to him.

Explanation: And if they testify to that while they are fasiq, or it becomes apparent that they are fasiq, they are not punished because the fasiq is not from the people of testimony, so he is like a slave according to him.

If the number of witnesses is less than four, the rest are punished:

And if the number of witnesses is less than four, they are punished because they are slanderers, since there is no [؟] consideration when the number is deficient, and the testimony exits from [being] slander by consideration.

Summary: And if the number of witnesses is less than four, all are punished with hadd qadhf because they are slanderers. Because due to the deficiency in number, the testimony cannot be for religious reward, and the exit of this testimony from slander is based on the fact that testimony is a religious act.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on the testimony of fasiq (corrupt) witnesses in a case of zina. The matn states: If four witnesses testify to zina while they are fasiq, or it later becomes known they were fasiq, they are not punished with hadd qadhf (the penalty for false accusation of zina). The reason given is that the fasiq, despite his flaw, still possesses legal capacity for testimony, so his testimony creates doubt (shubha) sufficient to prevent the hadd penalty on the accused. However, if the number of witnesses is less than four, all of them are punished for qadhf because they have failed to provide the required number, thereby becoming slanderers.

This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school. A note mentions the disagreement of Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that a fasiq is entirely disqualified from testimony, like a slave, and thus his testimony is inadmissible. The commentary makes clear that the Hanafi position relies on the concept that even a deficient witness creates enough doubt to avoid the harsh fixed penalties (hudud). The passage also emphasizes that the judge's enforcement of hadd based on such testimony is valid (wajib al-'amal).

Key Terms
فاسق (fāsiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, but his testimony is accepted in Hanafi law with deficiency.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina, punishable by eighty lashes (hadd).
شبهة (shubhah): Legal doubt that prevents application of hadd penalties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if four fasiq witnesses testify to zina?
A) They are all punished with hadd qadhf
B) They are not punished, and the accused is also not punished
C) Only the accused is punished
D) The witnesses are punished but not the accused

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats fasiq witnesses as deficient but not disqualified; their testimony creates a doubt that prevents hudud when the required number of four is met.

Ruling When a Witness is Disqualified After Hadd is Carried Out
Ruling on witness disqualification after hadd execution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a witness in a zina case is later found to be a slave or previously punished for qadhf, and explain why all four witnesses are punished.

Core Idea
If after carrying out hadd, one witness is found incompetent, all four become slanderers and are punished.

In Hudud cases, the testimony of four upright witnesses is required. But what happens if a witness is later found to be a slave or previously punished for qadhf? This passage from al-Hidayah gives the ruling: all four are punished. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Four witnesses testify to zina, the accused is flogged based on their testimony, then one witness is discovered to be a slave or a person previously punished for qadhf (false accusation).
2
Determine the effective number of valid witnesses
Since the slave or one punished for qadhf is not a valid witness in hudud, the effective witnesses are reduced to three.
Slaves and mahdud fi qadhf are disqualified in Hanafi law.
3
Apply the rule for insufficient witnesses
Three witnesses are insufficient to prove zina; without four, the testimony becomes slander (qadhf) retroactively.
Qur'an 24:4 requires four witnesses; less than four makes the accusers liable for qadhf.
4
Conclude the ruling
All four witnesses are now considered slanderers and receive the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes).
The text says 'they are slanderers' (qadhaftun) because the witnesses are three.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چار گواہوں نے زنا کی گواہی دی اور زانی کو حد لگائی گئی پھر گواہوں میں سے کوئی غلام یا محدود فی القذف تھا تو حد لگائی جائے گی:

وَإِنْ شَهِدَ أَرْبَعَةٌ عَلَى رَجُلٍ بِالزِّنَاءِ فَضُرِبَ بِشَهَادَتِهِمْ ثُمَّ وُجِدَ أَحَدُهُمْ عَبْدًا أَوْ مَحْدُودًا فِي قَذَفٍ فَإِنَّهُمْ يُحَدُّونَ لِأَنَّهُمْ قَذَفَةٌ إِذِ الشُّهُودُ ثَلَاثَةٌ

ترجمہ: اور اگر چار آدمیوں نے کسی پر زنا کی گواہی دی اور ان کی گواہی کی وجہ سے اس مرد کو حد لگائی گئی۔ بعد میں یہ معلوم ہوا کہ ان چار میں سے ایک غلام ہے یا کسی پر تہمت لگانے کی بناء پر حد لگائی جا چکی ہے تو ان سب کو حد لگائی جائے گی اور گواہوں کی تعداد تین ہی رہ جانے کی وجہ سے یہ سب بہتان لگانے والے ہو گئے۔

تشريح: ..... وَإِنْ شَهِدَ أَرْبَعَةٌ عَلَى رَجُلٍ بِالزِّنَاءِ فَضُرِبَ بِشَهَادَتِهِمْ ثُمَّ وُجِدَ أَحَدُهُم الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
Four witnesses testified to zina against a man, and the hadd was carried out due to their testimony. Then one of them was found to be a slave or one who had been punished for qadhf—then all are punished with hadd because they are slanderers, since the witnesses are [only] three.

Translation: And if four men testify against someone for zina, and due to their testimony that man is punished with hadd, then later it is discovered that one of the four is a slave or has already been punished for slander (qadhf), then all of them are punished with hadd because due to the reduction in number of witnesses to three, they all become slanderers.

Explanation: ... And if four testify against a man for zina, and he is flogged due to their testimony, then one of them is found to be a slave or one punished for qadhf, then they are all punished because they are slanderers, since the witnesses are three. The meaning is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents a scenario: Four witnesses testify to zina, and based on their testimony, the accused is flogged (the hadd of zina is carried out). Subsequently, it is discovered that one of the witnesses is either a slave (whose testimony is not accepted in hadd cases) or a person who has previously been convicted of qadhf (false accusation, hence his testimony is inadmissible). In such a case, the effective number of valid witnesses is reduced to three, which is insufficient for the proof of zina. Therefore, all four original witnesses become guilty of qadhf (false accusation) and are themselves punished with the hadd of eighty lashes. The reasoning is that the deficiency in the number of qualified witnesses retroactively renders their testimony slander, as the required four are not met.

Key Terms
محدود في قذف (maḥdūd fī qadhf): A person who has already been punished for false accusation of zina (qadhf); his testimony is no longer accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where four witnesses testify to zina and the accused is flogged, then one witness is found to be a slave, what is the ruling on the witnesses?
A) Only the slave witness is punished for qadhf
B) All four witnesses are punished for qadhf
C) None are punished because the hadd was already carried out
D) Only the accused is retried

Key Takeaway
When a witness is later found incompetent after hadd execution, all four witnesses become guilty of qadhf and are punished.

Liability for Injury or Death from Flogging in Hadd Zina and Retraction of Witnesses
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for flogging harm and witness retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for arsh and diyah when flogging in hadd zina causes injury or death, and apply the ruling to scenarios of witness retraction.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: No compensation for flogging harm in hadd; Sahibayn: Treasury or witnesses pay. The key is the nature of prescribed jald.

This passage presents a sharp intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. At stake is whether compensation (arsh or diyah) is due when the flogging punishment for zina causes injury or death, and whether retracting witnesses bear liability. Understanding the reasoning behind each position illuminates the Hanafi school's method of distinguishing between the prescribed punishment and incidental harm.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi (Abu Hanifa) position
Identify what Abu Hanifa rules regarding liability for flogging harm and stoning, and his position on witness retraction.
Note the distinction: flogging harm — no liability; stoning death — treasury liable.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's opposing view
State that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that treasury is liable for flogging harm and witnesses are liable if they retract.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
Trace their reasoning: the obligatory flogging is absolute and wounding cannot be avoided, so the harm is attributed to the testimony; thus retraction triggers witness liability, and without retraction, the act is attributed to the judge as a public functionary, so treasury pays.
They analogize to stoning and qisas.
4
Analyse Abu Hanifa's response
Understand Abu Hanifa's counter-argument: the prescribed hadd is jald — a painful but non-wounding and non-lethal striking. Any wounding is due to the striker's lack of skill, not the testimony itself. Moreover, imposing liability would deter people from establishing hudud.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) based on the definition of jald and public policy.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Identify the practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, no compensation for flogging injury; under Sahibayn, compensation from treasury or witnesses. The text states 'al-sahih' that no liability is required, indicating Abu Hanifa's view is relied upon.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position to avoid deterrence.
