وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلَا عَلَى بَيْتِ الْمَالِ أَرْشُ الضَّرْبِ وَإِنْ رُجِمَ فَدِيَتُهُ عَلَى بَيْتِ الْمَالِ وَهَذَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا أَرْشُ الضَّرْبِ أَيْضًا عَلَى بَيْتِ الْمَالِ قَالَ الْعَبْدُ الضَّعِيفُ عَصَمَهُ اللهُ مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا كَانَ جَرَحَهُ وَعَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَافِ إِذَا مَاتَ مِنَ الضَّرْبِ وَعَلَى هَذَا إِذَا رَجَعَ الشُّهُودُ لَا يَضْمَنُونَ عِنْدَهُ وَعِنْدَهُمَا يَضْمَنُونَ لَهُمَا أَنَّ الْوَاجِبَ بِشَهَادَتِهِمْ مُطْلَقُ الضَّرْبِ إِذْ لَا احْتِرَازَ عَنِ الْجَرْحِ خَارِجٌ عَنِ الْوَسْعِ فَيَنْتَظِمُ الْجَارِحَ وَغَيْرَهُ فَيُضَافُ إِلَى شَهَادَتِهِمْ فَيَضْمَنُونَ بِالرُّجُوعِ وَعِنْدَ عَدَمِ الرُّجُوعِ يَجِبُ عَلَى بَيْتِ الْمَالِ لِأَنَّهُ يَنْتَقِلُ فِعْلُ الْجِلَادِ إِلَى الْقَاضِي وَهُوَ عَامِلٌ لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ فَتَجِبُ الْغَرَامَةُ فِي مَالِهِمْ فَصَارَ كَالرَّجُمِ وَالْقِصَاصِ وَلِأَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّ الْوَاجِبَ هُوَ الْجَلْدُ وَهُوَ ضَرْبٌ مُولِمٌ غَيْرُ جَارِحٍ وَلَا مُهْلِكَ فَلَا يَقَعُ جَارِحًا ظَاهِرًا إِلَّا لِمَعْنَى فِي الضَّارِبِ وَهُوَ قِلَّةُ هِدَايَتِهِ فَاقْتَصَرَ عَلَيْهِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ الضَّمَان فِي الصَّحِيحِ كَيْ لَا يَمْتَنِعَ النَّاسُ عَنِ الْإِقَامَةِ مَخَافَةَ الْغَرَامَةِ
And there is not upon them nor upon the public treasury the compensation (arsh) of the flogging. And if he is stoned, his blood money (diyah) is upon the public treasury. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The arsh of the flogging is also upon the public treasury. Al-'Abd al-Da'if (the author) said, may Allah protect him: Its meaning is when it wounds him. And upon this difference is when he dies from the flogging. And upon this, when the witnesses retract, they are not liable according to him, but according to them they are liable. Their proof is that what is obligatory by their testimony is absolute flogging, since it is not possible to avoid wounding, so it includes the wounding and other things, thus it is attributed to their testimony, so they are liable upon retraction. And when there is no retraction, it is obligatory upon the public treasury because the act of the flogger is transferred to the judge, and he is a functionary of the Muslims, so the indemnity becomes obligatory from their wealth, so it becomes like stoning and qisas. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that what is obligatory is lashing (jald), and it is a painful striking that is neither wounding nor killing, so it does not occur as wounding manifestly except due to a cause in the striker, which is his lack of skill. So he confined it to that. However, no liability is obligatory upon him in the correct view, so that people may not refrain from establishing the hadd for fear of indemnity.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage discusses a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding compensation (arsh or diyah) when flogging during the hadd of zina causes injury or death. The matn begins by stating the ruling: If the flogging causes a wound (jarh), there is no arsh upon the witnesses nor upon the public treasury (bayt al-mal). However, if the punishment was stoning (rajm), the diyah is upon the treasury. Abu Hanifa holds this distinction. The Sahibayn, however, hold that even in the case of flogging, the arsh is upon the treasury. The commentator (al-'Abd al-Da'if) clarifies that the Sahibayn's view applies when the flogging actually caused a wound (not just a bruise). The same disagreement applies if the flogging results in death: Abu Hanifa says no compensation, Sahibayn say the diyah is upon the treasury. The dispute extends to the scenario where witnesses retract their testimony (ruju'): According to Abu Hanifa, the witnesses are not liable for the harm; according to Sahibayn, they are liable because the flogging was mandated by their testimony, and since wounding is unavoidable, the entire act is attributed to them. If they do not retract, the liability shifts to the treasury because the execution is by the judge acting for the community. Abu Hanifa's reasoning distinguishes between the obligatory flogging (jald), which is defined as a painful but non-wounding and non-lethal striking; any wounding is due to the striker's lack of skill, not the testimony itself. Therefore, no liability falls on the witnesses or the striker to prevent people from avoiding implementing hudud out of fear of financial responsibility. The correct opinion (al-sahih) is that neither the witnesses nor the striker must pay compensation.

Key Terms
أرش الضرب (arsh al-ḍarb): Compensation for wounding caused by flogging; the amount equal to the difference in value if a slave, or diyah if a free person.
رجوع الشهود (rujūʿ al-shuhūd): Retraction of witnesses from their testimony after the hadd has been carried out.
جَلْد (jald): Flogging as a hadd punishment; defined as painful but non-wounding and non-lethal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if witnesses do not retract and the flogging causes injury, who bears the arsh?
A) The witnesses
B) The public treasury
C) The flogger
D) No one

Key Takeaway
The dominant Hanafi view is that flogging in hadd is non-wounding, so no compensation arises from incidental injury or death, preserving the implementation of hudud.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
Liability for Injury from Hadd Flogging: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on arsh/diya for flogging injury and retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on liability for injury from flogging in hadd punishment, and explain the rationale behind each position.

Core Idea
Flogging is non-injurious by nature; injury comes from the striker's fault, so no compensation is due from witnesses or treasury.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding who bears financial responsibility when a hadd punishment for zina causes injury or death. The Sahibayn hold that the public treasury or retracting witnesses are liable for compensation, while Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the prescribed punishment is simply a painful lashing, not a wounding act. Therefore, no liability attaches to witnesses or the treasury. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the school is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, as indicated by 'في الصحيح'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the dispute about? The dispute concerns liability for injury or death resulting from flogging in the hadd penalty for zina, and the effect of witness retraction.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position
He says neither the witnesses nor the public treasury are liable for injury from flogging; if death occurs, no diya is due. If witnesses retract, they are not liable.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
They say the public treasury is liable for injury from flogging; if death occurs, diya from treasury. If witnesses retract, they become liable for injury/diya.
4
Examine the proofs: Sahibayn's reasoning
They argue that the testimony requires absolute flogging, which inevitably includes risk of injury, so the act is attributed to witnesses (if retract) or judge (if not), thus liability.
5
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof and tarjih
He argues flogging is merely painful, not injurious by nature; injury is due to striker's lack of skill. The striker is responsible, but even he is not liable in the correct view to avoid deterring enforcement of hadd.
The text says 'في الصحيح' (in the correct view), indicating tarjih.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم
کوڑے مارنے سے جو زانی اور زانیہ کو خم ہو اس کا نقصان نہ گواہوں پر ہے نہ بیت المال پر وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلَا عَلَى بَيْتِ الْمَالِ اَرْشُ الضَّرْبِ وَإِنْ رُحِمَ فَدِيَتُهُ عَلَى بَيْتِ الْمَالِ وَهَذَا عِنْدَابِي حَنِيفَةٌ وَقَالَا اَرْشُ الضَّرْبِ أَيْضًا عَلَى بَيْتِ الْمَالِ قَالَ الْعَبْدُ الضَّعِيفُ عَصَمَهُ اللهُ مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا كَانَ جَرَحَهُ وَعَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَافِ إِذَامَاتَ مِنَ الضَّرْبِ وَعَلَى هَذَا إِذَا رَجَعَ الشُّهُودُ لَا يَضْمَنُوْنَ عِنْدَهُ وَعِنْدَهُمَا يَضْمَنُونَ لَهُمَا أَنَّ الْوَاجِبَ بِشَهَادَتِهِمْ مُطْلَقُ الضَّرْبِ إِذَا لُاِحْتِرَازُ عَنِ الْجَرْحِ خَارِجٌ عَنِ الْوَسْعِ فَيَنْتَظِمُ الْجَارِحَ وَغَيْرَهُ فَيُضَافُ إِلَى شَهَادَتِهِمْ فَيَضْمَنُوْنَ بِالرُّجُوعِ وَعِندَ عَدَمِ الرُّجُوعِ يَجِبُ عَلَى بَيْتِ الْمَالِ لِأَنَّهُ يَنْتَقِلُ فِعْلُ الْجِلَادِ إِلَى الْقَاضِي وَهُوَ عَامِلٌ لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ فَتَجِبُ الْغَرَامَةُ فِي مَالِهِمْ فَصَارَ كَالرَّجُمِ وَالْقِصَاصِ وَلَابِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّ الْوَاجِبَ هُوَ الْجَلْدُ وَ هُوَ ضَرْبٌ مُوْلِمٌ غَيْرُ جَارِحٍ وَلَا مُهْلِكَ فَلَا يَقَعُ جَارِحَاظَاهِرًا إِلَّا لِمَعْنَى فِي الضَّارِبِ وَهُوَقِلَّةُ هِدَايَتِا فَاقْتَصَرَ عَلَيْهِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ الضَّمَان فِي الصَّحِيحِ كَيْلا يَمْتَنِعَ النَّاسُ عَنِ الْإِقَامَةِ مَخَافَةَ الْغَرَامَةِ ترجمہ اور جن لوگوں کو درے مارے گئے ہوں گے اور اس مار کی وجہ سے وہ زخمی ہو گئے ہوں تو اس زخم کا نقصان نہ ان گواہوں پر ہوگا اور نہ بیت المال پر جرمانہ ہوگا اور اگر اسے رجم کر دیا گیا ہو تو اس کی دیت بیت المال پر لازم آئے گی۔ یہ تفصیل امام ابوحنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کے قول کے مطابق ہے ( بلکہ رحم کر دینے کی صورت میں حکم پر تمام ائمہ کا اتفاق ہے )۔
صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہما نے فرمایا ہے کہ درے مارے جانے کی صورت میں بھی ( زخم کا تاوان) بیت المال سے یہی ادا کرنا ہوگا۔ عبد ضعیف (مصنف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ ) نے فرمایا ہے کہ صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہا کا یہ قول اس صورت میں ہے کہ اسے درے مارنے سے صرف چوٹ نہ لگی ہو بلکہ زخم بھی آگئے ہوں۔ اسی طرح اگر درے مارے جانے سے وہ مر گیا تو بھی یہی اختلاف ہے۔ یعنی امام اعظم رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک کسی پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہوگا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس کی دیت بیت المال سے ادا کی جائے گی۔ اسی طرح اگر گواہوں نے اپنے دعووں سے رجوع کر لیا یعنی اپنی گواہی سے پھر گئے تو امام اعظم رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک وہ ضامن نہیں ہوں گے اور صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہما کے نزدیک ضامن ہوں گے۔ یعنی زخم کا ائے اور جرمانہ دیں گے اور اگر وہ مرگیا ہو تو اس کی دیت دیں گے۔
صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہا کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان گواہوں کی گواہی سے ہی اس پر ور نے مارنے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے۔ خواہ کسی صورت سے بھی ہو کیونکہ ان کو مار کر زخم ہو جانے سے بچا لینا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یہ مار زخمی کرنے والی مار کو بھی شامل ہے۔ اس لئے یا تو زخمی ہونا یا زخم سے مرجانا سب ان ہی لوگوں کی گواہی کی طرف منسوب ہوگا۔ لہذا گواہی سے رجوع کرلینے کی صورت میں ضامن نہیں ہوں گے اور اگر انہوں نے گواہی سے منہ نہیں موڑا تو ایسی ضمانت بیت المال پر لازم ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس وقت درے مارنے کے عمل کو قاضی کی طرف منسوب کرنا ہوگا۔ پھر چونکہ قاضی کا ہر کام تمام مسلمانوں کا کام ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر جو تاوان آئے گا وہ تمام بھی مسلمان کے مال میں واجب ہوگا۔ یعنی بیت المال سے دینا ہوگا۔ الحاصل دروں کی یہ حالت بھی رجم اور قصاص کے مثل ہو گئی۔
امام ابوحنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان کی گواہی سے صرف درے مارنا واجب ہو یعنی اتنی چوٹ پہنچائی کہ اس سے اس شخص کو تکلیف ہو اور ایسی مارسے کوئی بھی ہلاک نہیں ہوتا ہے اور بظاہر یہ چوٹ زخمی کرنے والی نہ ہوگی مگر جب کہ مارنے والوں کی طرف سے کوئی زیادتی ہو جائے ( یعنی اسکے مارنے کا انداز بیج نہ ہو)۔ تو اس چوٹ اور زخم کا ذمہ دار خود مارنے والا ہوگا اور گواہ اس کے ذمہ دار نہ ہوں گے ۔ لیکن اس مارنے والے پر بھی اس کا تاوان لازم نہیں آئے گا۔ یہی قول صحیح ہے۔ تا کہ تاوان کے خوف سے لوگ حد مارنے سے انکار نہ کر دیں۔
And there is not upon them nor upon the public treasury the compensation for the flogging, but if he was stoned, then his blood-money is upon the public treasury. This is according to Abu Hanifa, and they (the two) said: the compensation for the flogging is also upon the public treasury. Al-Abd al-Da'eef said: meaning when it wounded him. And upon this difference if he died from the flogging, and upon this if the witnesses retract, they do not become liable according to him, but according to them they become liable. Their proof: that what is obligatory by their testimony is absolute flogging, since avoiding injury is beyond capacity, so it includes injurious and other, so it is attributed to their testimony, so they become liable upon retraction. And in the absence of retraction, it is obligatory upon the public treasury because the act of the flogger is transferred to the judge, and he is an agent of the Muslims, so the penalty becomes obligatory in their wealth, so it became like stoning and qisas. And for Abu Hanifa: that the obligatory is merely the lashing, which is a painful blow not injurious nor fatal, so it does not occur as injurious apparently except due to a meaning in the striker, which is his lack of skill, so it is restricted to that; however, no liability is upon him in the correct view, so that people are not deterred from establishing the penalty for fear of liability. Translation: And those who were flogged and due to that flogging they became injured, then the compensation for that injury is not upon the witnesses nor upon the public treasury, and if he was stoned, his blood-money is obligatory upon the public treasury. This detail is according to the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa (rather, in the case of stoning, all imams agree). The Sahibayn said: in the case of flogging also, the compensation for injury is to be paid from the public treasury. Al-Abd al-Da'eef (the author) said: their saying is in the case where from the flogging not only bruise but also injury occurred. Similarly, if he died from the flogging, the same difference exists: according to Imam A'zam, nothing is obligatory on anyone; according to the Sahibayn, his blood-money is paid from the public treasury. Similarly, if the witnesses retract from their claim, i.e., withdrew their testimony, then according to Imam A'zam they are not liable, and according to the Sahibayn they are liable, i.e., they will pay the compensation for injury and if he died, they will pay the blood-money. The proof of the Sahibayn: that by the testimony of these witnesses, the order to flog him was given, regardless of the manner, because avoiding injury during flogging is not possible, so this flogging includes injurious flogging. Therefore, either the injury or death from injury is all attributed to the testimony of these people. Hence, in case of retraction, they are liable; and if they did not retract, then such liability is upon the public treasury because then the act of flogging is attributed to the judge, and since every action of the judge is the action of all Muslims, the compensation that comes becomes obligatory in the wealth of all Muslims, i.e., from the public treasury. So the state of flogging became like stoning and qisas. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa: that by their testimony only flogging is obligatory, i.e., such a blow that causes pain but does not kill, and apparently this blow is not injurious unless there is excess from the striker, i.e., his manner of flogging was bad. So the one responsible for the injury and wound is the striker himself, and the witnesses are not responsible. But even on the striker, compensation is not obligatory in the correct view, so that people do not refuse to establish the hadd penalty out of fear of liability.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) concerning liability for injury or death resulting from flogging in the hadd penalty for zina, as well as the effect of witness retraction. The text begins by stating the ruling: neither the witnesses nor the public treasury are liable for any injury from the flogging; but if the penalty was stoning (rajm), the blood-money (diya) is upon the public treasury. This is Abu Hanifa's position. The Sahibayn hold that even in flogging, compensation for injury is upon the public treasury. The author, Al-Abd al-Da'eef (the commentator), clarifies that the Sahibayn's view applies when the flogging caused actual wounds, not just bruising. The same disagreement applies if the convicted person dies from the flogging. Then the text extends the dispute to the case where witnesses retract their testimony: according to Abu Hanifa, they are not liable; according to the Sahibayn, they are liable for injury and blood-money. The Sahibayn's reasoning is that the witnesses' testimony led to the flogging, and since it is impossible to guarantee that flogging will not cause injury, the flogging is considered absolute, including injurious flogging. Therefore, if the witnesses retract, the injury is attributed to their testimony, making them liable. If they do not retract, the flogging is attributed to the judge, who acts for the public, so liability falls on the public treasury, analogous to stoning and qisas. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that the prescribed punishment is mere lashing (jald), which is a painful but non-injurious and non-fatal blow. Injury or death occurs only due to the striker's lack of skill, so the striker is responsible, not the witnesses. However, in the correct view, even the striker is not liable for damages to encourage people to carry out hadd penalties without fear of financial liability. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, as the text says 'في الصحيح' (in the correct view).

Key Terms
ارش (arsh): Compensation for injury to the body where the amount is not fixed by law but assessed by experts.
دية (diya): Blood-money, fixed compensation for homicide or certain injuries.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction of testimony by witnesses after a judgment.
ضمان (daman): Liability for compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, if a person convicted of zina dies from injuries sustained during flogging, who is liable for the blood-money?
A) The witnesses
B) The public treasury
C) No one is liable
D) The judge

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi position is that no one is liable for injury or death from hadd flogging, as the punishment is inherently non-injurious and non-fatal.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
Testimony on Testimony (Shahada ala Shahada) in Zina Cases
Ruling that hadd is not applied in shahada ala shahada for zina, and even original direct testimony does not revive the case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the Hanafi school does not apply the hadd penalty when four witnesses testify on the testimony of four others in a zina case, and explain the ruling that even if the original witnesses later testify directly, the penalty is still not applied.

Core Idea
Increased doubt (shubha) in indirect testimony repels the hadd; this doubt persists even if original witnesses testify directly later.

This lesson examines a specific rule in Hanafi hudud law: the rejection of shahada ala shahada (testimony on testimony) in zina cases. While such indirect testimony is accepted in property disputes due to necessity, the stakes in hudud are far higher. The Hanafi school holds that any increase in doubt prevents the application of hadd, and this doubt is not cured by later direct testimony from the original witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being judged? Four witnesses testify on the testimony of four others that a man committed zina. The ruling: the accused is not given the hadd penalty.
This is a ruling of non-application.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the principle 'ادرأوا الحدود بالشبهات' (Avert hadd penalties by doubts). The text explicitly cites 'زيادة الشبهة' (increased doubt) and lack of necessity.
The dalil is a qiyas based on the general principle, not a specific textual proof from Quran or hadith.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase is 'زيادة الشبهة' – increased doubt. Since shahada ala shahada inherently involves double layers of reporting, the possibility of error multiplies. Hadd is repelled by the slightest doubt, so this increased doubt makes the testimony unacceptable.
There is no necessity (لا ضرورة) to accept such testimony in hudud, unlike in property cases.
4
Determine the thamarah (practical consequence)
The practical consequence is that even if the original four witnesses later come and testify directly about witnessing the act, still no hadd is applied. This is because their testimony was already rejected due to the rejection of the branch witnesses; they stand in the place of the branches.
The witnesses themselves are not liable for qadhf because their number is complete (four), so the condition for qadhf (less than four witnesses) is not met.

ترجمہ اور اگر چار آدمیوں نے دوسرے چار آدمیوں کے گواہی دینے پر گواہی دی کہ فلاں نے زنا کیا ہے۔ تو اس شخص کو حد نہیں لگائی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ ان لوگوں کی گواہی میں بہت سے شبہات پیدا ہو جاتے ہیں اور اس گواہی کو قبول کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت بھی نہیں ہے۔ تشریح وَإِنْ شَهِدَ ارْبَعَةٌ عَلَى شَهَادَةِ أَرْبَعَةٍ عَلَى رَجُلٍ بِالزِّنَاءِ لَمْ يُحَدُّ لِمَا فِيهَا مِنْ زِيَادَةِ الشُّبْهَةِ ... الخ اگر چار آدمیوں نے دوسرے چار آدمیوں کی گواہی کی بناء پر کسی پر زنا کا الزام لگایا۔ ف۔ جس کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ مرد پر زنا کا الزام لگانے والے چار گواہ تھے۔ ان چاروں نے اپنی گواہی پر دوسرے چار مردوں کو گواہ بنایا۔ پس ان دوسرے چاروں نے پہلے چاروں گواہوں کی گواہی پر مرد کے خلاف زنا کرنے کی گواہی دی تو اس گواہی کی بناء پر اس شخص کو حد زنا نہیں لگائی جائے گی جس پر الزام لگایا گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس جگہ یہ شبہ پیدا ہو جاتا ہے کہ نجانے اصل گواہوں نے کیا کہا تھا۔ اس لئے اس میں یہ احتمال ہو سکتا تھا کہ اسے قبول نہ کیا جائے اور اگر ان لوگوں نے تو صیح طریقہ سے کہا تھا مگر اب یہ دوسرے گواہ اس کی ادائیگی میں کچھ فرق کر رہے ہوں ۔ اس طرح اس میں شبہ پر شبہ پیدا ہو گیا اور اسی گواہی قبول کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اس لئے وہ رد کر دی جائے گی اور ان دوسرے گواہوں کی گواہی نا مقبول ہوئی تو پہلے گواہوں کی بھی گواہی نا مقبول ہوگئی ۔ فان جاء الاولون .. الخ ترجمہ سے مطلب واضح ہے۔
......
اصل چار گواہوں نے معین مقام پر اپنے دیکھنے کی گواہی دی پھر بھی حد نہیں لگائی جائے گی
فَإِنْ جَاءَ الْأَوَّلُونَ فَشَهِدُوا عَلَى الْمُعَايَنَةِ فِي ذَالِكَ الْمَكَانِ لَمْ يُحَدَّ أَيْضًا مَعْنَاهُ شَهِدُوا عَلَى ذَالِكَ الزِّنَاءِ بِعَيْنِهِ لانَّ شَهَادَتَهُمْ قَدْرُدَّتْ مِنْ وَجْهِ بِرَدِ شَهَادَةِ الْفُرُوعِ فِي عَيْنِ هَذِهِ الْحَادِثَةِ إِذْهُمْ قَائِمُونَ مَقَامَهُمْ فِي الْأمْرِ وَالتَّحْمِيلِ وَلَا يُحَدُّ الشُّهُودُ لِاَنَّ عَدَدَهُمْ مُتَكَامِلٌ وَامْتِنَاعُ الْحَدِعَنِ الْمَشْهُودِ عَلَيْهِ لِنَوْعِ شُبْهَةٍ وَهِيَ كَافِيَةٌ لِدَرْءِ الْحَدِلَا لِإِيجَابِهِ
ترجمہ پھر اگر پہلے چاروں یعنی اصل گواہوں نے اگر اس مقام پر اپنے دیکھنے کی گواہی دی تو بھی اس شخص کو جس کے خلاف الزام لگایا گیا ہے حد نہیں ماری جائے گی۔ اس مقام کے کہنے سے مراد یہ ہے کہ بعینہ اس زنا کی گواہی دی (بغیر کسی فرق کے ) تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ان اصل گواہوں کی گواہی بھی ایک طرح سے رد کر دی گئی ہے۔ اس صورت ہے کہ اسی حادثہ ( واقعہ ) میں ان کے فروع ( دوسرے گواہ) کی گواہی رد کی گئی ہے۔ کیونکہ گواہی کو قبول کرنے پھر اسے بیان کرنے میں ان کے فروع ( دوسرے گواہ) ان کے حکم سے ان کے قائم مقام ہیں۔ پھر ان گواہوں کو بھی حد قذف نہیں لگائی جائے گی۔ نہ پہلے اور اصل گواہوں کو اور نہ دوسرے گواہوں کو۔ کیونکہ تعداد میں وہ پورے پورے ہیں اور جس کے خلاف انہوں نے گواہی دی اس سے بھی حد کا ساقط ہونا ایک قسم کا شبہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے ہے اور یہی شبہ اس سے حد کو ختم کرنے کے لئے کافی ہے۔ مگر گواہوں پر حد قذف واجب ہونے کے لئے کافی نہیں ہے۔ تشریح فَإِنْ جَاءَ الْأَوَّلُونَ فَشَهِدُوا عَلَى الْمُعَايَنَةِ فِي ذَالِكَ الْمَكَانِ لَمْ يُحَدَّ أَيْضًا مَعْنَاهُ الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
And if four testify on the testimony of four against a man of zina, he is not subjected to hadd, because there is increased doubt in it and there is no necessity to bear it. Translation: And if four men testify on the testimony of four other men that so-and-so committed zina, then that person will not be subjected to hadd. Because many doubts arise in this testimony and there is no need to accept it. Explanation: If four men accused a man of zina based on the testimony of four others—the scenario being there were four witnesses accusing the man of zina; these four made four other men as witnesses on their testimony. Then those four testified against the man based on the testimony of the first four, then based on this testimony the accused is not given the hadd of zina. Because here doubt arises: what did the original witnesses actually say? So it could be rejected; and if the original witnesses said it correctly but these second witnesses made a mistake in conveying it, thus doubt upon doubt. And there is no need to accept this testimony, so it is rejected. And when the second witnesses' testimony is rejected, the first witnesses' testimony also becomes rejected. Then if the original witnesses come and testify on direct observation in that place, still he is not hadded. Meaning: they testify about that specific act of zina, because their testimony was already rejected from one aspect due to the rejection of the branches' testimony in this same incident, since they stand in their place in the matter of bearing and conveying. And the witnesses themselves are not subjected to hadd of qadhf because their number is complete (four), and the prevention of hadd from the accused is due to a type of doubt, and that is sufficient for repelling hadd, not for imposing it.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage contains two related rulings. First, if four witnesses come and testify on the basis of the testimony of four other witnesses that a man committed zina (i.e., shahada ala shahada), the hadd penalty is not applied because the testimony involves increased doubt (shubha). The reason given is that there is uncertainty about what the original witnesses actually said, and there is no necessity to accept such indirect testimony, unlike in property cases where shahada ala shahada is sometimes accepted due to necessity. Therefore, the testimony of the branch witnesses is rejected, and consequently the testimony of the original witnesses is also deemed rejected for this incident. Second, even if the original witnesses later come and testify directly about witnessing the act, again the hadd is not applied. This is because the case was already concluded with the rejection of the branch witnesses, and the original witnesses are considered to stand in the place of the branches in bearing and conveying. So their later direct testimony is not accepted for this case. However, the witnesses themselves are not liable for the hadd of qadhf (false accusation) because their number is complete (four men), so the condition for qadhf (less than four) is not met. The repelling of hadd from the accused is due to doubt, which is sufficient to prevent the hadd but not sufficient to impose hadd on the witnesses.

Key Terms
شهادة على شهادة (shahada 'ala shahada): Testimony based on the testimony of another witness, permissible in certain cases like property but not in hadd.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt that prevents the application of hadd penalties.
حد (hadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Islamic law for certain crimes.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina, punishable by 80 lashes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of shahada ala shahada for zina, why is hadd not applied even if the original witnesses later testify directly?
A) Because the original witnesses are not reliable
B) Because the branch witnesses' rejection caused the original witnesses' testimony to be rejected for this case
C) Because the accused confessed
D) Because the number of witnesses is incomplete

Key Takeaway
Shahada ala shahada is not accepted in zina cases due to increased doubt, and this doubt prevents hadd even if original witnesses later testify directly.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

Retraction of Witness Before Hadd Execution: Whose Liability?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hadd qadhf liability when witness retracts before execution of hadd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for hadd qadhf when a witness retracts before execution, explain the differing positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad/Zufar, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Retraction before execution nullifies the entire testimony; all witnesses face hadd qadhf.

This passage addresses a specific intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of a witness's retraction after a guilty verdict but before the hadd punishment is carried out. The key question is whether the retraction invalidates the testimony of all witnesses or only the retractor. The answer determines who receives the punishment for false accusation (hadd qadhf). Understanding this ruling clarifies how the Hanafi school balances the finality of a judge's verdict with the right of witnesses to retract before actual punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Context
Determine what type of testimony and retraction is being discussed. The case involves witnesses to adultery (zina) who retract their testimony after the judge has issued a stoning verdict but before the stoning (hadd) is executed on the accused.
This is distinct from retraction after execution, which only affects the retracting witness.
2
State the Base Ruling (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf)
State what Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold: all witnesses are liable for hadd qadhf (eighty lashes for false accusation), and the accused's hadd is dropped.
This is the position from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi.
3
Analyze Imam Muhammad's Position
Explain why Imam Muhammad limits liability to only the retracting witness. He argues that the testimony was confirmed by the judge's verdict; therefore, the retraction only nullifies the testimony regarding the retractor himself, similar to retraction after execution.
Muhammad cites the principle that once the verdict is passed, the testimony is strengthened and cannot be undone for non-retracting witnesses.
4
Analyze Imam Zufar's Position
Explain Imam Zufar's different reasoning: he argues that the retracting witness's word is not believed against the other witnesses, so only the retractor should be punished.
Zufar focuses on evidentiary credibility rather than the timing of the verdict.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Response and Tarjih
Understand why the majority position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is preferred. The response is that execution is part of the judgment; without execution, the verdict is incomplete. Thus, retraction before execution nullifies the entire connection between the testimony and the verdict, reverting the speech to an accusation (qadhf).
The tarjih is based on the principle that 'al-imdā' min al-qaḍā'' (execution is part of the judgment), making retraction before execution equivalent to retraction before judgment.

Source Text

سے رجم کا حکم باطل ہے۔ اس لئے کچھ شبہ نہیں ہوگا کہ اس نے ایک ایسے محسن کو جس میں کوئی عیب نہیں ہے زنا کی غلط تہمت لگائی ہے۔ البتہ اگر گواہ کے سوا کوئی دوسرا شخص اسے زنا کی تہمت لگائے تو قاضی کا حکم اس کے حق میں باقی رہے گا۔ اس لئے حد قذف نہیں لگائی جائے گی۔ مشہود علیہ کو ابھی حد جاری نہیں کی گئی کہ گواہوں میں سے ایک نے رجوع کر لیا سب کو حد لگائی جائے گی فَإِنْ لَمْ يُحَدَّ الْمَشْهُودُ عَلَيْهِ حَتَّى رَجَعَ وَاحِدٌ مِنْهُمْ حُدُّوا جَمِيعًا وَسَقَطَ الْحَدُّ عَنِ الْمَشْهُودِ عَلَيْهِ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ حد الراجع خَاصَّةً لأنَّ الشَّهَادَةَ تَأكَّدَتْ بِالْقَضَاءِ فَلَا يَنفَسِحُ إِلَّا فِى حَقِّ الرَّاجِعِ كَمَا إِذَا رَجَعَ بَعْدَ الْإِمْضَاءِ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّ الْإِمْضَاءَ مِنَ الْقَضَاءِ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا رَجَعَ وَاحِدٌ مِنْهُمْ قَبْلَ الْقَضَاءِ وَلِهَذَا سَقَطَ الْحَدُّ عَنِ الْمَشْهُودِ عَلَيْهِ وَلَوْ رَجَعَ وَاحِدٌ مِنْهُمْ قَبْلَ الْقَضَاءِ حُدُّوا جَمِيعًا وَقَالَ زُفَرُ يُحَدُّ الرَّاجِعُ خَاصَةٌ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُصَدِّقَ عَلَى غَيْرِهِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ كَلَامَهُمْ قَذَتْ فِي الْأَصْلِ وَإِنَّمَا يَصِيْرُ شَهَادَةً بِاتِّصَالِ الْقَضَاءِ به فَإِذَالَمْ يَتَّصِلْ بَقِيَ قَدَفًا فَيُحَدُّونَ ترجمه . پس اگر مکمل گواہی کے بعد بھی اس ملزم (جس کے خلاف گواہی دی گئی) کو حد نہیں لگائی گئی ہو کہ ان میں سے کوئی ایک گواہ بھی اپنے دعوئی سے پھر گیا ہو تو ان تمام گواہوں پر حد قذف لگائی جائے گی اور اس ملزم سے وہ حد قذف ختم ہو جائے گی اور امام محمد رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ تمام گواہوں پر نہیں بلکہ صرف رجوع کرنے والے پر حد جاری کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ قاضی کے فیصلہ کے ساتھ ہی ان لوگوں کی گواہی پختہ اور مضبوط ہوگئی ہے۔ اس لئے مکمل گواہی فسخ نہیں ہو گی۔ البتہ صرف اس کے حق میں فتح ہو گی۔ جس نے اب رجوع کر لیا ہے۔ جیسے کہ ملزم (مشہود علیہ ) پر حد جاری کئے جانے کے بعد کسی گواہ نے رجوع کر لیا ہو تو فقط اس کو حد قذف لگائی جاتی ہے اور اس کی ذمہ داری میں سے ہے۔ اس لئے یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے قاضی کے فیصلہ سے پہلے ہی کسی نے رجوع کر لیا ہو۔ اسی وجہ سے اس مشہود علیہ سے حد ساقط ہوگئی اور اگر قاضی کے حکم سے پہلے کسی ایک گواہ نے بھی رجوع کرلیا تو ان تمام گواہوں کو حد ماری جائے گی اور امام زفر رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ صرف رجوع کرنے والے کو حد لگائی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ اس کے قول کی تصدیق دوسرے گواہوں پر نہ ہوگی اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ گواہوں کا کلام اصل میں ایک بہتان اور الزام ہے مگر جب اس کے بعد قاضی کا فیصلہ بھی صادر ہو جائے تو وہی بہتان گواہی سے بدل جاتا ہے اور موجودہ صورت میں جب قاضی کا حکم اس کے ساتھ نہیں ہوا تو وہ اپنی حالت پر بہتان ہی باقی رہا۔ اسی لئے سب کو حد لگائی جائے گی۔
Chapter: Testimony for Adultery and Retraction Therefrom. Benefit: Imam Zufar's argument is that the hadd of qadhf is imposed on a witness only if he accused a chaste Muslim of adultery during his lifetime. In the present case, the person against whom testimony was given was stoned. Now if the witness retracts his testimony, his statements cannot become an accusation of adultery because the one stoned is dead. If we consider the accusation as having been made during his life, the hadd of qadhf is waived due to death, as it is not inherited. If we consider it after death, it is not an accusation since the person was stoned by the judge's order. But when the retraction invalidates the proof of adultery, the person is not actually an adulterer, though the judge's order created a semblance. Hence the witness's qadhf hadd is dropped. Our proof: the judge issued the stoning order based on complete testimony; when a witness retracts, the judge's order is nullified. Thus the witness becomes an accuser of a chaste person, so there is no doubt that he falsely accused a chaste person. However, if someone other than the witness accuses him, the judge's order remains effective, so no qadhf hadd. The accused not yet punished, one witness retracted, so all are punished. If the accused is not hadded until one of them retracts, they are all hadded and the hadd is dropped from the accused. Muhammad said: only the retractor is hadded because the testimony was strengthened by the judgment, so it is not void except regarding the retractor, as if he retracted after execution. The two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) said: execution is part of judgment, so it is like retraction before judgment, and therefore the hadd is dropped from the accused. If one retracts before judgment, all are hadded. Zufar said: only the retractor is hadded because his word is not believed against others. Our proof: their speech is originally an accusation, and it becomes testimony only by connection with judgment. If it does not connect, it remains an accusation, so they are all hadded. Translation: So if the accused (against whom testimony was given) is not hadded until one of the witnesses retracts from his claim, then all witnesses are given the hadd of qadhf, and the hadd is dropped from the accused. Imam Muhammad said: not all, but only the retractor is hadded. Because with the judge's decision, their testimony became firm and strong. Therefore the complete testimony is not annulled; rather it is annulled only regarding the retractor. This is like when a witness retracts after the hadd is executed on the accused, only that witness is hadded. So this becomes like retraction before the judge's decision. Hence the hadd is dropped from the accused. If one witness retracts before the judge's decision, all witnesses are hadded. Imam Zufar said: only the retractor is hadded because his statement is not believed against others. Our proof: the witnesses' speech is originally an accusation, but when the judge's decision follows, that accusation becomes testimony. In the present case, when the judge's decision did not follow, it remains an accusation, so all are hadded.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability for hadd qadhf when one of the witnesses retracts before the hadd (stoning) is executed on the accused. The base ruling (from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that all witnesses receive the hadd of qadhf, and the hadd is dropped from the accused. Imam Muhammad argues that only the retracting witness is liable, because the testimony was already confirmed by the judge's decision (even though execution didn't occur), so the retraction only affects the retractor's own liability. Imam Zufar also holds that only the retractor is liable, but for a different reason: the retractor's statement cannot be believed against the other witnesses. The preferred Hanafi position is that all witnesses are liable, as the retraction before execution prevents the testimony from being finalized; thus their speech remains an accusation (qadhf). This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah. The key is that once the judge issues a verdict, the testimony is considered confirmed; retraction after verdict only affects the retractor. But before execution, the verdict is not fully implemented, so the retraction undoes the entire testimony.

Key Terms
رجوع (rujūʿ): Retraction of testimony by a witness after having given it.
حد قذف (ḥadd qadhf): Fixed punishment for false accusation of adultery (eighty lashes).
مشهود عليه (mashhūd ʿalayh): The person against whom testimony is given (the accused).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the base ruling (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is the consequence when one witness retracts before the hadd is executed on the accused?
A) Only the retracting witness receives hadd qadhf
B) All witnesses receive hadd qadhf and the accused's hadd is dropped
C) The accused is still executed but the witness is not punished
D) No one receives hadd qadhf

Key Takeaway
Retraction before execution reverts testimony to an accusation, making all witnesses liable for hadd qadhf.

Five Witnesses: One or Two Retract
Ruling on liability when one or two out of five witnesses retract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings when one or two out of five witnesses retract in a hadd case and apply the principle that consideration is given to the remaining witnesses.

Core Idea
With five witnesses, one retraction leaves four sufficient; two retractions trigger hadd and quarter diyah.

In Hudud cases, the testimony of four witnesses is required. If there are initially five, the retraction of one does not affect the validity of the testimony, but retraction of a second reduces the count below four. This makes the retractors liable for false accusation (hadd qadhf) and a proportional share of the diyah. This lesson explains the precise consequences and the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial and required numbers
Note that there are five witnesses initially, but the requirement for establishing hadd is four witnesses. Determine the threshold.
2
Analyze the first retraction
If one retracts, four remain. Since four satisfy the requirement, the claim remains valid and no penalty is incurred.
The retractor alone does not cause the testimony to become defective.
3
Analyze the second retraction
If a second retracts, only three remain. The testimony is now insufficient to prove the hadd, so the retractors' speech becomes an accusation.
The number falls below the required four.
4
Determine the consequences for the two retractors
The two retractors are subject to hadd qadhf (since their retraction implies the others were false) and are liable for a quarter of the diyah, because the remaining three preserve three-quarters of the right.
The diyah is apportioned according to the number of witnesses who did not retract.
5
Apply the principle
Remember: consideration is given to those who remain, not to those who retract. This principle is consistent with the rules of testimony.
The ruling follows the logic of preserving the right based on the remaining witnesses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ كَانُوا خَمْسَةٌ فَرَجَعَ أَحَدُهُمْ فَلَاشَى عَلَيْهِمْ لِأَنَّهُ بَقِيَ مَنْ يَبْقَى بِشَهَادَتِهِ كُلُّ الْحَقِّ وَهُوَ شَهَادَةُ الْأَرْبَعِ فَإِنْ رَجَعَ الخَرُحُدًا وَغَرِ مَارُبْعَ الذِيَةِ أَمَّا الْحُدَّ فَلِمَا ذَكَرْنَا وَأَمَّا الْغَرَامَةُ فَلَانَّهُ بَقِيَ مَنْ يَبْقَى بِشَهَادَتِهِ ثَلَثَةُ أَرْبَاع الْحَقِّ وَالْمُعْتَبَرُ بَقَاءُ مَنْ بَقِيَ لَا رُجُوعُ مَنْ رَجَعَ عَلَى مَاعُرِفَ ترجمہ اور اگر گواہ پانچ ہوں ان میں سے ایک نے گواہی سے رجوع کر لیا تو باقی لوگوں پر کچھ بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا اورحکم میں فرق نہیں آئے گا۔ کیونکہ اس وقت بھی مکمل چار گواہ باقی نہیں جس سے دعوئی صحیح ہوتا ہے اور اگر اس کے بعد ایک اور گواہ نے بھی رجوع کر لیا تو ان دونوں پر حد قذف لگائی جائے گی اور یہ دونوں چوتھائی دیت کے ذمہ دار ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ حد تو اسی وجہ سے واجب ہوگی جو ہم نے ابھی بیان کر دی ہے ( یعنی جب پانچ میں سے دو گواہوں نے بھی رجوع کر لیا تو ان سب کی بات تہمت سے بدل گئی کیونکہ اب ان کی بات قاضی کے فیصلہ جاری کرنے کے لائق نہیں رہی کہ وہ گواہی میں کہی جاسکے ۔ اور چوتھائی دیت کے ضامن وہ دونوں اس لئے ہوں گے کہ باقی تینوں پر تین چوتھائی حق باقی رہ گیا ہے اور جو گواہ اپنی گواہی پر باقی رہے اس کے باقی رہنے کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے اور جو گواہی سے نکل گیا اس کے نکلنے کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ کتاب الشهادات میں ذکر کیا گیا ہے۔ تشریح... فَإِنْ كَانُوا خَمْسَةٍ فَرَجَعَ أَحَدُهُمْ فَلَاشَى عَلَيْهِمْ لِأَنَّهُ بَقِيَ مَنْ يَبْقَى بِشَهَادَتي ... الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
If there are five witnesses and one of them retracts, then nothing is upon them (the remaining) because there remains one whose testimony preserves all the right, which is the testimony of four. If another retracts, then the two [retractors] are hadded and are liable for a quarter of the diyah. As for the hadd, it is for the reason we mentioned; as for the fine, because there remains one whose testimony preserves three-quarters of the right, and consideration is given to the one who remains, not the one who retracted, as is known. Translation: And if the witnesses are five, and one of them retracts from the testimony, then nothing is incumbent on the remaining ones and the ruling does not change. Because there still remain four witnesses sufficient for the claim. If after that another witness also retracts, then both of them are given the hadd of qadhf and they are liable for a quarter of the diyah. The hadd is wajib for the reason we just explained (i.e., when two out of five retract, their speech becomes an accusation because it is no longer capable of being the basis for the judge's verdict). And they are liable for a quarter of the diyah because three-quarters of the right remains with the remaining three witnesses. The consideration is given to those who remain on their testimony, not to those who left it, as mentioned in Kitab al-Shahadat. Explanation: The text 'Fa in kanu khamsatun...' etc. is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage clarifies a specific scenario: if there are five witnesses and one retracts, the remaining four are sufficient, so no penalty. This is because the testimony of four is enough to establish the hadd. If two retract, leaving only three witnesses, the testimony becomes incomplete, so the retractors are liable for hadd qadhf (since their speech now amounts to false accusation). Additionally, they are liable for a quarter of the diyah (blood money) because the remaining three witnesses preserve three-quarters of the right (i.e., the diyah is apportioned according to the number of witnesses who did not retract). The principle is that consideration is given to those who remain, not those who retract. This ruling is consistent with the general rules of testimony found in Kitab al-Shahadat. No intra-Hanafi dispute is mentioned here; it is a straightforward application.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money paid for wrongful death or injury; here, a fine paid by witnesses who retract after conviction.
غرامة (gharāmah): Financial liability; here, a quarter of the diyah imposed on retracting witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If five witnesses to adultery testify and two retract, what is the liability of the two retractors?
A) Hadd qadhf only
B) Hadd qadhf and quarter diyah
C) Full diyah
D) No liability

Key Takeaway
With five witnesses, retraction of one is harmless; retraction of two makes the retractors liable for hadd qadhf and a quarter of the diyah.

Four Witnesses Found to Be Slaves or Magians After Tazkiya
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diyah liability after defective tazkiya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on diyah liability when witnesses are disqualified after tazkiya, and identify the practical difference between the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Tazkiya is either a cause of the cause or a condition—the difference determines who pays diyah.

When four witnesses are certified by tazkiya evaluators, the accused is executed, and the witnesses are later discovered to be disqualified (slaves or non-Muslims), who bears the blood money? Abu Hanifa and his two students disagree on this point. Their dispute hinges on the legal nature of tazkiya: is it integral to the testimony's effect or merely an endorsement? This lesson unpacks their arguments and the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize the case: four witnesses testify for zina, are certified by tazkiya evaluators, the accused is stoned, then the witnesses turn out to be slaves or Magians. The question is who is liable for diyah.
The text specifies the evaluators retracted their certification for liability to arise.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa: the diyah is on the tazkiya evaluators (muzakkūn).
This applies if they explicitly retract and admit they knew the witnesses were disqualified.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: the diyah is on the state treasury (bayt al-māl).
They argue the evaluators merely praised the witnesses, similar to praising the accused's ihsan.
4
Analyze the proofs of each side
Abu Hanifa: testimony becomes effective only through tazkiya, so tazkiya is the cause of the cause (ʿillat al-ʿilla), thus the ruling is attributed to it. Sahibayn: tazkiya is like ihsan testimony—a pure condition, not a cause.
The text uses qiyas: Sahibayn analogize to ihsan; Abu Hanifa distinguishes them.
5
Determine the tarjih and practical consequence
The text indicates the preferred view is Abu Hanifa's (wa qīla). Practical consequence: if liable on evaluators, they pay from personal funds; if on treasury, the state pays.
Also note the exception: if evaluators only said 'they are upright' (not specifying freedom/Islam), they are not liable even if witnesses are slaves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ شَهِدَ أَرْبَعَةٌ عَلَى رَجُلٍ بِالِزَّنَاءِ فَرُكُوْا فَرْجِمَ فَإِذَا الشُّهُودُ مَجُوسٌ اَوْعَبِيدٌ فَالدِّيَةُ عَلَى الْمُزَكِّيْنَ عِنْدَابِي حَنِيفَةَ مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا رَجَعُوا عَنِ التَّرْكِيَةِ وَقَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ وَ مُحَمَّدٌ هُوَ عَلَى بَيْتِ الْمَالِ وَقِيلَ هَذَا إِذَا قَالُوا تَعَمَّدْنَا التَّزْكِيَةَ مَعَ عِلْمِنَا بِحَالِهِمْ لَهُمَا أَنَّهُمْ اثْنَوْا عَلَى الشُّهُودِ خَيْرًا فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا اثْنَوْا عَلَى الْمَشْهُودِ عَلَيْهِ خَيْرًا بِانَّهُ شَهِدُوا عَلَى إِحْصَانِهِ وَلَهُ اَنَّ الشَّهَادَةَ إِنَّمَا تَصِيْرُ حُجَّةً عَامِلَةً بِالتَّزْكِيَةِ فَكَانَتِ التَّزْكِيَةِ فِي مَعْنَى عِلَّةِ الْعِلَّةِ فَيُضَافُ الْحُكْمُ إِلَيْهَا بِخِلَافِ شُهُودِ الْإِحْصَان لأَنَّهُ مَحْضُ الشَّرْطِ وَلَا فَرْق بَيْنَهُمَا إِذَاشَهِدُ وَابلَفْظَةِ الشَّهَادَةِ أوْ أَخْبَرَ واوَهَذَا إِذَا خَبَرُ وا بِالْحُرِّيَّةِ وَالْإِسْلَامِ أَمَّا إِذَا قَالُوا هُمْ عُدُولٌ وَظَهَرُوا عَبِيْدًا لَا يَضْمَنُوْنَ لِأَنَّ الْعَبْدَ قَدْ يَكُونُ عَدْلًا وَلَا ضَمَانَ عَلَى الشُّهُودِلَانَّهُ لَمْ يَقَعُ كَلَامُهُمْ شَهَادَةً وَلَا يُحَدُّونَ حَدًا لِّقَذَفِ لِأَنَّهُمْ قَذَفُوا حَيًّا وَقَدْ مَاتَ فَلَايُورَتْ عَنْهُ ترجمہ اگر چار آدمیوں نے کسی ایک کے خلاف زنا کرنے کی گواہی دی۔ پھر تزکیہ کرنے والوں (جانچنے والوں) نے ان سہوں کو عادل اور شہادت دینے کے قابل مان لیا۔ اس کے بعد اس ملزم کو رجم کر دیا گیا تب ان کے متعلق اچانک یہ تحقیق ہوئی کہ وہ سب مجوس (غیر مسلم ) یا غلام ہیں ۔ تو امام ابوحنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک اس شخص کی دیت ان کی تحقیق اور تزکیہ کرنے والوں پر لازم آئے گی۔ گواہوں کو عادل بتلانے کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ
And if four testify against a man for adultery, and they [the witnesses] are ridden? [the text is unclear] and he is stoned, and then it turns out that the witnesses are Magians or slaves, then the diyah is upon the tazkiya evaluators according to Abu Hanifa, meaning if they retract from the tazkiya. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: it is upon the treasury. It is said: this is if they said 'we deliberately gave tazkiya knowing their condition'. Their proof: they praised the witnesses, so it is like if they praised the accused by testifying to his ihsan. His proof: testimony becomes a working proof only by tazkiya, so tazkiya is like the cause of the cause, thus the ruling is attributed to it, unlike witnesses of ihsan because it is a pure condition. And there is no difference between them when they testify with the word of testimony or inform. And that is when they inform of freedom and Islam. But if they say 'they are upright' and they appear to be slaves, they are not liable because a slave may be upright. And there is no liability on the witnesses because their speech did not become testimony, nor are they hadded for qadhf because they accused a living person [who] has died, so it is not inherited. Translation: If four men testify against someone for adultery, then the tazkiya evaluators (the verifiers) considered them upright and fit for testimony. Then the accused was stoned. Afterwards it is suddenly discovered that they are all Magians (non-Muslims) or slaves. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the diyah of that person will be upon those who investigated and gave tazkiya. The meaning of pronouncing the witnesses upright is that...
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage deals with the case where four witnesses testify against a man for adultery, they are evaluated (tazkiya) as upright, the accused is stoned, and then it is discovered that the witnesses were actually slaves or Magians (i.e., not qualified to testify). The question is who is liable for the diyah (blood money). Abu Hanifa holds that the evaluators (muzakkūn) who certified the witnesses are liable for the diyah, provided they retract their certification. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the diyah is on the state treasury (bayt al-mal). The text mentions that if the evaluators knowingly and deliberately gave false tazkiya, then they are liable. The reasoning of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that the evaluators simply praised the witnesses, analogous to praising the accused's ihsan (which does not create liability). Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that testimony becomes effective only through tazkiya, so tazkiya is the cause of the cause, and thus the ruling (diyah) is attributed to it. Distinction is made between tazkiya of witnesses and testimony of ihsan; the latter is a pure condition, whereas tazkiya is instrumental. Further details: if the evaluators merely said the witnesses are 'upright' (ʿudūl) and they turn out to be slaves, they are not liable because a slave can be upright (in character). Also, the original witnesses are not liable for the diyah because their speech never became valid testimony (due to their disqualification), and they are not hadded for qadhf because they accused a living person who then died, and the hadd is not inherited. The passage is incomplete but covers the main points.

Key Terms
تزکیہ (tazkiyah): The process of evaluating and certifying the uprightness of witnesses.
مزکی (muzakkī): The person who performs tazkiyah, i.e., the evaluator or verifier of witnesses.
بیت المال (bayt al-māl): The public treasury of the Islamic state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After four witnesses testified and the accused was stoned, the witnesses were found to be slaves. According to Abu Hanifa, who is liable for the diyah?
A) The witnesses themselves
B) The tazkiya evaluators
C) The state treasury
D) No one

Key Takeaway
The liability for diyah in cases of defective witness certification falls on the evaluators per Abu Hanifa, because tazkiya is considered the effective cause of the testimony's legal effect.

Establishing Ihsan Through Childbirth: Testimony and Denial
Ruling on proving ihsan via childbirth despite denial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on establishing ihsan when the defendant denies entry but has a child from his wife, and explain the legal reasoning based on lineage.

Core Idea
A child's legal lineage from a man conclusively proves marital entry, thus establishing ihsan for hudud even if the man verbally denies it.

In cases of zina testimony, the penalty of stoning requires that the accused be muhsan — married and having consummated the marriage. But what if the accused denies having had marital relations (dukhul) while his wife has given birth to his child? The Hanafi school upholds the ruling that childbirth establishes entry, overriding the verbal denial. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind this strong evidentiary presumption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed element
The act is zina testimony. The disputed element is ihsan, specifically the condition of entry (dukhul). The defendant verbally denies entry.
Ihsan requires valid marriage, freedom, Islam, and consummation.
2
Recognize the evidence
The evidence is the existence of a child born from the wife of the accused. The child is legally attributed to him (thubut al-nasab).
Lineage is established by birth in a valid marriage.
3
Understand the inference
The Hanafi school reasons that establishing lineage (thubut al-nasab) necessitates a prior ruling that dukhul occurred, because a child cannot be legally attributed without possible intercourse between the spouses.
This is a legal presumption, not merely a factual inference.
4
Apply the ruling
Therefore, the defendant's denial of entry is ineffective. He is muhsan, and the hadd of rajm (stoning) is applied if four witnesses testify for zina.
Other conditions for stoning (free, Muslim, valid marriage) must also be satisfied.
5
Note the additional evidentiary point
The passage also mentions that if he divorces her, he has the right of ruju' (taking back) — this further supports the existence of marital relations.
Ruju' is only possible after consummation in a valid marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا شَهِدَ أَرْبَعَةٌ عَلَى رَجُلٍ بِالزِّنَاءِ فَأَنْكَرَ الْإِحْصَانَ وَلَهُ اِمْرَأَةٌ قَدْ وَلَدَتْ مِنْهُ فَإِنَّهُ يُرْجَمُ مَعْنَاهُ أَنْ يُنْكِرَ الدُّخُولَ بَعْدَ وُجُودِ سَائِرِ الشَّرَائِطِ لِأَنَّ الْحُكْمَ بِثُبُوتِ النَّسَبِ مِنْهُ حُكْمٌ بِالدُّخُولِ عَلَيْهِ وَلِهَذَا لَوْ طَلَّقَهَا يُعَقِّبُ الرَّجْعَةَ وَالْإِحْصَانُ يُثْبَتُ بِمِثْلِهِ
And when four testify against a man for zina, and he denies ihsan, while he has a wife who has given birth from him, then he is stoned. Its meaning is that he denies entry after the existence of all conditions, because the ruling of establishing lineage from him is a ruling of entry upon him. And for this reason, if he divorces her, he may take her back (ruju‘). And ihsan is established by the like of this.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on testimony for zina. The issue is when the accused denies being muhsan (i.e., having had lawful marital intercourse), but the court knows he has a wife and child. The Hanafi position is that the child’s lineage from him establishes that marital intercourse (dukhul) occurred, thus confirming ihsan. The ruling uses logical inference: since the child is legally attributed to him, this implies entry. Therefore, his denial is ineffective. Additionally, if he divorces her, he has the right to take her back (ruju‘), further supporting the existence of marital relations. Ihsan is proven by such circumstantial evidence.

Key Terms
الإحصان (al-iḥṣān): The condition of being married and having had lawful marital intercourse, which makes the penalty for zina stoning (rajm).
ثبوت النسب (thubūt al-nasab): Establishment of lineage; here, the child’s legal attribution to the man proves marital intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He is not stoned because he denies entry.
B) He is stoned because the child proves entry, thus ihsan.
C) He is lashed instead of stoned because of disagreement.
D) The testimony is rejected because of the denial.

Key Takeaway
Childbirth from the wife conclusively establishes marital entry for ihsan, overriding any verbal denial by the accused.

Dispute on Accepting Women's Testimony for Ihsan
Dispute on accepting one man and two women's testimony for ihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school accepts the testimony of one man and two women to prove ihsan and distinguish the positions of al-Shafi‘i and Zufar.

Core Idea
Ihsan is a preventive quality, not a cause of punishment—hence women's testimony is accepted.

This passage addresses a critical dispute in the law of zina: can the condition of ihsan (marital status leading to stoning) be proven by the testimony of one man and two women? The Hanafi school answers yes, while Imam al-Shafi‘i and Hanafi scholar Zufar disagree. Understanding their reasoning is essential for differentiating between a true effective cause (illa) and a mere condition in Hanafi legal theory.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: if one man and two women testify to a defendant's ihsan, he is stoned. Note the practical consequence.
The passage begins with 'فإن لم تكن ولدت منه وشهد عليه بالإحصان رجل وامرأتان رجم'.
2
Identify the opposing positions
Recognize that al-Shafi‘i and Zufar both reject this testimony but on different grounds. Al-Shafi‘i follows a general principle; Zufar uses an analogy.
Al-Shafi‘i's principle: women's testimony only in financial matters. Zufar: ihsan resembles a cause.
3
Follow each opponent's proof
Examine al-Shafi‘i's general rule and Zufar's analogy to a true cause (illa). Zufar argues that ihsan makes the crime more severe, so it resembles the cause of the increased penalty.
Zufar's proof: 'إنه شرط في معنى العلة لأن الجناية تتغلظ عنده'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response defines ihsan as 'commendable qualities' (khisal hamidah) that prevent zina, not a cause. The analogy to the dhimmi witnesses case is distinguished.
The Hanafi proof: 'الإحصان عبارة عن الخصال الحميدة وإنها مانعة من الزناء'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, stoning; under Shafi‘i, lashing or acquittal; under Zufar, no stoning based on that testimony.
This shows why the dispute matters in actual courtroom outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ وَلَدَتْ مِنْهُ وَشَهِدَ عَلَيْهِ بِالْإِحْصَانِ رَجُلٌ وَامْرَأَتَانِ رُجِمَ خِلَافًا لِزُفَرَ وَالشَّافِعِيِّ فَالشَّافِعِيُّ مَرَّ عَلَى أَصْلِهِ أَنَّ شَهَادَتَهُنَّ غَيْرُ مَقْبُولَةٍ فِي غَيْرِ الْأَمْوَالِ وَزُفَرُ يَقُولُ إِنَّهُ شَرْطٌ فِي مَعْنَى الْعِلَّةِ لِأَنَّ الْجِنَايَةَ تَتَقَلَّظُ عِنْدَهُ فَيُضَافُ الْحُكْمُ إِلَيْهِ فَأَشْبَهَ حَقِيقَةَ الْعِلَّةِ فَلَا تُقْبَلُ شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ فِيهِ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا شَهِدَ ذِمِّيَّانِ عَلَى ذِمِّيٍّ زَنَى عَبْدُهُ الْمُسْلِمَ إِنَّهُ أَعْتَقَهُ قَبْلَ الزِّنَاءِ فَلَا تُقْبَلُ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْإِحْصَانَ عِبَارَةٌ عَنِ الْخِصَالِ الْحَمِيدَةِ وَإِنَّهَا مَانِعَةٌ مِّنَ الزِّنَاءِ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَا فَلَا يَكُونُ فِي مَعْنَى الْعِلَّةِ وَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا شَهِدُوا بِهِ فِي غَيْرِ هَذِهِ الْحَالَةِ بِخِلَافِ مَا ذُكِرَ لِأَنَّ الْعِتْقَ يَثْبُتُ بِشَهَادَتِهِمَا وَإِنَّمَا لَا يَثْبُتُ بِسَبْقِ التَّارِيخِ لِأَنَّ الْمُسْلِمَ يُنْكِرُهُ أَوْ يَتَضَرَّرُ بِهِ الْمُسْلِمُ
If she has not given birth from him, and a man and two women testify against him about ihsan, he is stoned, contrary to Zufar and al-Shafi‘i. Al-Shafi‘i follows his principle that their testimony is not accepted in other than financial matters. Zufar says that ihsan is a condition in the sense of a cause, because the crime becomes more severe with it, so the ruling is attributed to it, thus it resembles a true cause, so women’s testimony is not accepted in it. It becomes like when two dhimmis testify against a dhimmi whose Muslim slave committed zina, that he freed him before the zina—it is not accepted for what we mentioned. And our proof: ihsan is a term for commendable qualities, and they prevent zina as we mentioned, so it is not in the sense of a cause. It becomes like when they testify about it in other than this situation. Contrary to what was mentioned, because emancipation is established by their testimony; it is only not established regarding the precedence of the date because the Muslim denies it or the Muslim would be harmed by it.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on accepting the testimony of one man and two women to prove ihsan for the penalty of stoning. The Hanafi position is that ihsan can be proven by such testimony, contrary to Imam al-Shafi‘i and Imam Zufar. Al-Shafi‘i holds that women’s testimony is only accepted in financial matters, not in criminal cases like zina. Zufar argues that ihsan is like a cause (illa) for the increased punishment, resembling the actual zina itself, so women’s testimony is excluded. The Hanafi response is that ihsan is not a cause but a description of good qualities that deter zina; hence it is akin to other matters where women’s testimony is accepted. The example of the dhimmi witnesses is distinguished because it involves a Muslim’s right and potential harm.

Key Terms
الإحصان (al-iḥṣān): The condition of being married and having consummated the marriage, making the zina penalty stoning.
علة (ʿillah): Effective cause; here debated whether ihsan is like a true cause of punishment or merely a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the testimony of one man and two women accepted to prove ihsan?
A) Because ihsan is a cause (illa) for stoning.
B) Because ihsan is a collection of good qualities that prevent zina, not a cause.
C) Because women can testify in all hudud cases.
D) Because the defendant consented.

Key Takeaway
Women's testimony is accepted for ihsan because ihsan is a condition, not a cause; the Hanafi view is followed in practice.

Liability of Ihsan Witnesses upon Retraction
Ruling on liability of retracting ihsan witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the liability of ihsan witnesses who retract, identify the opposing view of Imam Zufar, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Ihsan witnesses are not liable upon retraction because their testimony only affects punishment, not the act itself.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding witnesses who testify to a person's ihsan (marital status required for stoning) and then retract their testimony. The school's majority, including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, rule that such witnesses are not liable for damages. Imam Zufar holds the opposite view. The core issue is whether ihsan testimony is direct or indirect regarding the hadd punishment.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
Identify the ruling and the imams who hold it: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The ruling is that retracting ihsan witnesses are not liable (la yadmanun).
The text says 'indana' indicating the relied-upon position of the school.
2
Identify the opponent and his view
Imam Zufar holds that such witnesses are liable (yadmanun). This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
Zufar was a student of Abu Hanifa but differed on some issues.
3
Analyze the basis of the majority view
The majority view rests on the fact that ihsan testimony does not directly cause the hadd penalty; it only affects the severity of punishment (stoning vs. lashing). The direct cause is testimony on the act of zina itself.
If witnesses retract regarding the act of zina, they may be liable. That case is distinguished.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if ihsan witnesses retract, under the majority they are not liable for blood money or damages; under Zufar, they would be liable.
This affects whether the witnesses face financial consequences or not.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi is the majority position: no liability. The text's phrasing 'indana' and the rejection of Zufar's view indicate this is the operative ruling for fatwa.
Authority weight: zahir riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ رَجَعَ شُهُودُ الْإِحْصَانِ لَا يَضْمَنُونَ عِنْدَنَا خِلَافًا لِزُفَرَ رَجْعًا لِمَا تَقَدَّمَ
If the witnesses of ihsan retract, they are not liable for damages in our view, contrary to Zufar, as a return to what preceded.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and Imam Zufar on the liability of witnesses who testify to ihsan and then retract their testimony. The Hanafi position is that such witnesses are not liable to pay any blood money or damages. This is because ihsan testimony only affects the severity of punishment; it is not direct testimony on the act of zina itself. Imam Zufar holds that they are liable. The phrase 'as a return to what preceded' refers to the earlier disagreement on the nature of ihsan testimony.

Key Terms
رجع (rajaʿa): To retract testimony; the witnesses withdraw their statement about ihsan.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to pay compensation; here debated whether witnesses must pay blood money or damages.
إحصان (iḥṣān): The condition of being married and free (or Muslim) that makes a person liable to stoning for zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) They are not liable.
C) They are stoned in turn.
D) They are imprisoned for false testimony.

Key Takeaway
Ihsan witnesses are not liable upon retraction because their testimony only indirectly affects the punishment, distinguishing it from testimony on the act of zina.

Establishing the Hadd for Drinking Wine
Ruling on when the hadd for drinking is applied

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for applying the hadd for drinking wine and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
The hadd is applied when the crime is evident — smell or intoxication — and the proof is the Prophet's command to flog.

This passage from Al-Hidayah outlines the conditions for applying the fixed punishment (hadd) for consuming wine. It clarifies that the penalty is not dependent on catching the person in the act, but on clear evidence such as the smell of wine or visible intoxication. The primary source is a direct command from the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is drinking wine (khamr). The ruling is that the hadd (flogging) is wajib upon proof.
2
Locate the conditions for proof
The text gives two scenarios: being caught with the smell of wine, or being brought while drunk. Also, confession while the smell is present suffices.
The common element is the freshness of evidence.
3
Understand the rationale
The reason is that the crime is evident and the time is not remote, so there is no doubt.
This prevents punishment based on stale evidence.
4
Examine the evidence
The Prophet (S) said: 'Whoever drinks wine, flog him; if he returns, flog him.' This is a direct command.
The imperative form indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
5
Apply the ruling
If a person is brought to the judge with the smell of wine, the hadd is applied. If the smell is gone, there is a need for other proof.
The hadd is not applied if evidence is weak or uncertain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ حَدِّ الشُّرْبِ. مَنْ شَرِبَ الْخَمْرَ فَأُخِذَ وَرِيحُهَا مَوْجُودَةٌ أَوْ جَاءَ بِهِ سَكْرَانَ فَشَهِدَ الشُّهُودُ عَلَيْهِ بِذَلِكَ فَعَلَيْهِ الْحَدُّ وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا أَقَرَّ وَرِيحُهَا مَوْجُودَةً لِأَنَّ جِنَايَةَ الشُّرْبِ قَدْ ظَهَرَتْ وَلَمْ يَتَقَادَمِ الْعَهْدُ وَالْأَصْلُ فِيهِ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: «وَمَنْ شَرِبَ الْخَمْرَ فَاجْلِدُوهُ فَإِنْ عَادَ فَاجْلِدُوهُ»
Chapter of the penalty for drinking. Whoever drinks wine, and is caught while its smell is still present, or is brought while drunk, and the witnesses testify to that, then the penalty is upon him. Similarly, if he confesses while its smell is present, because the crime of drinking has appeared and the time has not become distant. The basis for it is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever drinks wine, flog him; if he returns, flog him.'
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on the hadd for drinking (shurb). It states the conditions for establishing the penalty of flogging for drinking wine (khamr). The penalty is enforced if the accused is caught with the smell of wine in his mouth or is brought to the judge while still intoxicated. Testimony of witnesses or confession while the smell is present is sufficient. The reason is that the crime (jinayah) of drinking is evident and the time is not remote, so there is no doubt about its occurrence. The primary proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanding flogging for the drinker and repeating it upon relapse. This is a direct textual proof (dalil naqli) from the Sunnah.

Key Terms
الخمر (al-khamr): Wine; intoxicating beverage made from grapes (or generally any intoxicant, but here specifically khamr).
الحد (al-ḥadd): The fixed corporal punishment (flogging) for drinking wine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The person must be caught in the act of drinking.
B) The smell of wine or intoxication must be present when caught or brought.
C) The person must confess twice.
D) The person must be a repeat offender.

Key Takeaway
The hadd for drinking wine is established when the crime is evident through smell or intoxication at the time of capture or confession, based on the Prophet's command.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Hadd After Smell of Wine Disappears
Intra-Hanafi dispute on evidential value of wine smell for hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the hadd for drinking is established after the smell disappears, apply the mufta bihi position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and evaluate the evidentiary basis of the disagreement.

Core Idea
The hadd for drinking requires the smell of wine to be present; its absence creates doubt that prevents punishment.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the application of the hadd (fixed punishment) for drinking wine. The central question is whether the punishment can be imposed after the smell of wine has vanished, whether through confession or testimony. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the smell must be present, while Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees. Understanding this dispute is essential for grasping how Hanafi jurists balance textual evidence (the practice of Ibn Mas'ud) and analogical reasoning (qiyas).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine what exactly is being disputed: the requirement of the smell of wine for establishing the hadd, covering both confession and testimony scenarios.
The smell is seen as the primary trace of recent consumption.
2
Present the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
State that the two imams condition the hadd on the presence of the smell. Their evidence includes the statement of Ibn Mas'ud and the Consensus (ijma) of the Companions. They argue that the smell is the strongest indicator and that distinguishing smells is possible for experts.
They do not reject confession or testimony entirely, but condition their acceptance on the existence of the smell.
3
Outline Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad holds that the hadd can be applied even after the smell disappears. He analogizes with the hadd for zina, where time does not invalidate proof. He measures the delay by a fixed time, not by the persistence of the smell.
He also notes that the smell could come from other sources (e.g., quince), so it is not definitive.
4
Compare the proofs and responses
Analyze the dalil of each side. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rely on naqli (text) and ijma; Muhammad uses qiyas. The Hanafi response rejects the analogy because hadd shurb has a specific textual condition (smell) unlike zina, and the presence of the smell is direct evidence while its absence raises doubt (shubha).
The hadd is lifted in cases of doubt.
5
Identify the thamarah and mufta bihi
The practical difference: if a person confesses after the smell is gone, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf do not apply hadd (only tazir), while Muhammad applies hadd. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the two imams, as reflected in al-Hidayah and later fatwa works.
This is the operative fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن أقر بعد ذهاب رائحتها لم يحد عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وقال محمد يحد. وكذلك إذا شهدوا عليه بعد ما ذهب ريحها عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وقال محمد يحد. فالتقادم يمنع قبول الشهادة بالاتفاق غير أنه مقدر بالزمان عنده اعتبار حد الزناء. وهذا لأن التأخر يتحقق بمضي الزمان والرائحة قد تكون من غيره كما قيل: يقولون لي إنكه شربت مدامة: فقلت لهم: لا بل أكلت السفرجلا. وعندهما يقدر بزوال الرائحة لقول ابن مسعود فيه: "فإن وجدتم رائحة الخمر فاجلدوه" ولأن قيام الأثر من أقوى دلالة على الشرب وإنما يصار إلى التقدير بالزمان عند تعذر اعتباره والتمييز بين الروائح ممكن للمستدل وإنما يشتيه على الجهال. وأما الإقرار فالتقادم لا يبطله عند محمد كما في حد الزناء على ما مر تقريره. وعندهما لا يقام لحد إلا عند قيام الرائحة لأن حد الشرب ثبت بإجماع الصحابة ولا إجماع إلا برأي ابن مسعود وقد شرط قيام الرائحة على ما روينا.
If he confesses after the disappearance of its smell, he is not punished according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said: he is punished. Likewise, if they testify against him after its smell has gone, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (no punishment), and Muhammad said: he is punished. So passage of time prevents acceptance of testimony by agreement, but according to him (Muhammad) it is measured by time, in consideration of the punishment for zina. This is because delay is realized by the passage of time, and the smell may come from something else, as it is said: 'They say to me: you drank wine; I said to them: no, I ate quince.' And according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), it is measured by the disappearance of the smell due to the statement of Ibn Mas'ud: 'If you find the smell of wine, then flog him.' And because the presence of the trace is the strongest indication of drinking, and recourse to estimation by time is only when consideration of the trace is impossible, and distinguishing between smells is possible for the expert, and it is only confusing for the ignorant. As for confession, passage of time does not invalidate it according to Muhammad, as in the hadd of zina as previously explained. And according to the two, the hadd is not established except when the smell is present, because the hadd of drinking is established by the consensus of the Companions, and there is no consensus except through the opinion of Ibn Mas'ud, and he conditioned the presence of the smell as we have narrated.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding whether the hadd punishment for drinking wine can be imposed after the smell of the wine has disappeared. The dispute covers two scenarios: (1) the offender confesses after the smell is gone, and (2) witnesses testify after the smell is gone. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the hadd is not applied in either case because the trace (the smell) is the primary evidence of recent drinking. They rely on the statement of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) who conditioned the hadd on finding the smell. They also argue that the smell could come from other sources (like eating quince), so it must be present to confirm the act. Imam Muhammad, on the other hand, considers that the hadd can still be applied even after the smell disappears, by analogy with the hadd for zina, where time does not invalidate a confession. He measures the delay by time, not by the persistence of the smell. He argues that the smell is not the only indicator; other evidence can suffice. However, all three agree that if a significant amount of time has passed such that the act is no longer fresh, testimony is not accepted. The point of contention is the criterion: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the smell is the standard; Muhammad says a fixed time period (like in zina) should be used. The author of al-Hidayah (and the commentator) clarifies that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the view of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) because it is based on the direct practice of the Companion Ibn Mas'ud and the consensus of the Companions (ijma' al-sahabah). The fact that distinguishing smells is possible for experts strengthens their position. Thus, in practice, the hadd for drinking is only applied when the smell of wine is present at the time of confession or testimony.

Key Terms
التقادم (al-taqāddum): The passage of time; in this context, the time elapsed between the act of drinking and the confession or testimony.
الرائحة (al-rā'iḥah): The smell of wine on the breath; used as evidence of recent consumption.
الإقرار (al-iqrār): Confession; the accused admits to drinking wine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what happens if a person confesses to drinking wine after the smell has completely disappeared?
A) The hadd is applied because confession alone suffices.
B) The hadd is not applied because the smell is absent.
C) The hadd is applied only if witnesses also testify.
D) The person is given tazir but not hadd.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the fixed punishment for drinking wine is only applied when the smell of wine is present at the time of confession or testimony; its absence repels the hadd due to doubt.
