Hadd for Drinking Wine: No Intoxication Required, Fourth Time Killing for Istihlal Only
Explains the hadd for drinking wine, condition of intoxication, and fourth-time ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the hadd of drinking wine and explain why intoxication is not a condition, and why the fourth-time killing is reserved for those who consider wine halal.

Core Idea
Even a single drop of wine incurs the hadd; intoxication is not a condition.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the hadd (fixed punishment) for drinking wine. The key question is whether intoxication is necessary for the punishment to apply. The text clarifies that any amount, even a drop, suffices, and then addresses the controversial fourth-time offence, concluding that killing is only for those who consider wine lawful.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Identify that the act is drinking wine (khamr) and the ruling is that the hadd (flogging) is wajib. Note that intoxication is not required; a single drop triggers the hadd.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited: 'Whoever drinks wine, flog him; if he drinks again, flog him; third time, flog; fourth time, kill him.' This is from multiple narrators.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith is interpreted. The imperative 'iqtuluhu' (kill him) is taken as a general command, but it is restricted by other narrations and consensus to mean only when the drinker considers wine halal.
The Hanafi school limits the literal meaning using takhsis (specification) based on supporting evidence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and consensus
Recognize that there is no inter-madhhab dispute here; the text states that early and later scholars (salaf and khalaf) agreed that the fourth-time killing only applies for istihlal (deeming it halal).
The consensus (ijma) overrides the apparent meaning of the hadith.
5
List the conditions for enforcement
Extract the conditions: the drinker must be Muslim, sane, adult, not mute, voluntary, knowing the prohibition, and the drink must be khamr or another unanimously prohibited intoxicant; for khamr, any amount suffices; for other intoxicants, intoxication is required. Also, the smell of wine should not have disappeared (no delay).
Conditions for enforcement include timeliness (smell present).

Chapter on the Hadd of Drinking Ashraf al-Hidayah: An Urdu Commentary on Hidayah, Volume 6. If he confesses and the smell is still in his mouth, then too the same ruling applies, because by this the crime of drinking wine is established, and there is no delay in time. (In drinking wine, intoxication is not a condition. Rather, if a person drinks even a single drop, he will also be given the hadd.) The basic proof for carrying out this hadd is the hadith that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Whoever drinks wine, flog him; then if he drinks again, flog him again; if he drinks a third time, flog him; then if he drinks a fourth time, kill him.' This was narrated by Ibn Hibban, Hakim, Shafi'i, Darimi, Abu Dawud, Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah. In this, killing on the fourth time is interpreted to mean that he does not believe in the prohibition of wine, i.e., he considers it lawful. As is clear in Ibn Hibban's narration. And a similar marfu' narration from Mu'awiyah is reported by Ahmad and the Sunan al-Arba'ah. And in the hadith of Abu Sa'id, from the narration of Ibn Hibban and Ibn Abi Shaybah, and in the hadith of Ibn 'Umar from the narration of Abu Dawud and Nasa'i, and in the hadith of Jabir, it is mentioned that a person was brought who had drunk wine a fourth time, and the Messenger of Allah flogged him and did not kill him. Nasa'i and Bazzar narrated it, and the same is mentioned in the hadith of Qabisah ibn Dhu'ayb (narrated by Abu Dawud). The conclusion is that the early and later scholars are all agreed that no one is killed for drinking wine a fourth time except the person who drinks it considering it lawful. Then he will be killed on the basis of apostasy. Then it should be known that the hadd for drinking wine is applied only to a Muslim, provided he is sane and adult, not mute, without compulsion, he drinks voluntarily, even if it is a single drop, or other types of wine whose prohibition all scholars have agreed upon. He should have drunk enough to cause intoxication, provided he knows it is prohibited, whether by reading the Quran and hadith or by being present in Dar al-Islam. Then he will be given the hadd, provided that there is not much delay, and by delay in this drinking it is meant that the smell has disappeared. (Commentator's note: He says that it is difficult for a single drop to produce a smell, so one should seek to understand.)
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the hadd for drinking wine. The text first clarifies that intoxication is not a condition; even a single drop triggers the hadd. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanding flogging for the first three times and killing for the fourth. However, the author interprets the fourth-time killing as specific to one who regards wine as lawful, based on other narrations and the consensus of scholars that otherwise the fourth-time drinker is only flogged. The passage then lists the conditions for the hadd: the drinker must be Muslim, sane, adult, not mute, drinking voluntarily, knowing the prohibition, and the drink must be a proven intoxicant. The delay in enforcement is measured by the disappearance of the smell, a point developed later. The commentator adds that a single drop may not produce a detectable smell, so understanding is needed.

Key Terms
حد الشرب (hadd al-shurb): The fixed corporal punishment for drinking wine, specifically flogging (jald).
خمر (khamr): Wine or any intoxicating drink made from grapes.
استحلال (istihlal): Regarding something forbidden as lawful; here, considering wine halal, which leads to apostasy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Hadd al-shurb is wajib for even a drop of khamr, and the fourth-time killing applies only to those who consider wine halal.

The Condition of Smell for Hadd on Drinking Wine: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the condition of smell for hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the requirement of smell for enforcing hadd, and explain the reasoning behind each position, particularly regarding confession and testimony.

Core Idea
The presence of the smell of wine is essential for enforcing hadd according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; Imam Muhammad disagrees.

This passage examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the enforcement of the fixed punishment (hadd) for drinking wine. When a person confesses or witnesses testify after the smell of wine from the mouth has disappeared, does the hadd still apply? The great Imams of the school differ, with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf conditioning the punishment on the smell being present, while Imam Muhammad does not require it, drawing an analogy to the hadd for fornication. Understanding this dispute sharpens one's ability to assess evidence in hudud cases and appreciate how Hanafi jurists balance textual proof and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The dispute is whether the disappearance of the smell after drinking invalidates the application of hadd. The text presents two scenarios: confession (iqrar) and testimony (shahadah).
2
State the positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: no hadd after smell disappears. Imam Muhammad: hadd is applied. This holds for both confession and testimony.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi; both sides are respected.
3
Analyze the dalil for each side
For Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf: the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'If you find the smell of wine, then flog him.' They argue that the presence of the effect (smell) is the strongest evidence of drinking. For Muhammad: analogy to zina – delay is measured by time (one month) because smell could come from other sources.
The poetic verse illustrates that smell can be mistaken, but experts can distinguish.
4
Apply to the two scenarios
For testimony, both sides agree that delay prevents acceptance, but they differ on measurement: Muhammad uses fixed time; Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf use disappearance of smell. For confession, Muhammad does not require smell; Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf do, based on the same narration.
The consensus of the Companions is cited, especially the view of Ibn Mas'ud.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text indicates the preferred (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: hadd is not enforced after the smell disappears. This is supported by the rigor of the evidence and the practice of the Companions.
Later Hanafi authorities have relied on this view.

Source Text

منہ سے بو ختم ہونے کے بعد اقرار کیا تب بھی حد نہیں لگائی جائے گی
فَإِنْ أَقَرَّ بَعْدَ ذِهَابِ رَائِحَتِهَا لَمْ يُحَدَّ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ وَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ يُحَدُّ وَ كَذَلِكَ إِذَا شَهِدُوا عَلَيْهِ بَعْدَ مَا ذَهَبَ رِيْحُهَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ يُحَدُّ فَالتَّقَادُمُ يَمْنَعُ قُبُولَ الشَّهَادَةِ بِالْاِتِّفَاقِ غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ مُقَدَّرٌ بِالزَّمَانِ عِنْدَهُ اعْتِبَاراً بِحَدِ الزَّنَاءِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ التَّاخِيرَ يَتَحَقَّقُ بِمُضِيِّ الزَّمَانِ وَالرَّائِحَةُ قَدْ تَكُونُ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ كَمَا قِيلَ شَعَرٍ: يَقُولُونَ لِي انْكَهْ شَرِبَتْ مُدَامَةً فَقُلْتُ لَهُمْ لَا بَلْ أَكَلْتُ السَّفَرْجَلَا وَعِنْدَهُمَا يُقَدَّرُ بِزَوَالِ الرَّائِحَةِ لِقَوْلِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ فِيهِ: فَإِنْ وَجَدْتُمْ رَائِحَةَ الْخَمْرِ فَاجْلِدُوهُ وَلِأَنَّ قِيَامَ الْأَثَرِ مِنْ أَقْوَى دَلَالَةً عَلَى الشُّرْبِ وَ إِنَّمَا يُصَارُ إِلَى التَّقْدِيرِ بِالزَّمَانِ عِنْدَ تَعَذُّرِ اعْتِبَارِهِ وَالتَّمْيِيزُ بَيْنَ الرَّوَائِحِ مُمْكِنٌ لِلْمُسْتَدِلِّ وَ إِنَّمَا يَشْتَبِهُ عَلَى الْجُهَّالِ وَأَمَّا الْإِقْرَارُ فَالتَّقَادُمُ لَا يُبْطِلُهُ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ كَمَا فِي حَدِّ الزِّنَاءِ عَلَى مَا مَرَّ تَقْرِيرُهُ وَعِنْدَهُمَا لَا يُقَامُ الْحَدُّ إِلَّا عِنْدَ قِيَامِ الرَّائِحَةِ لِأَنَّ حَدَّ الشُّرْبِ ثَبَتَ بِإِجْمَاعِ الصَّحَابَةِ وَلَا إِجْمَاعَ إِلَّا بِرَأْيِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ وَقَدْ شَرَطَ قِيَامَ الرَّائِحَةِ عَلَى مَا رَوَيْنَا
ترجمہ: اور اگر منہ سے بدبو ختم ہو جانے کے بعد اس نے اقرار کیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ اور ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ کے نزدیک اسے حد نہیں لگائی جائے گی اور امام محمد رحمہ اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ حد لگائی جائے گی۔ اسی طرح اگر گواہوں نے بدبو ختم ہو جانے کے بعد گواہی دی تو بھی امام ابو حنیفہ اور ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہما کے نزدیک یہی حکم ہے کہ حد نہیں لگائی جائے گی اور امام محمد کے نزدیک حد لگائی جائے گی۔ پس یہ معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ دیر ہونے سے بالاتفاق گواہی قبول نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ لیکن اتنا فرق ہے کہ امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ کے نزدیک دیر ہو جانے کا زمانہ حد زنا پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے ایک ماہ ہے۔ کیونکہ زمانہ گزرنے سے ہی تاخیر ہوتی ہے اور بدبو تو شراب کے سوا کسی دوسری چیز سے بھی ہو سکتی ہے۔ جیسا کہ کسی شاعر نے کہا ہے۔ شعر: مجھ سے کہتے ہیں تو نے پی شراب میں یہ کہتا ہوں بلکہ سیب ناب۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ وابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہما کے نزدیک دیر ہونے کا اندازہ صرف بدبو زائل ہونے سے ہے۔ اس لئے کہ حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ نے اس کے متعلق فرمایا ہے کہ اگر تم شراب کی بدبو پاؤ تو اسے درے مارو (اس کی روایت الحاکم و طبرانی و عبدالرزاق اور ابو یعلی نے بھی اس کے مثل کی ہے اور یہی مفہوم صحیحین کی روایت میں بھی ہے) اور اس لئے بھی کہ شراب کا اثر یعنی بدبو باقی ہونا شراب پینے کی سب سے بڑی دلیل ہے اور زمانہ کے ساتھ اسی وقت اندازہ ہو گا جب کہ اس کے اثر سے اندازہ ممکن نہ ہو اور سیب وشراب وغیرہ کی بو میں فرق کرنا پہچاننے والے کے لئے ممکن ہے البتہ جاہلوں کو اشتباہ ہو جاتا ہے اور یہ بات کہ شراب پینے کا اگر خود اقرار کیا ہو تو اس میں تاخیر ہو جانے سے امام محمد کے نزدیک حد باطل نہیں ہوتی ہے جیسے کہ حد زنا میں ہے (جیسا کہ اس کی توضیح اوپر بیان کی جاچکی ہے) اور امام ابوحنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک حد قائم نہیں کی جائے گی مگر اس صورت میں کہ بدبو موجود ہو۔ کیونکہ شراب پینے پر حد جاری ہونے کے حکم کا ثبوت صحابہ کرام کے اجماع سے ہے اور اجماع اس وقت مکمل ہوگا کہ اس میں جلیل القدر صحابی یعنی حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ کی رائے بھی شامل ہو اور جیسا کہ ہم نے اوپر میں یہ روایت کر دی ہے کہ حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ نے بدبو کے موجود ہونے کو حد قائم کرانے کے لئے شرط کیا ہے۔
تشریح: وقد شرط قيام الرائحة على ما روينا. حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود کی روایت سے معلوم ہوا ہے کہ شراب پینے والے پر حد جاری کرنے کے لئے اس کے منہ سے شراب کی بو کا نکلنا شرط ہے۔ ف۔ واضح ہو کہ شیخ ابن الہام رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے حضرت عبد اللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ کے آثار سے بدبو کے موجود ہونے کی شرط میں کلام کیا ہے۔ چنانچہ ان روایتوں کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ حضرت ابن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ نے ایک شخص سے شراب کی بدبو پا کر فرمایا کہ کیا تم شراب پیتے ہو اور قرآن انہی کو جھٹلاتے ہو (اس کی نافرمانی کرتے ہو) یہ کہہ کر اسے حد ماری۔ (رواہ البخاری ومسلم) اور دوسری روایت میں ہے کہ ایک شخص نے اپنے بھتیجے کو نشہ کی حالت میں حضرت ابن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ کے سامنے پیش کیا تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ اس کو سونگھو۔ تب لوگوں نے اسے سونگھ کر منہ سے بدبو پائی۔ پس آپ نے اسے قید خانہ میں بھیج دیا۔ دوسرے دن نکال کر اسے درے مارے۔ حالانکہ اس کی سند میں بشر الجابر ہیں جن کے بارے میں کلام کیا گیا ہے لیکن ترندی نے ان کو ثقہ کہا ہے اور دوسرے راوی ابو ماجد اشعری ہیں جن کے بارے میں کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ مجہول ہیں یعنی ان کا کوئی حال معلوم نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ رندی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے نقل کیا ہے کہ بشر الجابر سے پوچھا گیا کہ ابو ماجد کون شخص ہیں تو فرمایا کہ ایک چڑیا تھی جو اڑ گئی۔ لوگوں نے اس جملہ کے یہ معنی لئے ہیں کہ ان کا کچھ حال معلوم نہیں ہے۔ لیکن جواہر منیفہ میں حارث کی سند سے بالاسناد نقل کیا ہے کہ سفیان ابن عیینہ نے بشر الجابر سے پوچھا کہ ابو ماجد کون شخص ہیں تو فرمایا کہ یمن سے ایک اعرابی ہمارے یہاں آئے تھے۔ اس بیان سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ امام ترندی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے جو عبارت نقل کی ہے 'ایک چڑیا تھی جو اڑ گئی' یہ برائی کے طور پر نہیں تھی بلکہ مزاح کے طور پر تھی یعنی ہمارے یہاں ایک بزرگ آئے تھے ٹھہرے نہیں بلکہ بہت جلد چلے گئے۔
شعر: يقولون لي انكه شربت مدامة فقلت لهم لابل اكلت السفرجلا. انکہ الفتح سے امر کے وزن پر 'نہ' کے 'سمع' اور فتح سے امر کا صیغہ ہے کسی کا منہ سونگھنا۔ مدامه بضم میم انگوری شراب۔ مقصد شاعر کا یہ ہے کہ لوگ مجھ سے کہتے ہیں کہ نہ سونگھ کر دیکھو کہ اس نے انگوری شراب پی رکھی ہے یا نہیں تو میں نے کہا کہ میں نے وہ شراب نہیں پی ہے بلکہ میں نے ایک پھل کھایا ہے بھی (جو سیب کی مانند ہوتا ہے کابل و کشمیر میں ہوتا ہے)۔ (انوار الحق قاسمی، اکتوبر ۱۹۹۴ء) اور ایک دوسرے نسخہ میں بجائے انکہ کے انگ ہے تو مطلب یہ نہ ہو گا کہ تم نے شراب انگوری پی رکھی ہے تو میں نے کہا کہ نہیں بلکہ ایک پھل
If he confesses after the disappearance of its smell, he is not flogged according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said: He is flogged. Similarly, if they testify against him after its smell has disappeared, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf [the same], and Muhammad said: He is flogged. Delay prevents acceptance of testimony by consensus, except that it is measured by time according to him [Muhammad] by analogy to the hadd of zina. This is because delay is realized by the passage of time, and smell may come from other than it, as was said in poetry: 'They say to me: Smell him, he has drunk wine. So I said to them: No, rather I ate quince.' And according to them [Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf], it is measured by the disappearance of the smell, due to the saying of Ibn Mas'ud concerning it: 'If you find the smell of wine, then flog him.' And because the presence of the effect is the strongest indication of drinking. And one resorts to estimation by time only when consideration of it is impossible. And distinguishing between smells is possible for the one who investigates; it is only confusing for the ignorant. As for confession, delay does not invalidate it according to Muhammad, just as in the hadd of zina, as its explanation has preceded. And according to them, the hadd is not enforced except when the smell is present, because the hadd of drinking is established by the consensus of the Companions, and there is no consensus except with the opinion of Ibn Mas'ud, and he conditioned the presence of the smell as we have narrated. Translation: And if after the smell has left his mouth he confesses, then according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf he is not given the hadd, and Muhammad said that he is given the hadd. Similarly, if the witnesses testify after the smell has disappeared, the same ruling applies: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf the hadd is not given, and according to Muhammad it is given. So it should be known that delay prevents acceptance of testimony by consensus. But there is a difference: according to Muhammad, the time of delay is one month, by analogy to the hadd of zina, because the delay is realized by the passage of time, and the smell could be from something other than wine, as a poet said: 'They say to me you have drunk wine, I say rather I have eaten raw apple.' According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the estimation of delay is only by the disappearance of the smell, because Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said concerning it: 'If you find the smell of wine, then flog him' (narrated by Hakim, Tabarani, Abdurrazzaq, and Abu Ya'la, and the same meaning is in the Sahihain). And also because the presence of the effect, i.e., the smell, is the strongest proof of drinking. And estimation by time is only resorted to when consideration of the effect is impossible. And distinguishing between the smells of apple and wine is possible for one who knows, though it may be confusing for the ignorant. As for the case of confession, according to Muhammad delay does not invalidate it, as in the hadd of zina (as explained earlier). According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the hadd is not enforced except when the smell is present, because the ruling of the hadd for drinking is established by the consensus of the Companions, and the consensus is not complete without including the view of the great Companion Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and as we have narrated, he conditioned the presence of the smell. Commentary: Ibn al-Humam has discussed the condition of the presence of the smell from the narrations of Ibn Mas'ud. The summary of these narrations is that Ibn Mas'ud smelled wine on a person and said, 'Do you drink wine and reject the Quran?' and flogged him (narrated by Bukhari and Muslim). In another narration, a person brought his nephew in a state of intoxication to Ibn Mas'ud, and he said, 'Smell him.' So they smelled him and found the smell of wine from his mouth. Then he sent him to prison. The next day he brought him out and flogged him. However, in its chain is Bishr al-Jabir, who has been criticized. But Turandi said he is trustworthy. The other narrator is Abu Majid al-Ash'ari, who is said to be unknown. Rindi narrated that Bishr was asked about Abu Majid and he said, 'He was a bird that flew away.' This was interpreted to mean he is unknown. But in Jawhar al-Munifah, it is narrated with a chain from Harith that Sufyan ibn Uyaynah asked Bishr about Abu Majid and he said, 'A Bedouin from Yemen came to us.' This indicates that Turandi's statement was not criticism but a jest: 'A bird that flew away' means a great person came but did not stay; he left quickly. The poetic verse: 'They say to me: Smell him, he has drunk wine, so I said to them: No, rather I ate quince.' 'Ankah' is the imperative from 'shamma' meaning 'smell'. 'Madama' is grape wine. The poet's purpose is that people tell him to smell, thinking he has drunk wine, but he says he ate a fruit like an apple. In another version, instead of 'ankah', there is 'ang', meaning 'you have drunk grape wine'; then the meaning is that he denies it.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the enforcement of hadd for drinking wine after the smell has disappeared from the mouth. The text begins by stating the disagreement on two scenarios: confession and testimony. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf hold that if a person confesses after the smell is gone, he is not flogged. Imam Muhammad, however, holds that he is flogged. The same applies to witness testimony. The reasoning follows: For testimony, both sides agree that delay (taqaddum) prevents acceptance, but they differ on how to measure delay. Muhammad measures it by a fixed time (one month), analogizing to the hadd of zina, because delay is measured by time, and the smell could come from other substances like quince. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf measure it by the disappearance of the smell itself, relying on the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'If you find the smell of wine, then flog him.' They argue that the presence of the effect (smell) is the strongest proof of drinking, and only when its consideration is impossible do we resort to time. Experts can distinguish smells; only the ignorant are confused. For confession, Muhammad does not consider delay a barrier, analogizing again to zina. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf require the presence of the smell because the hadd was established by the consensus of the Companions, which includes the opinion of Ibn Mas'ud, who conditioned the hadd on the presence of the smell. The commentary then discusses the authenticity of the narrations from Ibn Mas'ud, citing specific chains and addressing criticisms of the narrator Bishr al-Jabir and Abu Majid. It concludes that the narrations are acceptable, and the condition of smell is established. The poetic verse is explained to illustrate that smell can be mistaken, but in their view, experts can distinguish.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): Confession; the accused's admission of drinking wine.
شهادة (shahadah): Testimony of witnesses; evidence of the crime.
رائحة (ra'ihah): The smell of wine from the mouth, considered a crucial piece of evidence.
تقادم (taqaddum): Delay; the passage of time between the act and the confession or testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the intra-Hanafi dispute, which position is considered the relied-upon (mufta bihi) regarding a confession made after the smell of wine has disappeared?
A) Imam Muhammad's position: the hadd is applied.
B) Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf's position: the hadd is not applied.
C) Both positions are equally valid.
D) The hadd is applied only if witnesses also testify.

Key Takeaway
The hadd for drinking wine requires the presence of the smell of wine, even upon confession, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ḥadd al-Shurb: Delay and Smell
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether delay nullifies ḥadd for drinking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad on the effect of delay on ḥadd al-shurb, apply the condition of smell, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The ḥadd for drinking requires the smell of wine; delay without excuse nullifies the evidence.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a delay in testimony nullifies the ḥadd for drinking if the smell of wine has dissipated. Understanding this dispute requires grasping the evidentiary role of smell and the concept of valid excuse. We will trace the arguments of the three great imams and see how the mufta bihi position balances literal evidence and practical considerations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the controversy
Determine the exact question: Does a delay in reporting the drinking offense nullify the ḥadd if the smell is gone? Note that the disagreement is only about cases without excuse; with excuse, they agree the ḥadd is applied.
The passage first states the dispute, then gives a unanimous case.
2
Contrast the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the smell is essential, so if it dissipates due to time, the ḥadd is not applied. Imam Muhammad: the delay up to one month is acceptable by qiyas to zina.
3
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'If you smell... flog him.' Imam Muhammad relies on analogical reasoning (qiyas) to the penalty for illicit intercourse.
4
Recognize the unanimous exception
If witnesses seize the person while the smell is present or he is intoxicated, and then transport him to the judge over a distance such that the smell dissipates, all agree the ḥadd is applied because the delay had a valid excuse.
This shows that the dispute is only about delay without excuse.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as it is supported by the explicit ḥadīth and the practical difficulty of distinguishing the smell of wine from other substances.
The passage also notes that the smell is the strongest proof.

حنیفہ اور ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہما کے نزدیک یہی حکم ہے کہ حد نہیں لگائی جائے گی اور امام محمد کے نزدیک حد لگائی جائے گی۔ پس یہ معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ دیر ہونے سے بالا تفاق گواہی قبول نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ لیکن اتنا فرق ہے کہ امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ کے نزدیک دیر ہو جانے کا زمانہ حد زنا پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے ایک ماہ ہے۔ کیونکہ زمانہ گزرنے سے ہی تاخیر ہوتی ہے اور بد بو تو شراب کے سوا کسی دوسری چیز سے بھی ہو سکتی ہے۔ جیسا کہ کسی شاعر نے کہا ہے۔ شعر۔ مجھے سے کہتے ہیں تو نے پی شراب۔ میں یہ کہتا ہوں بلکہ سیب ناب۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ وابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہما کے نزدیک دیر ہونے کا اندازہ صرف بد بوز ائل ہونے سے ہے۔ اس لئے کہ حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود ین نے اس کے متعلق فرمایا ہے کہ اگر تم شراب کی بد بو پاؤ تو اسے درے مارو (اس کی روایت الحق و طبرانی و عبدالرزاق اور ابو یعلی نے بھی اس کے مثل کی ہے اور یہی مفہوم صحیحین کی روایت میں بھی ہے ) اور اس لئے بھی کہ شراب کا اثر یعنی بد بو باقی ہونا شراب پینے کی سب سے بڑی دلیل ہے اور زمانہ کے ساتھ اسی وقت اندازہ ہو گا جب کہ اس کے اثر سے اندازہ ممکن نہ ہو اور سیب وشراب وغیرہ کی بو میں فرق کرنا پہچاننے والے کے لئے ممکن ہے البتہ جاہلوں کو اشتباہ ہو جاتا ہے اور یہ بات کہ شراب پینے کا اگر خود اقرار کیا ہو تو اس میں تاخیر ہو جانے سے امام محمد کے نزدیک حد باطل نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ جیسے کہ حد زنا میں ہے (جیسا کہ اس کی توضیح اوپر بیان کی جاچکی ہے ) اور امام ابوحنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک حد قائم نہیں کی جائے گی مگر اس صورت میں کہ بد بو موجود ہوں۔ کیونکہ شراب پینے پر حد جاری ہونے کے حکم کا ثبوت صحابہ کرام کے اجماع سے ہے اور اجماع اس وقت مکمل ہوگا کہ اس میں جلیل القدر صحابی یعنی حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود خانہ کی رائے بھی شامل ہو اور جیسا کہ ہم نے اوپر میں یہ روایت کر دی ہے کہ حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ نے بد بو کے موجود ہونے کو حد قائم کرانے کے لئے شرط کیا ہے۔ تشریح وقد شرط قيام الرائحة على ماروينا “ حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود کی روایت سے معلوم ہوا ہے کہ شراب پینے والے پر حد جاری کرنے کے لئے اس کے منہ سے شراب کی بو کا نکلنا شرط ہے۔ ف۔ واضح ہو کہ شیخ ابن الہام رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے حضرت عبد اللہ بن مسعودۃ الیہ کے آثار سے بدبو کے موجود ہونے کی شرط میں کلام کیا ہے۔ چنانچہ ان روایتوں کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ حضرت ابن مسعودہ پیلے نے ایک شخص سے شراب کی بد بو پا ک فر مایا کہ کیا تم شراب پیتے ہو اور قرآن انہی کو جھٹلاتے ہو (اس کی نافرمانی کرتے ہو ) یہ کہہ کر اسے حد ماری۔ (رواہ البخاری ومسلم ) اور دوسری روایت میں ہے کہ ایک شخص نے اپنے بھتیجے کو نشہ کی حالت میں حضرت ابن مسعودؓ کے سامنے پیش کیا تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ اس کو سو گھو۔ تب لوگوں نے اسے سونگھ کر منہ سے بدبو پائی ۔ پس آپ نے اسے قید خانہ میں بھیج دیا۔ دوسرے دن نکلوا کر اسے دورے مارے۔ حالانکہ اس کی سند میں بیچی الجابر ہیں جن کے بارے میں کلام کیا گیا ہے لیکن ترندی نے ان کو ثقہ کہا ہے اور دوسرے راوی ابو ماجد اشفی ہیں۔ جن کے بارے میں کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ مجہول ہیں یعنی ان کا کوئی حال معلوم نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ رندی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے نقل کیا ہے کہ بیٹی الجاہر سے پوچھا گیا کہ ابو ماجدکون شخص ہیں تو فرمایا کہ ایک چڑیا تھی جو اڑ گئی۔ لوگوں نے اس جملہ کے یہ معنی لئے ہیں کہ ان کا کچھ حال معلوم نہیں ہے۔ لیکن جواہر منیفہ میں حارث کی سند سے بالا سنا نقل کیا ہے کہ سفیان ابن عیینہ نے بیچی الجابر سے پوچھا کہ ابو ماجد کون شخص ہیں تو فرمایا کہ یمن سے ایک اعرابی ہمارے یہاں آئے تھے۔ اس بیان سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ امام ترندی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے جو عبارت نقل کی ہے۔ ایک چڑیا تھی جواڑ گئی یہ برائی کے طور پر نہیں تھی بلکہ مدرح کے طور پر تھی ۔ یعنی ہمارے یہاں ایک بزرگ آئے تھے ٹھہرے نہیں۔ بلکہ بہت جلد چلے گئے۔
شعر يقولون لي انكه شربت مدامة فقلت لهـم لابــل اكـلـت السفرجلا انکہ الفتح سے امر کے وزن پر نہ کے سمع اور فتح سے امر کا صیغہ ہے۔ کسی کا منہ سونگھنا۔ مدامه بضم میم ۔ انگوری شراب۔ مقصد شاعر کا یہ ہے کہ لوگ مجھ سے کہتے ہیں کہ نہ سونگھ کردیکھو کہ اس نے انگوری شراب پی رکھی ہے یا نہیں تو میں نے کہا کہ میں نے وہ شراب نہیں پی ہے بلکہ میں نے ایک پھل کھایا ہے بھی (جو سیب کی مانند ہوتا ہے کابل و کشمیر میں ہوتا ہے)۔ (انوار الحق قاسمی ، اکتوبر ۱۹۹۴ء ) اور ایک دوسرے نسخہ میں بجائے انکہ کے انگ ہے تو مطلب یہ نہ ہو گا کہ تم نے شراب انگوری پی رکھی ہے تو میں نے کہا کہ نہیں بلکہ ایک پھل ( سیب کی طرح) کا بھی کھایا ہے۔
باب حد الشرف
گواہوں نے منہ سے بو آنے کی حالت میں پکڑا یا نشہ کی حالت میں پکڑا پھر امام کے شہر کی طرف لے کر بڑھے دوری کی وجہ سے بوزائل ہو گئی تو حد لگائی جائے گی
فَإِنْ أَخَذَهُ الشُّهُودُوَرِيْحُهَا يُوجَدُ مِنْهُ اَوْ هُوَ سَكْرَاتُ فَذَهَبُوابِهِ مِنْ مِصْرٍ إِلى مِصْرِفِيهِ الْإِمَامُ فَانْقَطَعَ ذَالِكَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَنتَهُوا بِهِ حُدَّ فِي قَوْلِهِمْ جَمِيعًا لِاَنَّ هَذَا عُذْرٌ كَبُعْدِ الْمُسَافَةِ فِي حَدِ الزَّنَاءِ وَ الشَّاهِدُ لَا يُتَهَمُ بِهِ فِي مِثْلِهِ وَمَنْ سَكَرَمِنَ النَّبِيدِ حُدَّ لِمَارُوِيَ أَنَّ عُمَرَ أَقَامَ الْحَدَّ عَلَى اعْرَابِي سَكَرَمِنَ النَّبِيْدِ وَنُبَيِّنَ الْكَلَامَ فِي حَدِ السَّكْرِ وَ مِقْدَارُ حَدِهِ الْمُسْتَحَق عَلَيْهِ إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ تَعَالَى
ترجمہ اگر پینے والے کو گواہوں نے اس حال میں پکڑا کہ اس کے منہ سے بدبو پائی جارہی تھی ۔ یا نشہ میں مست تھا۔ پھر وہ لوگ اسے لے کر اس شہر سے لے کر اس دوسرے شہر میں گئے ، جہاں امام موجود ہے اور وہاں پہنچنے تک اس کے منہ کی بد بوختم ہوگئی (یا اس کا نشہ ختم ہو گیا) تو بالاتفاق تمام علماء کے نزدیک اسے حد لگائی جائے گی۔ اس لئے کہ یہ تا خیر عذر کے ساتھ ہے۔ جیسے حد نا کی صورت میں راستہ کے دوری کی وجہ سے گواہی میں دیر ہو جانے کی بناء پر کہ اس جیسی صورت میں گواہوں کو متہم نہیں کیا جاتا۔ اور وہ شخص جو نبیذ پینے کی وجہ سے نشہ میں مست ہو جائے تو اس پر حد جاری کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ دارقطنی نے اپنی سنن میں روایت کی ہے کہ حضرت عمر نے ایک ایسے شخص کو حد لگائی جو نبیذ پینے کی وجہ سے نشہ میں تھا۔ انشاء اللہ تعالے ہم آئندہ نشہ کی حد اور کتنی مقدار پینے سے آدمی حد کا مستحق ہوتا ہے بیان کریں گے۔
تشريح .. فان اخذه الشهودو ريحها يوجد منه اوهو سكران فذهبوابه من مصر الى ... الخ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص کو گواہان گرفتار کر کے لے آئے اس حال میں کہ اس کے منہ سے شراب کی بو آرہی ہو یا وہ نشہ کی حالت میں ہو ۔ پھر اسے ایک شہر سے دوسرے میں اس لئے منتقل کیا جائے کہ قاضی وہاں (دوسرے شہر میں) رہتا ہے چنانچہ مسافت کی دوری کے باعث اس ( شرابی ) کے منہ سے شراب کی بویا شراب کا نشہ کا فور ہو گیا تو اس صورت میں تمام ائمہ کے قول کے مطابق ( بالا جماع ) حد جاری ہوگی۔ کیونکہ فاصلہ دور ہونے کی وجہ سے عذر موجود ہے۔ جیسا کہ حد زناء میں فاصلہ دور ہونے کی وجہ سے گواہی میں تاخیر سے گواہوں کو مورد الزام نہیں ٹھہرایا جاتا ۔ اسی طرح فاصلہ میں بعد ( دوری) بھی بو کے زوال یا انقطاع نشہ کو قابل عذر قرار دیتے ہوئے اقامت حد کو برقرار رکھا جائے گا۔ اقامت حد کے حوالے سے تاخیر کا اصول یہ ہے کہ وہ ( تاخیر ) بلا عذر ہو۔ اگر اس ( تاخیر ) میں کوئی معقول عذر پایا گیا تو اس صورت میں تاخیر سقوط حد کا موجب ہوگی۔ اور تاخیر کے لئے معقول عذر سے مراد معرض راستے کا خوف طویل مسافت وغیرہ ہے۔ پس اس عذر کے ماسواء کوئی دوسرا عذر معقول متصور نہ ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اس دعویٰ کی دلیل۔ ا۔ خود ائمہ فقہا کا اجماع ہے جسے فی قولهم جميعاً ( ان تمام کے قول میں) کے الفاظ میں متن کے اندر بیان کیا گیا ہے۔ فتح القدیر میں الاصل کا لفظ استعمال کر کے عقبہ کی شراب نوشی کے بارے میں لکھا گیا ہے کہ کچھ لوگوں نے عقبہ کی شراب نوشی پر گواہی دی پھر اسے خلیفہ ثالث سید نا عثمان ذی النورین کے پاس کوفہ سے مدینہ کی طرف اٹھا کر لے گئے۔ اسی اثناء میں عقبہ کے منہ سے شراب کی بوزائل ہو گئی ( یا نشہ کا فور ہو گیا) چنانچہ اس ( عقبہ) پر حد جاری کی گئی۔ کیونکہ یہاں بعد مسافت ( دوری) کا معقول عذر موجود ہے۔ معقول عذر کے ہوتے ہوئے گواہی کی تاخیر قابل اعتبار ہوگی جیسا کہ حد زنا میں طویل فاصلہ کی بناء پر گواہی میں تا خیر مقبول ہوتی ہے۔ چنانچہ شراب نوشی کے گواہوں کو بھی فاصلے کی طوالت وغیرہ کے باعث مورد الزام نہیں ٹھہرایا جائے گا۔ یعنی ان پر حد قذف جاری نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ فاصلے کی طوالت
Chapter of the penalty for drinking. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the ruling is that the penalty is not inflicted, and according to Imam Muhammad, the penalty is inflicted. So it should be known that by consensus, testimony is not accepted after delay. However, the difference is that according to Imam Muhammad, the period of delay is one month, analogizing to the penalty for zina. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the measure of delay is only the dissipation of the smell. This is because Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: 'If you smell the odor of wine, then flog him.' (Recorded by al-Hakim, al-Tabarani, Abd al-Razzaq, and Abu Ya'la, and the meaning is also in the Sahihain.) And also because the effect of wine, i.e., the persistence of the odor, is the strongest proof of drinking. As for the case where the witnesses seized him while the smell was present or he was intoxicated, then they took him from one city to another where the imam was, and the smell dissipated before they reached, the penalty is inflicted by unanimous agreement, because this is an excuse like distance of travel in the case of zina. And whoever becomes intoxicated from nabidh is flogged, as it is narrated that Umar inflicted the penalty on a Bedouin who became intoxicated from nabidh. We will explain the discourse on the penalty for intoxication and its measure if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya deals with the conditions for establishing the ḥadd (punishment) for drinking wine (khamr) and nabīdh. It opens with an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that if there is a delay in testimony and the smell of wine has dissipated, the ḥadd is not applied, because the evidence of the smell is essential. Imam Muhammad, however, analogizes to the ḥadd for zinā (adultery), where testimony is accepted up to one month after the act; similarly, for drinking, he considers the delay up to one month as acceptable. The author then clarifies that the smell itself is the primary indicator, and that the distinction between the smell of wine and other substances is possible for those who know. The passage then presents a unanimous ruling: if witnesses seize a person while the smell of wine is present or he is intoxicated, and they transport him over a distance to the judge, and the smell dissipates during the journey, the ḥadd is still applied because the delay was due to a valid excuse (distance). This is analogous to the case in zinā where delay due to travel is excused. Finally, the passage mentions that nabīdh (a fermented drink) also incurs the ḥadd for intoxication, citing the practice of Caliph Umar. The discussion follows the order: first the intra-madhhab disagreement, then the agreed-upon case, and finally a preview of the upcoming section on the measure of intoxication.

Key Terms
حد الشرب (ḥadd al-shurb): The fixed corporal punishment for drinking wine or other intoxicants, which is 80 lashes according to the Hanafi school.
تاخیر (tākhīr): Delay in testimony regarding the act of drinking; if without valid excuse, it invalidates the ḥadd because the smell may have dissipated.
رائحة (rā'iḥah): The smell of wine emanating from the drinker's mouth, considered the primary evidence of drinking and a condition for establishing the ḥadd according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
نبیذ (nabīdh): A beverage made from dates or grapes that becomes intoxicating when fermented; in this context, drinking it to intoxication incurs the ḥadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what is the primary evidence required to establish the ḥadd for drinking wine?
A) The presence of two male witnesses who saw the act.
B) The confession of the drinker.
C) The smell of wine emanating from the drinker's mouth.
D) The intoxication of the person.

Key Takeaway
The ḥadd for drinking is not applied if the smell of wine dissipates due to delay without excuse, but delay due to a valid excuse (like distance) is accepted.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
5 min
Hadd Not Dropped When Evidence Vanishes Due to Travel
Ruling on applying hadd when evidence vanishes due to travel to the imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the Hanafi school applies the hadd punishment for intoxication even if the physical signs (smell or drunkenness) disappear during travel to the imam, and identify the analogy to zina and the precedent of Umar for nabidh.

Core Idea
Disappearance of evidence due to distance does not drop the hadd; travel is a valid excuse.

This lesson addresses a crucial scenario in hudud enforcement: what happens when witnesses seize a person reeking of alcohol or clearly drunk, and before they can bring him before the imam the evidence fades? The Hanafi school holds that the hadd must still be applied. The key reasoning is that the distance traveled is a legitimate excuse, akin to the case of zina witnesses who travel far. In addition, the lesson establishes that intoxication from nabidh (date wine) also incurs the same hadd, based on a precedent from Caliph Umar. Understanding this ruling reinforces the principle that procedural delays do not undermine fixed punishments when the original testimony was sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Witnesses apprehend a person with clear signs of drinking (smell of wine or visible intoxication) and travel a considerable distance to reach the imam. By the time they arrive, the signs have vanished.
The key tension: evidence (qarinah) is lost, but witnesses exist.
2
State the ruling and its basis
The Hanafi imams unanimously apply the hadd. Why? Because the delay due to travel is a valid excuse ('udhr), analogous to the hadd of zina where witnesses who travel a long distance are not accused of false testimony. The witness’s credibility is not undermined by the loss of signs.
في قولهم جميعا indicates consensus among the three imams.
3
Analyze the analogy (qiyas) to zina
The text explicitly compares this case to the hadd of zina: just as in zina the hadd is not dropped if witnesses travel and the physical evidence (like pregnancy) disappears, here the same principle applies. Distance is a legal excuse.
This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy) with the illa being the excuse of distance.
4
Examine the precedent for nabidh
The passage cites the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab (رضي الله عنه) who flogged a Bedouin for becoming drunk from nabidh. This establishes that intoxicating nabidh is subject to the same hadd as wine.
The hadd for drinking is 80 lashes for a free person, whether the beverage is khamr or nabidh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ أَخَذَهُ الشُّهُودُ وَرِيْحُهَا يُوجَدُ مِنْهُ أَوْ هُوَ سَكْرَانُ فَذَهَبُوا بِهِ مِنْ مِصْرٍ إِلَى مِصْرٍ فِيهِ الْإِمَامُ فَانْقَطَعَ ذَلِكَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَنْتَهُوا بِهِ حُدَّ فِي قَوْلِهِمْ جَمِيعًا لِأَنَّ هَذَا عُذْرٌ كَبُعْدِ الْمُسَافَةِ فِي حَدِ الزَّنَاءِ وَالشَّاهِدُ لَا يُتَّهَمُ بِهِ فِي مِثْلِهِ وَمَنْ سَكَرَ مِنَ النَّبِيذِ حُدَّ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ عُمَرَ أَقَامَ الْحَدَّ عَلَى أَعْرَابِيٍّ سَكَرَ مِنَ النَّبِيذِ وَنُبَيِّنَ الْكَلَامَ فِي حَدِ السَّكْرِ وَ مِقْدَارِ حَدِّهِ الْمُسْتَحَقِّ عَلَيْهِ إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ تَعَالَى
If the witnesses seize him while the smell of wine is still coming from him, or he is drunk, and they take him from one city to another city where the imam is, and that (smell or drunkenness) disappears before they reach him, he is flogged according to all of them, because this is an excuse like the distance of travel in the hadd of zina, and the witness is not suspected in such a case. And whoever becomes drunk from nabidh is flogged, because it is narrated that Umar inflicted the hadd on a Bedouin who became drunk from nabidh. We will explain the discussion on the hadd of intoxication and the amount of punishment due upon him, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: if witnesses apprehend a person showing clear signs of drinking (smell of wine or visible drunkenness) and then travel a considerable distance to bring him before the imam, and in the process those signs vanish, the hadd punishment is still applied by unanimous agreement of the Hanafi scholars (في قولهم جميعا). The reason is that the delay caused by distance is a valid excuse (عذر), analogous to the case of zina witnesses who travel a long distance—they are not accused of false testimony, and the hadd is not dropped. This principle protects the integrity of testimony. The passage also introduces the rule for nabidh: intoxication from date wine also incurs the hadd, citing the precedent of Caliph Umar ibn al-Khattab who flogged a Bedouin for drinking nabidh. The author promises to discuss the specifics later.

Key Terms
حَدّ (hadd): A fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Islamic law for specific offenses; here, for drinking or intoxication, it is 80 lashes for a free person.
نَبِيذ (nabidh): An intoxicating beverage made from dates or grapes that has been cooked or concentrated until it thickens; it is considered akin to wine in its legal effect.
عُذْر ('udhr): A legally recognized excuse that justifies delay in testimony or enforcement of a punishment; here, the physical distance traveled is such an excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Hanafi imams unanimously apply the hadd to a drunkard even after the smell of wine vanished during transport to the imam?
A) Because the witnesses had other proof of his drinking
B) Because the distance traveled is a valid excuse (عذر) like in zina cases
C) Because the imam ordered it regardless of evidence
D) Because the man confessed upon arrival

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the hadd for drinking is not dropped when the signs of intoxication disappear due to travel distance, because the travel is a valid excuse and the witnesses remain credible.

Hadd Not Applied Based on Smell or Vomit Alone
Ruling that mere smell or vomit is insufficient evidence for hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that hadd for drinking is not established by smell or vomiting alone, and explain the two rational reasons (uncertainty and potential duress) that support it.

Core Idea
Hadd requires certainty; smell and vomiting are ambiguous evidence.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies evidentiary standards in hudud. It establishes that mere physical traces like smell or vomiting are insufficient for conviction because they could originate from permissible sources or coercion. This ruling protects individuals from punishment based on doubt, reflecting the Hanafi principle that hudud are averted by uncertainties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being negated? The hadd penalty for drinking (shurb al-khamr). The ruling is clear: la hadd (no penalty).
The act is the punishment, not the drinking itself.
2
Locate the evidence
Why is the hadd negated? Two reasons are given: the trace of smell is uncertain (muhtamalah), and the drinking may have occurred under coercion (ikrah) or necessity (idtirar).
The evidence is rational (dalil aqli): doubt prevents punishment.
3
Trace the reasoning
The text extends the principle: intoxication from permissible substances (e.g., banj, mare's milk) does not incur hadd. Similarly, coerced drinking does not. This shows that the core issue is the origin of intoxication, not the state itself.
The illa (legal cause) is the presence of doubt about the prohibited act.
4
Note the implied condition
Hadd is only applied when it is established that the person drank prohibited nabidh willingly (taw'an). The text explicitly says: 'until it is known that he became drunk from nabidh and drank it willingly.'
This sets a high evidentiary bar for conviction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا حَدَّ عَلَى مَنْ وُجِدَ مِنْهُ رَائِحَةُ الْخَمْرِ أَوْ تَقَيَّأَ هَالَةَ الرَّائِحَةِ مُحْتَمِلَةٌ وَ كَذَا الشَّرْبُ قَدْ يَقَعُ عَنْ إِكْرَاهٍ وَاضْطِرَارٍ فَلَا يُحَدُّ السَّكْرَانُ حَتَّى يُعْلَمَ أَنَّهُ سَكَرَ مِنَ النَّبِيذِ وَشَرِبَهُ طَوْعًا لِأَنَّ السُّكْرَ مِنَ الْمُبَاحِ لَا يُوجِبُ الْحَدَّ كَالْبَنْجِ وَلَبَنِ الرَّمَاكِ وَكَذَا شُرْبُ الْمُكْرَهِ لَا يُوجِبُ الْحَدَّ
And there is no hadd upon one from whom the smell of wine is found or who vomits, because the trace of the smell is uncertain, and likewise the drinking may have occurred under coercion or necessity. So the drunk person is not flogged until it is known that he became drunk from nabidh and drank it willingly, because intoxication from a permissible thing does not obligate the hadd, like [intoxication from] banj (henbane) and mare's milk. And likewise, the drinking of a coerced person does not obligate the hadd.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage states a legal maxim: hadd for drinking is not imposed solely based on circumstantial evidence like the smell of wine or vomiting. The reason is twofold: first, the smell could be from a non-alcoholic source (e.g., spilled perfume or medicine), so it is uncertain (محتملة). Second, a person may have been forced to drink (إكراه) or in dire necessity (اضطرار). Therefore, the burden of proof is higher: the person must be seen drinking willingly (طوعًا) and the intoxication must be from an explicitly prohibited substance. The text also clarifies that intoxication from permissible substances (e.g., henbane/bangh, mare's milk) does not incur hadd, because the sin is in the act of drinking the prohibited intoxicant, not in the state of intoxication per se. Likewise, coerced drinking is not punishable.

Key Terms
رَائِحَةُ الْخَمْرِ (ra'ihah al-khamr): The odor of wine; it is considered ambiguous evidence, not sufficient alone for hadd.
إِكْرَاه (ikrah): Coercion or duress; if a person drinks under threat, hadd is not imposed.
سُكْرُ مِنَ الْمُبَاحِ (sukr min al-mubah): Intoxication resulting from a permissible substance (e.g., medicine); does not incur hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is hadd not applied if a person is found with the smell of wine on his breath?
A) Because the smell may be from a permissible source
B) Because two witnesses must smell it
C) Because the person must have confessed
D) Because vomiting removes the evidence

Key Takeaway
Hadd for drinking requires certainty of willing consumption of a prohibited intoxicant; ambiguous signs like smell or vomiting do not suffice.

The Hadd for Wine: 80 Lashes and the Dispute on Stripping
Ruling on hadd for intoxicants and the procedure of stripping

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the hadd of wine (80 lashes for a free person) and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding stripping the offender before flogging.

Core Idea
The hadd for wine is 80 lashes due to Companion consensus, and the offender is stripped in the mashhur view to avoid double leniency.

The passage establishes both the quantity and procedure of the hadd for intoxication. It first sets the punishment at 80 lashes for free individuals, based on the consensus of the Sahaba, then addresses a procedural debate within the Hanafi school about whether the offender should be stripped before flogging. This lesson unpacks both the ruling and the reasoning behind the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is consumption of an intoxicant (wine or other) by a free person. The ruling is that the hadd is 80 lashes, based on ijma al-sahabah.
2
Understand the condition for execution
The flogging is not carried out until the intoxication has subsided, to ensure the purpose of deterrence is achieved.
This condition ensures the offender is conscious and understands the punishment.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on stripping
The mashhur riwaya (well-known narration) states that the offender is stripped (except for covering the 'awrah), as in the hadd for zina. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that he is not stripped, to show leniency.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The mashhur view argues that leniency has already been shown by setting the punishment at 80 lashes (a lighter punishment than stoning or 100 lashes), so showing leniency again by not stripping would be a second act of leniency, which is not justified.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is the mashhur riwaya: the offender is stripped before flogging. This is the operative fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُحَدُّ حَتَّى يَزُولَ عَنْهُ السَّكْرُ تَحْصِيلًا لِمَقْصُودِ الْاِنْزِجَارِ وَحَدَّ الْخَمْرِ وَ السَّكْرِ فِي الْحُرِّ ثَمَانُونَ سَوْطًا لِإِجْمَاعِ الصَّحَابَةِ يُفَرَّقُ عَلَى بَدَنِهِ كَمَا فِي حَدِ الزَّنَا عَلَى مَا مَرَّ ثُمَّ يُجَرَّدُ فِي الْمَشْهُورِ مِنَ الرِّوَايَةِ وَعَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّهُ لَا يُجَرَّدُ إِظْهَارًا لِلتَّخْفِيفِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَرِدْ بِهِ نَصُّ وَوَجْهُ الْمَشْهُورِ أَنَّا أَظْهَرْنَا التَّخْفِيفَ مَرَّةً فَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ ثَانِيَا
And he is not flogged until the intoxication leaves him, in order to achieve the purpose of deterrence. And the hadd of wine and intoxication for a free man is eighty lashes, due to the consensus of the Companions. It is distributed over his body as in the hadd of zina, as has passed. Then, in the well-known narration, he is stripped, but Muhammad reports that he is not stripped, to show leniency, because no text requires it. The well-known view is that we have already shown leniency once, so it is not considered a second time.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage covers two main points. First, the hadd for wine and intoxication (i.e., for drinking any intoxicant) is 80 lashes for a free person, based on the consensus (ijma) of the Companions. The punishment is not administered until the person is sober (to ensure deterrence). The lashes are spread over the body (as in zina procedures). Second, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the offender should be stripped of his clothes (except covering the private parts) during flogging. The well-known narration (mashhur riwaya, attributed to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) holds that he is stripped, as in zina. Muhammad al-Shaybani says he should not be stripped, to show leniency (takhfif), because there is no explicit text commanding stripping. The mashhur view responds that leniency has already been shown by setting 80 lashes (instead of a harsher punishment), so showing it again by not stripping is unnecessary. The text clarifies that the well-known position is the relied-upone one.

Key Terms
ثَمَانُونَ سَوْطًا (thamanun sawtan): Eighty lashes: the fixed punishment for consumption of intoxicants for a free person.
يُجَرَّدُ (yujarrad): He is stripped of his clothes except to cover the 'awrah, before flogging.
إِجْمَاع الصَّحَابَة (ijma' al-sahabah): Consensus of the Companions, specifically that the hadd for wine is 80 lashes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He is fully clothed
B) He is stripped completely
C) He is stripped except for covering his private parts
D) He wears a thick garment to reduce pain

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hadd for wine is 80 lashes based on ijma, and the preferred procedure includes stripping the offender except for the 'awrah.

Proof that Intoxicating Nabidh is Subject to Hadd
Establishes that intoxicating nabidh incurs hadd through hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intoxicating nabidh and explain the hadith proofs that establish hadd.

Core Idea
Intoxicating nabidh incurs the same hadd as wine because intoxication is the criterion, not the substance.

This lesson explores the Hanafi position that any intoxicating drink, including nabidh (a date/raisin infusion), is subject to the fixed hadd punishment. We will examine the proofs from the actions of Umar and the Prophet, and understand why this ruling differs from the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is drinking intoxicating nabidh. The ruling is that it incurs the hadd punishment (fixed lashing).
The ruling is not limited to grape wine.
2
Examine the first proof: Umar's action
Umar applied hadd on a Bedouin who became intoxicated from nabidh, as recorded in Sunan Dar Qutni.
This shows a companion's practice supporting the ruling.
3
Examine the second proof: the Prophet's action
A man who drank nabidh from a gourd was brought to the Prophet and claimed he did not drink wine; the Prophet ordered flogging.
Direct prophetic precedent.
4
Note the third proof: Abu Hurairah narration
A similar narration from Abu Hurairah further confirms the practice.
Strengthens the cumulative evidence.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf with Shafi'i
The Shafi'i school restricts hadd to grape wine; Hanafi applies it to all intoxicants. The practical difference is punishment severity.
Both schools prohibit intoxication, but penalty differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حد الشرب
19.
. اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم گواہوں کے حق میں معقول عذر ہے۔ جو شراب نوشی کے گواہوں پر اتہام (تہمت ) مانع ہے۔ کیونکہ کسی قابل حد جرم پر اقامت حد کے لئے تاخیر مانع حد ہے اگر کسی شخص نے نبیذ پی کرنشہ حاصل کیا تو اس پر بھی حد جاری ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ سنن دار قطنی میں مروی ہے کہ حضرت عمر نے اس اعرابی (دیہاتی) پر حد جاری کی تھی جس نے نبیذ سے نشہ حاصل کیا تھا۔ حضرت ابو درداء حضرت ابوسعید رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ سے روایت کرتے ہیں کہ جب سے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پاس ایک نئے والا آدمی لایا گیا سنے کہ وقت سے میں ملے میں بنایا گیا نیز ( جوس ) نہیں پیتا ۔ اس شخص ( نشے والا ) نے عرض کیا یا رسول اللہ ! میں نے شراب نہیں پی میں نے کدو کے برتن میں کھجور اور کشمش کا جوس ( نبیذ) پیا ہے۔ رسول علیہ السلام نے حکم دیا تو اسے زدو کوب کیا گیا۔ ایک دوسری سند سے حضرت ابو ہریرہ کے واسطہ سے رسول علیہ السلام سے اس کی مثل مروی ہے۔ ( طحاوی مترجم جلد سوم ) ان دلائل سے ثابت ہوا کہ نشہ آور نبیذ بھی موجب حد ہے۔
نبیذ ہر چیز سے تیار ہوتی ہے۔ جس چیز کا نبیذ تیار کیا جائے تو اس کو پکایا جاتا ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ وہ (نبیذ ) تھوڑا سا گاڑھا ہو جائے۔ اسی کا پینا جائز ہے۔ مثال کے طور پر نبیذ کا شربت کھجور گندم شہر جو ' چاول' جوار باجرہ انگور وغیرہ سے نبیذ تیار ہوتا ہے۔
Chapter of the Hadd of Drinking. 19. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume Six. A reasonable excuse regarding witnesses of wine drinking is an accusation (imputation) that prevents. Because delay in establishing the hadd for an offense liable to hadd is a bar to the hadd. If a person drank nabidh and became intoxicated, then the hadd will be applied on him as well. Because in Sunan Dar Qutni it is narrated that Umar applied the hadd on that Bedouin who became intoxicated from nabidh. Abu Darda and Abu Sa'id narrated that a man who had drunk something new was brought to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. He said, 'I did not drink wine, I drank juice (nabidh) of dates and raisins in a gourd.' The Prophet ordered and he was flogged. Another chain from Abu Hurairah similar to it (Tahawi translation vol. 3). From these proofs it is established that intoxicating nabidh also necessitates hadd. Nabidh is prepared from everything. Whatever thing nabidh is made from, it is cooked until it thickens a little. Drinking that is permissible. For example, syrup of nabidh is made from dates, wheat, barley, rice, millet, grapes, etc.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage begins by presenting the ruling that intoxicating nabidh (a fermented drink from dates or raisins) incurs the hadd punishment for drinking. The author cites three proofs: 1) Umar applied hadd on a Bedouin who became intoxicated from nabidh, 2) a hadith where a man claimed he drank nabidh from a gourd and the Prophet ordered flogging, and 3) another similar narration from Abu Hurairah. These establish that the prohibition and penalty apply to any intoxicating drink, not just grape wine. The passage then explains that nabidh can be made from various substances (dates, wheat, barley, rice, etc.) and must be cooked until thickened. The halal type is the non-intoxicating version. The key point is that intoxication is the criterion, not the specific substance.

Key Terms
نبیذ (nabidh): A beverage made by soaking dried dates or raisins in water, or from other grains, with the potential to become intoxicating if left to ferment.
حد (hadd): A fixed, unchangeable punishment prescribed by Islamic law for specific crimes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Intoxicating nabidh is legally equivalent to wine: hadd applies because the criterion is intoxication, not the specific substance.

Hadd for Drinking: Conditions of Proof and Exemptions
Explains that hadd is not imposed based on smell or vomit alone, and coercion or permissible intoxication are defenses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the evidentiary conditions required in the Hanafi school to impose hadd for drinking and identify the exemptions due to coercion or intoxication from permissible substances.

Core Idea
Hadd is not imposed on ambiguous evidence; voluntary intoxication from a prohibited substance must be proven.

The hadd for drinking is a severe penalty, but the Hanafi school demands certainty before applying it. This passage clarifies that mere smell or vomit are ambiguous and insufficient. Additionally, if the drinking was coerced or the intoxication came from a permissible source such as bangh or mare's milk, the hadd is lifted. Understanding these limits safeguards against wrongful punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous indicators
The passage mentions two indicators that are insufficient: the smell of wine and vomiting wine. Explain why each is doubtful—the smell could come from another source, and vomiting could be caused by coercion or necessity.
2
Recognize the exemptions based on causation
The passage lists two exemptions: coercion (ikrah) and intoxication from permissible substances (sukr min al-mubah). Note that these remove the element of volition or the prohibition itself.
3
Extract the underlying legal principle (illah)
The common illah is the presence of doubt (shubha). In Hanafi law, the maxim 'al-hadd yadra'u bi al-shubuhat' (hadd is averted by doubts) applies. The passage extends this to ambiguous evidence and the exemptions.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school may accept smell as circumstantial evidence, while Hanafi requires direct proof. Note the practical difference in court outcomes.
5
Apply the rule to a hypothetical
Given a scenario, determine if hadd applies by checking for voluntary consumption of a prohibited intoxicant, the presence of doubt, and any exemptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا حَدَّ عَلَى مَنْ وُجِدَ مِنْهُ رَائِحَةُ الْخَمْرِ أَوْ تَقَيَّأَ هَا لَأَنَّ الرَّائِحَةَ مُحْتَمِلَةٌ وَ كَذَا الشَّرْبُ قَدْ يَقَعُ عَنْ إِكْرَاهٍ وَاضْطِرَارِ فَلَا يُحَدُّ السَّكْرَانُ حَتَّى يُعْلَمَ أَنَّهُ سَكِرَ مِنَ النَّبِيذِ وَشَرِبَهُ طَوْعًا لِأَنَّ السُّكْرَ مِنَ الْمُبَاحِ لَا يُوجِبُ الْحَدَّ كَالْبَنْجِ وَلَبَنِ الرَّمَاكِ وَكَذَا شُرْبُ الْمُكْرَهِ لَا يُوجِبُ الْحَدَّ
There is no hadd on one from whom the smell of wine is found or who vomits it, because the smell is doubtful; similarly drinking may occur under coercion or necessity, so the intoxicated person is not penalized until it is known that he became intoxicated from nabidh and he drank it voluntarily; because intoxication from permissible things does not necessitate hadd, like bangh (henbane) and mare's milk; likewise, one who is coerced to drink does not incur hadd.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage sets conditions for imposing the hadd of drinking. Two evidentiary factors – the smell of wine on the breath or vomiting wine – are insufficient by themselves because they are ambiguous: the smell could be from other sources, and vomiting could be caused by force. Similarly, drinking may result from coercion or dire necessity, not choice. Therefore, to impose hadd it must be proven that the person voluntarily drank an intoxicant (nabidh or wine) and became intoxicated. If the intoxication came from a permissible substance like bangh (a narcotic) or mare's milk (which are not inherently prohibited), no hadd is applied. Coerced drinking also exempts. The underlying principle (illah) is the element of free choice in consuming a prohibited intoxicant.

Key Terms
إكراه (ikrah): Coercion or compulsion that negates free will; a defense against hadd.
السكر من المباح (al-sukru min al-mubah): Intoxication from a substance that is inherently permissible, like bangh or mare's milk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following does NOT exempt a person from hadd for drinking?
A) The person voluntarily drank a non-intoxicating nabidh
B) The person vomited wine
C) The person was coerced to drink
D) The person became intoxicated from permissible bangh

Key Takeaway
Hadd for drinking requires certainty of voluntary consumption of a prohibited intoxicant; ambiguous evidence, coercion, or permissible intoxication prevent its application.

The Hadd for Drinking: 80 Lashes and the Stripping Dispute
States the fixed hadd for drinking (80 lashes) and discusses whether to strip clothes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the hadd for drinking and identify the intra-madhhab dispute regarding stripping the offender.

Core Idea
Eighty lashes for drinking is fixed by ijma; the dispute is over stripping clothes — a debate about showing leniency.

The hadd for drinking intoxicants is one of the established hudud punishments. This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the amount (80 lashes for a free person) and an interesting subsidiary issue: whether the offender's clothes should be removed during execution. The Hanafi school has a known internal difference on this point, which we will unpack.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on the hadd amount
The passage states that the hadd for wine and intoxication for a free person is eighty lashes. Note that this applies after the intoxication has worn off.
The number 80 is based on the consensus of the Companions.
2
Understand the distribution method
The lashes are distributed over the body, as in the hadd of zina. This means they are not concentrated on one spot.
The method is similar to the execution of the zina hadd.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute on stripping
The text presents two views: the well-known narration (mashhur) that the offender is stripped of outer clothes (except covering the 'awrah), and Imam Muhammad's view that he is not stripped.
Imam Muhammad's view is based on showing leniency and the absence of an explicit text.
4
Analyze the reasoning behind each position
The well-known view argues that leniency was already shown by reducing the number from 100 to 80, so further leniency is not warranted. Imam Muhammad's view prioritizes leniency as there is no textual command to strip.
Both are considered valid within the school, but the well-known view is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُحَدُّ حَتَّى يَزُولَ عَنْهُ السَّكْرُ تَحْصِيلًا لِمَقْصُودِ الْاِنْزِجَارِ وَحَدُّ الْخَمْرِ وَ السُّكْرِ فِي الْحُرِّ ثَمَانُونَ سَوْطًا لِاجْمَاعِ الصَّحَابَةِ يُفَرَّقُ عَلَى بَدَنِهِ كَمَا فِي حَدِّ الزِّنَا عَلَى مَا مَرَّ ثُمَّ يُجَرَّدُ فِي الْمَشْهُورِ مِنَ الرِّوَايَةِ وَعَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ إِنَّهُ لَا يُجَرَّدُ إِظْهَارًا لِلتَّخْفِيفِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَرِدْ بِهِ نَصٌّ وَوَجْهُ الْمَشْهُورِ أَنَّا أَظْهَرْنَا التَّخْفِيفَ مَرَّةً فَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ ثَانِيًا
He is not penalized until intoxication leaves him, to achieve the purpose of deterrence. The hadd of wine and intoxication for a free person is eighty lashes, due to the consensus of the Companions. It is distributed over his body, as in the hadd of zina as previously mentioned. Then he is stripped (of clothes) in the well-known narration. From Muhammad (al-Shaybani) that he is not stripped, to show leniency, because no text came regarding it. The well-known view's reasoning is that we have shown leniency once (by reducing from 100 to 80), so leniency is not considered a second time.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage first stipulates that the hadd is executed after the offender's intoxication wears off, so that the punishment achieves its deterrent effect (zajr). The hadd for a free person for drinking wine or any intoxicant is eighty lashes, based on the consensus of the Companions (the 40 lashes set by Umar was increased to 80 by later consensus? Actually, the standard is 80, as per the school). The lashes are distributed over the body, like in zina. The passage then discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute: the 'mashhur' (well-known) narration says the offender's outer garment is removed (jarrud) to expose the body? Actually, the text says 'yujarradu' meaning stripped of clothes except covering the 'awrah. Imam Muhammad's narration says not to strip, to show leniency (takhfif) because there is no explicit text commanding it. The well-known view's reasoning is that leniency was already shown by reducing the number from 100 (for adultery) to 80 for drinking, so further leniency is not warranted.

Key Terms
تجرید (tajrid): The act of stripping the offender of outer clothes during the execution of hadd, only covering the 'awrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 40
B) 80
C) 100
D) 60

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school fixes 80 lashes for drinking by ijma; the stripping of clothes is debated, with the majority opting for it to avoid over-leniency.

Hadd for Slave and Retraction of Confession in Drinking Cases
States slave's hadd, retraction effect, and dispute on confessions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadd for a slave for drinking, explain why retraction of confession averts the punishment, and compare the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the number of confessions required.

Core Idea
A slave's hadd is halved to 40 lashes; retraction of confession averts punishment for a pure Haqq Allah crime, but the number of confessions needed is disputed within the Hanafi school.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents three interrelated rulings concerning the hadd for drinking wine. It addresses the reduced punishment for slaves, the effect of retracting a confession, and the evidentiary requirements. These rulings illustrate key Hanafi principles: slavery halves punishments, doubts (shubuhāt) avert hudud, and the school accommodates legitimate ikhtilaf among its founding imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling for a slave
The passage states that if the offender is a slave, the hadd is 40 lashes, half of the free person's 80. Note the reason: slavery halves punishments, analogous to the hadd for zina.
This is based on qiyas with the hadd of zina for slaves.
2
Understand the effect of retracting a confession
If a person confesses to drinking or intoxication and then retracts, the hadd is not applied. The reason given is that this is a pure right of Allah (haqq Allah), and retraction introduces doubt that averts the punishment.
In Hanafi law, retraction of confession is accepted in hudud that are pure Haqq Allah.
3
Note the evidentiary requirements for proof
Drinking is established by the testimony of two witnesses or by a single confession. This is the position of Abu Hanifa.
The text then presents a differing view from Abu Yusuf.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf requires two confessions (marratayn) for the hadd to be established. The author notes this dispute is similar to the one in theft cases.
Muhammad al-Shaybani's view is not mentioned here but typically follows Abu Hanifa.
5
Link to other cases and the tarjih
The passage references that the dispute parallels theft, which will be explained later. The mufta bihi position is Abu Hanifa's: one confession suffices.
This illustrates how Hanafi jurists cross-reference similar disputes within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ كَانَ عَبْدًا فَحَدُّهُ أَرْبَعُونَ لِأَنَّ الرِّقَّ مُنَصِّفٌ عَلَى مَا عُرِفَ وَمَنْ أَقَرَّ بِشُرْبِ الْخَمْرِ أَوِ السُّكْرِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ لَمْ يُحَدَّ لِأَنَّهُ خَالِصُ حَقِّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَيَثْبُتُ الشُّرْبُ بِشَهَادَةِ شَاهِدَيْنِ وَيَثْبُتُ بِالْإِقْرَارِ مَرَّةً وَاحِدَةً وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ يُشْتَرَطُ الْإِقْرَارُ مَرَّتَيْنِ وَهُوَ نَظِيرُ الْاِخْتِلَافِ فِي السَّرْقَةِ وَسَنُبَيِّنُهَا هُنَاكَ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى
If he is a slave, his hadd is forty, because slavery halves (punishments) as has been established. Whoever confesses to drinking wine or intoxication and then retracts, he is not penalized, because it is the pure right of Allah. Drinking is established by the testimony of two witnesses, and it is established by one confession. From Abu Yusuf it is narrated that two confessions are required. It is similar to the difference in theft, and we will explain that there, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage gives three rulings. First, the hadd for a slave is 40 lashes (half of 80), because slavery reduces punishments (as in zina where the slave's hadd is 50? Actually for zina it's half, so analogy applies). Second, if a person confesses to drinking and then retracts, the hadd is dropped because this is a pure right of Allah (haqq Allah), and retraction averts the punishment due to doubt. Third, proof of drinking requires two witnesses or a single confession according to Abu Hanifa; Abu Yusuf requires two separate confessions (kurai) in two different sessions? The text says 'marratayn' meaning two occasions. The author notes this is similar to the dispute in theft cases, which will be covered later.

Key Terms
حقالله (haqq Allah): A right of Allah that cannot be waived by individuals; if a person retracts confession, it is accepted because it removes the right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One
B) Two
C) Four
D) Three

Key Takeaway
A slave's hadd for drinking is 40 lashes; retraction of confession averts the hadd, and the Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that one confession suffices.

Definition of Intoxication for Hadd: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Defines the threshold of intoxication that triggers hadd, with ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi definitions of legal intoxication (sukr) between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the correct definition to determine when hadd is incurred.

Core Idea
The threshold for intoxication triggering hadd differs: complete senselessness (Abu Hanifa) vs. incoherent speech (Sahibayn).

This lesson explores the legal definition of intoxication (sukr) that triggers the fixed punishment (hadd) for drinking non-wine intoxicants. Within the Hanafi school, there is a notable disagreement between the founder Imam Abu Hanifa and his two principal students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the hudud punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested legal element
The definition of 'sakran' (the legally intoxicated person) that triggers the hadd punishment.
Both definitions agree that the person must be intoxicated, but disagree on the degree.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the person must be completely senseless: unable to comprehend any speech (little or much) and unable to distinguish a man from a woman.
This is a very high threshold, requiring near-total loss of reason.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that it suffices if the person's speech becomes delirious and confused (yuhdi wa yakhtalit).
This is a lower threshold, based on observable signs of intoxication.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's reasoning
Their reasoning is that this is the common understanding of an intoxicated person in customary usage ('urf).
They give priority to 'urf over a stricter literal interpretation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi fatwa often relies on the Sahibayn's position because it is easier to establish and more practical.
The text ends with 'wa ilayhi' (and to it), possibly indicating preference, but the passage is truncated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالسَّكْرَانُ الَّذِي يُحَدُّ هُوَ الَّذِي لَا يَعْقِلُ مَنْطِقًا لَا قَلِيلًا وَلَا كَثِيرًا وَلَا يَعْقِلُ الرَّجُلَ مِنَ الْمَرْأَةِ وَقَالَ الْعَبْدُ الضَّعِيفُ هَذَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا هُوَ الَّذِي يَهْذِي وَيَخْتَلِطُ كَلَامُهُ لِأَنَّهُ هُوَ السَّكْرَانُ فِي الْعُرْفِ وَإِلَيْهِ
The intoxicated person who is penalized is he who does not comprehend any speech, little or much, and does not distinguish a man from a woman. The weak slave said: This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two said: He is the one whose speech is delirious and confused, because that is the intoxicated person in common understanding, and to it.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage provides the legal definition of intoxication (sukr) that triggers hadd for drinking non-wine intoxicants. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute. According to Abu Hanifa, the person must be so intoxicated that he cannot understand any speech (meaning he is completely senseless) and cannot distinguish between a man and a woman. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), it is sufficient that his speech becomes incoherent (yuhdi) and confused (yakhtalit). Their reasoning is that this is the common understanding of intoxication in customary usage ('urf). The phrase 'wa ilayhi' suggests that the preferred view is towards the Sahibayn? Or that the mashhur view aligns with them? The text ends abruptly. The passage highlights the difference in the threshold: a higher bar (Abu Hanifa) vs. a lower bar (Sahibayn) for application of hadd.

Key Terms
سكران (sakran): The legally intoxicated person who incurs hadd. Defined differently by Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

D) When he falls asleep

Key Takeaway
The legal definition of intoxication (sukr) for hadd punishment differs between Abu Hanifa (complete senselessness) and the Sahibayn (incoherent speech), with the latter being the relied-upon position.

Hadd for Drinking: Slave, Confession Retraction, and Proof
Clarifying hudud rulings for drinking: slave penalty, retraction, and proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadd penalty for a slave drinking, explain why retraction of confession drops the hadd, and identify the required proof methods for establishing the hadd of drinking.

Core Idea
Slavery halves the hadd; retraction of confession drops it; one confession suffices for proof.

The Hidayah consolidates three key rulings on the hadd for drinking into a single passage. Understanding these rules—how slavery affects punishment, when retraction nullifies a confession, and how proof is established—is essential for a judge or mufti. This lesson unpacks each ruling with its underlying reasoning and notes an intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of confessions required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling for a slave
Find where the text specifies the hadd for a slave (40 lashes). Understand the principle 'ar-riqqu munassifun' that slavery halves corporal punishments.
This principle applies across hudud: e.g., for zina, a slave receives 50 lashes instead of 100.
2
Analyze the rule on retraction
Note that if a person confesses to drinking and then retracts before punishment, the hadd is dropped. Reason: it is a pure right of Allah, and retraction introduces doubt (shubha) which averts the hadd.
This does not apply to theft because it involves a victim's right.
3
Examine the proof methods
Drinking can be proven by two male witnesses or by a single confession. Note the dispute: Imam Abu Yusuf requires two confessions, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad accept one.
This mirrors the dispute in theft hadd.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that one confession suffices, as stated in Zahir al-Riwayah.
The text presents Abu Yusuf's view as an alternative, but the main teaching is the single confession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ كَانَ عَبْدَافَحَدُّهُ أَرْبَعُونَ لِاَنَّ الرّقَ مُنَصِّفٌ عَلَى مَاعُرِفَ وَمَنْ اَقَرَّبِشُرْبِ الْخَمْرِ أَوِ السُّكْرِثُمَّ رَجَعَ لَمْ يُحَدُّلَانَّهُ خَالِصُ حَقِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَيَثْبُتُ الشَّرْبُ بِشَهَادَةِ شَاهِدَيْنِ وَيَثْبُتُ بِالْإِقْرَارِ مَرَّةً وَاحِدَةً وَ عَنْ أَبِي يُوْسُفٌ أَنَّهُ يُشْتَرَطُ الْإِقْرَارُ مَرَّتَيْنِ وَهُوَ نَظِيرُ الْاِخْتِلَافِ فِي السَّرْقَةِ وَسَنُبَيْنُهَا هُنَاكَ إِنْشَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى
And if (the drinker) is a slave, his hadd is forty (lashes), because slavery halves (the punishment) as is known. And whoever confesses to drinking wine or intoxication, then recants, he is not punished with hadd, because it is a pure right of Allah. And drinking is proven by the testimony of two witnesses, and it is proven by a single confession. And from Abu Yusuf (it is narrated) that two confessions (in two sessions) are required. This is similar to the disagreement in (the hadd of) theft, and we will explain it there, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage combines three rulings from the Hidayah on the hadd for drinking. First, if the offender is a slave, the hadd is forty lashes instead of eighty, because slavery halves corporal punishments—this is a general principle in Hanafi fiqh (e.g., for zina, a slave receives fifty lashes instead of one hundred). Second, if a person confesses to drinking wine or becoming intoxicated (with any intoxicant) and then retracts the confession before the hadd is carried out, the hadd is dropped. This is because the right of Allah is based on leniency; retraction introduces doubt (shubha) which averts the hadd. Third, the proof of drinking: it can be established by the testimony of two male witnesses (no women) or by a single confession. Imam Abu Yusuf, however, narrates that two confessions in two different sessions are required, mirroring the dispute in theft (where Abu Hanifa accepts one confession for amputation, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require two). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that one confession suffices, as the text states 'once'. The commentary clarifies that these rulings apply specifically to khamr (wine) and any intoxicant that causes loss of intellect.

Key Terms
الرّقّ مُنَصِّفٌ (ar-riqqu munassifun): Slavery halves the prescribed punishments
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Confession of the accused, acceptable as proof of drinking

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many lashes does a slave receive for drinking wine?
A) Eighty
B) Forty
C) Thirty
D) Fifty

Key Takeaway
For the hadd of drinking, a slave receives 40 lashes, retraction of confession drops the punishment, and proof can be either two witnesses or a single confession.
