Women's Testimony in Hadd of Drinking: The Hanafi Position
Ruling on inadmissibility of female testimony in drinking hadd cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's testimony in the hadd of drinking and explain the legal reasoning (shubhat al-badaliyyah).

Core Idea
Women's testimony in hudud is rejected due to suspicion of substitution and error.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the admissibility of women's testimony in the specific case of the hadd punishment for drinking alcohol. The Hanafi school rules that women's testimony, even when supported by male witnesses, is not accepted in hudud (fixed punishments) or qisas (retaliation). This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling, focusing on the concept of shubhat al-badaliyyah (suspicion of substitution) and the concern for error and forgetfulness. Understanding this ruling requires distinguishing between types of cases where women's testimony is accepted (financial transactions) and those where it is not (hudud).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the hadd punishment for drinking (shurb). The ruling is that women's testimony, even with men, is not accepted to prove this hadd.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a qiyas based on the general principle that women's testimony carries a suspicion of substitution and error. The reasoning is 'because there is suspicion of substitution and accusation of error and forgetfulness'.
The passage itself provides the dalil in the form of a reason (ta'lil).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The specific words 'shubhat al-badaliyyah wa tuhmat al-dalal wa al-nisyan' indicate that the law's concern is reliability and certainty. Hudud require the highest level of proof; women's testimony is considered less certain.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) rooted in the nature of testimony.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Shafi'is accept women's testimony in hudud except for zina and qisas for murder. The Hanafi position is more restrictive.
This difference has practical implications for evidence in hadd cases.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi is the established Hanafi position, based on zahir al-riwayah, and it is the relied-upon ruling in the school.
The tarjih authority is the general acceptance of this ruling in the Hanafi works.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُقْبَلُ فِيهِ شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ مَعَ الرِّجَالِ لِاَنَّ فِيهَا شُبْهَةُ الْبَدْلِيَّةِ وَتُهْمَةُ الضَّلَالِ وَالنِّسْيَانِ
And the testimony of women along with men is not accepted in it (hadd of drinking), because there is in it a suspicion of substitution (change) and accusation of error and forgetfulness.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage states that in cases of drinking (shurb), the testimony of women, even when accompanied by male witnesses, is not accepted. The reason given is that women's testimony carries a shubha (doubt) of badliyyah (change/alteration) and the accusation of dalal (error) and nisyan (forgetfulness). This reflects a general Hanafi principle that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud (fixed penalties) and qisas (retaliation), though it is accepted in financial transactions and other matters. The commentary explains that this is because hudud require certainty, and women's testimony is considered less reliable due to natural tendencies of forgetfulness and potential bias. This ruling is specific to hadd cases; in other matters, women's testimony is valid when accompanied by men.

Key Terms
شبهة البدلية (shubhat al-badaliyyah): Suspicion that the testimony might be altered or substituted

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is women's testimony not accepted in the hadd of drinking?
A) Because women are not allowed to testify in any legal matter
B) Because of the suspicion of substitution and accusation of error and forgetfulness
C) Because only two male witnesses can testify in hudud
D) Because the Quran explicitly says women's testimony is invalid

Key Takeaway
Women's testimony is not accepted in the hadd of drinking due to the suspicion of substitution (shubhat al-badaliyyah) and the concern for error and forgetfulness, reflecting the Hanafi principle that hudud require the highest certainty.

Definition of the Intoxicated Person (Sakran) for Hadd: Intra-Hanafi and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Defining the level of intoxication that incurs hadd, with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of sakran for hadd, distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Imam al-Shafi'i, and apply the mufta bihi view to determine when hadd applies.

Core Idea
Hadd for drinking requires severe intoxication; Hanafis define it by speech incoherence, not by external signs.

The hadd punishment for drinking is a serious penalty, and classical jurists debated the precise threshold of intoxication that triggers it. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position, including an internal difference between Abu Hanifa and his two students, and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view. Understanding this dispute helps clarify why some drinkers may receive ta'zir rather than hadd.

Guided Path
1
State the three positions
Identify the definitions of sakran according to Abu Hanifa (complete loss of discrimination), the Sahibayn (speech incoherence), and Imam al-Shafi'i (external signs in gait and movements).
Note that there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
2
Examine the proofs
Explain the dalil for each position: Abu Hanifa relies on the principle of dar' al-hadd (avert hadd by taking the fullest cause); the Sahibayn rely on 'urf (custom); al-Shafi'i relies on observable effects.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to Shafi'i
The Hanafi school rejects the Shafi'i criterion because external signs vary among individuals, making them unreliable. The Sahibayn's criterion of speech incoherence is more consistent.
This is a methodological critique based on the nature of the sign.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Most later mashayikh preferred the Sahibayn's view, so the relied-upon position for fatwa is that the intoxicated person is one whose speech becomes incoherent and confused.
Abu Hanifa's stricter view is a minority position within the school.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi (Sahibayn), a person who drinks but does not become incoherent is not liable for hadd (only ta'zir). Under Shafi'i, if external signs appear, hadd applies even if speech is coherent.
This practical difference highlights the real-world impact of the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالسَّكْرَاتُ الَّذِي يُحَدُّ هُوَ الَّذِي لَا يَعْقِلُ مَنْطِقًا لَا قَلِيْلًا وَلَا كَثِيرًا وَلَا يَعْقِلُ الرَّجُلُ مِنَ الْمَرْأَمْوَقَالَ الْعَبْدُ الضَّعِيفُ هَذَا عِنْدَابِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا هُوَ الَّذِى يَهْذِى وَيَخْتَلِطُ كَلَامُهُ لاَنَّهُ هُوَ السَّكْرَانُ فِي الْعُرْفِ وَإِلَيْهِ مَالَ اَكْثَرُ الْمَشَايِخِ وَلَهُ إِنَّهُ يُؤْخَذُ فِى أَسْبَابِ الْحُدُودِ بِأَقْصَاهَا دَرْء الِلْحَدِوَنِهَايَةُ السُّكْرَانِ يَغْلِبُ السُّرُورُ عَلَى الْعَقْلِ فَيَسْلُبُهُ التَّمْسِيرُ بَيْنَ شَيْءٍ وَشَيْءٍ وَمَا دُونَ ذَالِكَ لَا يَغْرَى عَنْ شُبْهَةِ الصُّحُو وَالْمُعْتَبَرُ فِي الْقَدْحِ الْمُسْكِرِ فِي حَقِّ الْحُرْمَةِ مَا قَالَاهُ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ أَحَدًا بِالْإِحْتِيَاطِ وَالشَّافِعِيُّ يَعْتَبِرُ ظُهُورَ أَثْرِهِ فِي مَشِيَّتِهِ وَحَرَكَاتِهِ وَأَطْرَافِهِ وَهَذَا مِمَّا يَتَفَاوَتُ فَلَامَعْنَى لِاعْتِبَارِهِ
And the intoxicated person who is punished is the one who does not understand speech, neither little nor much, and does not distinguish a man from a woman. (The author said: this is according to Abu Hanifa.) And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he is the one who raves and his speech becomes confused, because that is the drunkard in common custom, and this is what most of the early scholars inclined towards. And (Abu Hanifa's) proof is that in the causes of hudud, the highest degree is taken to avert the hadd. And the ultimate level of intoxication is when pleasure dominates the intellect so that it deprives him of discrimination between one thing and another. What is below that is not free from the suspicion of sobriety. And the consideration regarding the intoxicating drink in terms of prohibition is what the two said (i.e., the Sahibayn's view) by consensus, out of caution. And al-Shafi'i considers the appearance of its effect in his gait and movements and limbs, and this varies, so there is no meaning to considering it.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage defines the threshold of intoxication (sukr) that triggers the hadd punishment for drinking. The Hidayah presents three positions: (1) Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the hadd applies only when the person reaches extreme intoxication—he cannot understand any speech, however short or long, and cannot distinguish between a man and a woman. His reasoning is that in hudud, we take the fullest extent of the cause to avert the punishment (dar' al-hadd). Thus, only the highest degree of intoxication, where the intellect is completely overwhelmed, incurs hadd; lesser intoxication retains a shubha (suspicion) of sobriety. (2) Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn) define the sakran as one whose speech becomes incoherent (yuhdhi) and confused (yakhtalit kalamuhu). This is based on 'urf (custom) and is the view most of the later scholars (mashayikh) inclined towards. (3) Imam al-Shafi'i considers external signs: if the effect of the drink appears in the person's walking, movements, and limbs, the hadd applies. The Hanafi commentary rejects this because these signs vary from person to person. The passage also notes a consensus (ijma) regarding the prohibition of the intoxicating drink itself: the Sahibayn's definition (that the drink is haram when it intoxicates, i.e., causes incoherence) is adopted as a precaution. In practice, the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view is that of the Sahibayn, as most mashayikh preferred it. However, all agree that drinking khamr (wine) incurs hadd regardless of intoxication, while for other intoxicants, hadd only applies when actual intoxication (as per Sahibayn's definition) occurs; otherwise, ta'zir is given.

Key Terms
السَّكْرَانُ (as-sakran): The intoxicated person who is liable for hadd
دَرْءُ الْحَدِّ (dar' al-hadd): Averting the hadd punishment through doubts (shubhaat)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), when does a person become liable for the hadd of drinking?
A) When he cannot distinguish a man from a woman
B) When his speech becomes incoherent and confused
C) When his gait becomes unsteady
D) When he drinks any amount of wine

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi defines the drunkard liable for hadd as one whose speech becomes incoherent, a view based on custom and the principle of averting hudud by doubts.

Defining Sakran for Hadd: The Hanafi Criterion
Defines the legal threshold of drunkenness for hadd punishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sakran for hadd, distinguish between the definitions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and explain the majority's preference.

Core Idea
Intoxication for hadd is loss of discrimination or incoherent speech, not amount drunk or physical signs.

This lesson examines the legal definition of a 'sakran' (drunkard) for applying the hadd punishment. The Hanafi school has two internal definitions: Abu Hanifa requires total loss of discrimination, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) define it by incoherent speech. The majority of later scholars adopted the Sahibayn's view. We will also contrast this with Imam al-Shafi'i's reliance on physical signs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The passage defines who is legally considered intoxicated (sakran) for the purpose of applying the fixed punishment (hadd). This is a preliminary step before any punishment can be inflicted.
Hadd is averted by doubts (shubuhat), so the definition must be precise.
2
State Abu Hanifa's definition and its proof
Abu Hanifa defines sakran as one whose intellect is overcome by joy to the extent that he loses discrimination between things. His proof is the principle of dar' al-hudud (avert hadd by requiring the maximum degree).
This is the strictest definition.
3
State the Sahibayn's definition and its basis
The Sahibayn define sakran as one who speaks incoherently (hadhyan) with confused speech. They rely on common understanding ('urf).
This definition is more practical.
4
Identify the majority's choice and the mufta bihi
The majority of mashayikh preferred the Sahibayn's view because it aligns with 'urf and avoids the weakness of Abu Hanifa's proof. This is the operative position for fatwa.
Tarjih authority: Mulla Abd al-Aziz in Ashraf al-Hidayah.
5
Contrast with Shafi'i definition
Imam al-Shafi'i considers external physical effects (staggering, limb movements) as signs of intoxication. The Hanafi response is that these vary greatly among individuals, so they are unreliable.
Practical difference: a person who shows no external signs but speaks incoherently is sakran in Hanafi but not necessarily in Shafi'i.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حد الشرف ۱۹۲
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم مَالَ اَكْثَرُ الْمَشَايِخِ وَلَهُ إِنَّهُ يُؤْخَذُ فِى أَسْبَابِ الْحُدُودِ بِأَقْصَاهَا دَرْءًا لِلْحَدِّ وَنِهَايَةُ السُّكْرَانِ يَغْلِبُ السُّرُورُ عَلَى الْعَقْلِ فَيَسْلُبُهُ التَّمْيِيزُ بَيْنَ شَيْءٍ وَشَيْءٍ وَمَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لَا يَخْلُو عَنْ شُبْهَةِ الصَّحْوِ وَالْمُعْتَبَرُ فِي الْقَدَحِ الْمُسْكِرِ فِي حَقِّ الْحُرْمَةِ مَا قَالَاهُ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ أَخْذًا بِالْإِحْتِيَاطِ وَالشَّافِعِيُّ يَعْتَبِرُ ظُهُورَ أَثَرِهِ فِي مَشْيَتِهِ وَحَرَكَاتِهِ وَأَطْرَافِهِ وَهَذَا مِمَّا يَتَفَاوَتُ فَلَامَعْنَى لِاعْتِبَارِهِ

ترجمہ اور نشہ کا ایسا مست آدمی جسے حد لگائی جائے وہ شخص ہے جو آپس کی گفتگو کو نہ مجھے نہ تھوڑی نہ بہت اور مرد و عورت کے درمیان تمیز نہ کر سکے۔ مصنف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ قول امام ابوحنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کا ہے اور صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہا نے فرمایا ہے مست نشہ وہ شخص ہے جو ہذیان کرے ( بکواس کرنے) اور جس کی اکثر باتیں مختلط ہوں ( کوئی سر پیر نہ ہو) کیونکہ عرف میں اسی کو مست کہتے ہیں اور صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے قول ہی کی طرف اکثر مشائخ کا میلان ہے ( اور فتویٰ دینے کے لئے یہی قول مناسب اور مختار ہے کیونکہ امام اعظم رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کی دلیل ضعیف ہے۔ ) امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حدود قائم کرنے کے اسباب میں اس سب کا اعتبار کیا جاتا ہے جو کامل مرتبہ کا ہو۔ تا کہ کسی بھی طرح حدود دل سکیں اور نشہ کی انتہا ( آخری درجہ کا نشہ جسے کہا جاتا ہے ) یہ ہے کہ سرور عقل پر اتنا غالب ہو جائے کہ اس کو کسی بھی دو چیز کے درمیان امتیاز ختم ہو جائے اور جب اس سے کم نشہ ہوتو وہ ہوش کے شبہ سے خالی نہیں ہوتا ہے (یعنی اسے کچھ نہ کچھ ہوش بھی رہتا ہے)۔ اور شراب کے سوا دوسری نشہ آور چیزوں کے حرام ہونے میں (جس پیالہ یا گلاس سے پی جارہی ہو ) وہی گلاس اور پیالہ حرام ہو گا جس کے پینے سے ہذیان ( بکواس ) اور اختلاط ( بے سرو پیر ) کی باتیں ہونے لگیں۔ اسی کو تینوں اماموں نے احتیاطی اختیار کیا ہے۔ لیکن امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نشہ کے بارے میں اثر ظاہر ہونے کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں۔ یعنی اس کے ہاتھوں پیر اور دوسری حرکتوں سے اس کے نشہ میں ہونے کی علامت ظاہر ہونے لگیں۔ حالانکہ ان باتوں کے ہونے میں لوگوں کے درمیان بہت فرق ہوتا ہے۔ تو اس کے اعتبار کرنے کے کوئی معنی نہیں ہیں۔

تشريح " وهذا يتفادات فلا معنى لاعتباره " امام شافعی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نشہ کے بارہ میں اثر ظاہر ہونے کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں۔ یعنی نشہ کا اثر اس کی رفتار و حرکات و ہاتھ و پاؤں میں ظاہر ہو حالانکہ یہ باتیں لوگوں میں مختلف طور سے پائی جاتی ہیں۔ اس لئے اس کے اعتبار کرنے کے کچھ معنی نہیں ہیں۔ ( کیونکہ کوئی آدمی قوی ہوتا ہے کہ نشہ کی چیز پینے کے باوجود اس کی حرکتوں میں کوئی فرق نہیں آتا ہے اور کوئی ایسا کمزور ہوتا ہے کہ نشہ کے بغیر بھی جھومتا اورلڑکھڑاتا رہتا ہے۔)

اور واضح ہو کہ شراب کے سوا دوسری نشہ آور چیزوں میں جب تک نشہ نہ آجائے اس وقت تک اس کا پینا حرام نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے اگر کسی کو تین پیالے پی لینے کے باوجود نشہ نہ آیا تو وہ اس کے لئے جائز ہے اور اگر چوتھے پیالہ پر نشہ آ گیا تو یہی آخری پیالہ اس کے لئے حرام ہوگا۔ اس جگہ ا نشہ ہونے سے بالاتفاق یہ مراد ہے کہ اس کا کلام ہذیان اور مختلط ( بکواس اور بے تکا) ہو لیکن ایسا کلام اس کے کلام میں نصف سے زائد ہونا چاہئے۔ کیونکہ اگر نصف کلام سے بھی اس کا سلجھا ہوا ہو تو وہ نشہ میں مست نہیں ہوگا۔ البحر ۔ بھنگ، چرس اور افیون حرام ہے لیکن خمر سے ان کی حرکت کم ہے اب اگر ان چیزوں کے استعمال سے نشہ آجائے تو اسے حد نہیں ماری جائے گی۔ بلکہ اس کی تغریر ( مناسب سزا دی جائے گی۔ الجوہرہ لیکن تحقیق یہ ہے کہ بھنگ مباح ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ گھاس ہے لیکن اس سے نشہ میں ہونا حرام ہے۔ (النہر عن العنایہ )

اور اب میں مترجم یہ کہتا ہوں کہ یہ چیزیں مسکر نہیں ہیں۔ کیونکہ مسکر و نشہ کا مادہ گرم تر ہے۔ جب کہ افیون اور چرس سر دو خشک ہیں۔ پھر بھی ان کے حرام ہونے کی وجہ تخدیر یعنی اعضاء کو بے حس کر دینا تغیر اور جو اس میں کمزوری اور فتور پیدا کرنا ہے۔ جس کی دلیل حضرت ام سلمہ کی یہ حدیث ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ہر مفتر اور مفتر سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اسناد حسن کے ساتھ ابو داؤد نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ اور شامی نے شیخ ابن حجر رحمۃ اللہ علیہ وغیرہ سے نقل کیا ہے جس شخص کو افیون کھانے کی عادت ہو گئی ہو تو بھی اس کے لئے یہ حلال نہیں ہے۔ کہ اسی عادت پر قائم رہے۔ البتہ اگر ایک

ساتھ مکمل طور پر چھوڑنے میں ہلاکت یا بیماری کا خطرہ ہو تو اسے آہستہ آہستہ کم کرتا رہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اسے بالکل چھوڑ دے۔ش۔ اگر کسی معجون کے بنانے میں افیون کا حصہ دوسرے حصوں کے مقابلہ میں کم ہو تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ اور اسی ترکیب سے بچوں کو دینے میں بھی کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ واللہ تعالٰی اعلم۔
Definition of the drunkard: The majority of the mashayikh inclined [to the view of the Sahibayn]. And for him (Abu Hanifa): Indeed, in the causes of the hudud, one takes the maximum degree as a measure to avert the hadd. The ultimate state of drunkenness is that joy overcomes the intellect, stripping it of discrimination between one thing and another. Whatever is less than that is not free from the doubt of sobriety. The consideration regarding the intoxicating cup in matters of prohibition is what they both said, by consensus, taking precaution. And al-Shafi'i considers the appearance of its effect in his gait, movements, and limbs. This varies, so there is no meaning to considering it.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage defines the threshold of intoxication (sukr) that triggers the hadd punishment. Abu Hanifa requires total loss of discrimination between things; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) define sakran by incoherent speech. The majority of later mashayikh adopted the Sahibayn's view as the mufta bihi, as it aligns with common understanding ('urf) and avoids the weakness of Abu Hanifa's proof. Imam al-Shafi'i's reliance on visible physical effects (staggering, etc.) is rejected because these vary widely among individuals; a strong person may show no effect, while a weak person may stagger even without drink. The passage also clarifies that for intoxicants other than wine, prohibition is tied to actual intoxication, defined by more than half of one's speech being incoherent. Substances like bhang and opium have weaker effects; they incur ta'zir (discretionary punishment) rather than hadd, and some authorities consider bhang permissible unless it intoxicates. The hadith of Umm Salamah prohibits any substance causing languor or intoxication. Addiction to such substances is not permitted, but gradual withdrawal is allowed with genuine danger.

Key Terms
سكران (sakran): An intoxicated person subject to hadd; defined by loss of discrimination or incoherent speech.
حد (hadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for certain crimes.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt or ambiguity that averts the hadd punishment.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of adultery (zina).
هذيان (hadhyan): Incoherent, nonsensical speech; key indicator of intoxication in the Sahibayn's definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi mashayikh, what is the defining characteristic of a sakran for the purpose of hadd?
A) Inability to distinguish between a man and a woman.
B) Incoherent and confused speech (hadhyan) exceeding half of total speech.
C) Staggering gait and limb movements.
D) Having drunk more than three cups of wine.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi defines sakran for hadd as one whose speech is predominantly incoherent (hadhyan), not by amount drunk or physical signs.
